Women Not Raising Voice in Talbiyah
Ruling with proof for women lowering voice in talbiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman raising her voice in talbiyah, identify the proof (Ibn Umar's narration), and explain the rationale of avoiding fitnah.

Core Idea
Women lower voice in talbiyah to avoid fitnah; talbiyah is wajib for men to raise voice.

In Hajj, talbiyah is a repeated proclamation for those in ihram. While it is a sunnah for men to raise their voices loudly, the rule for women is different. This lesson explains the Hanafi position based on a clear proof from the practice of the Companions and the underlying wisdom of modesty and avoiding fitnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? (A woman raising her voice in talbiyah). What is the Hanafi ruling? (It is not allowed; she should lower her voice).
The ruling is specific to women; men are required to raise their voices.
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the evidence cited: the narration from Ibn Umar (رضي الله عنهما) that explicitly states a woman should not raise her voice in talbiyah.
This is a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for a non-obligatory ruling.
3
Understand the Illa (Reason)
Why does the Hanafi school hold this view? The text says 'because it may cause fitnah' – meaning attracting attention of non-mahram men.
This is a legal reasoning based on the principle of sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking the means to evil).
4
Classify the Hukm
In the Hanafi school, lowering the voice for women is sunnah ghayr muakkadah (recommended, not obligatory). Raising it is makruh tanzihi (reprehensible to avoid).
This is not haram, but it is better to avoid.
5
Note the Intra-Madhhab and Cross-Madhhab Status
The three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree. Other schools (Shafi'i, etc.) allow women to raise their voice moderately if no fitnah, but the Hanafi position is more cautious.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is that a Hanafi woman should keep her voice low even in an all-female group, while a Shafi'i woman may raise it if safe.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا ترفع صوتها بالتلبية(١٣٩٧ ) ترجمه : (۱۳۹۶) اور تلبیہ میں اپنی آواز کو بلند نہ کرے۔ وجه : (۱) عن ابن عمر قال لا تصعد المرأة فوق الصفا والمروة ولا ترفع صوتها بالتلبية (دارقطني ، كتاب الحج، ج ثانی ص ۲۵۹، نمبر ۴۱ ۲۷ سفن للبیھقی ، باب المرأة لاترفع صوتها بالتلبية، ج خامس ،ص۷۲، نمبر ۹۰۳۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت تلبیہ میں آواز بلند نہیں کرے گی۔ کیونکہ اس سے فتنہ پیدا ہوسکتا ہے۔
And she should not raise her voice in talbiyah (1397). Translation: (1396) And she should not raise her voice in talbiyah. Evidence: (1) From Ibn Umar who said: 'A woman should not ascend above Safa and Marwa, and she should not raise her voice in talbiyah' (Darqutni, Kitab al-Hajj, vol. 2, p. 259, no. 2741? ; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Mar'ah la taf'a' sawtaha bi al-talbiyah, vol. 5, p. 72, no. 9039). From this effect it is known that a woman does not raise her voice in talbiyah because it may cause fitnah.

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that a woman should not raise her voice in talbiyah. The evidence is a narration from Ibn Umar that explicitly states two things: a woman should not ascend the hills of Safa and Marwa (possibly meaning she should not go to the top? But the main point is not raising voice). The reason given is that raising her voice may attract attention or cause fitnah. In the Hanafi school, it is recommended (mustahabb) for women to lower their voice in talbiyah and other dhikr to avoid being heard by men.

Key Terms
تلبیة (talbiyah): The repeated recitation of 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' during ihram in Hajj or Umrah.

A) Because it is not sunnah for anyone.
B) Because it may cause fitnah.
C) Because she cannot recite properly.
D) Because it is mandatory for men only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a woman should lower her voice in talbiyah to avoid fitnah, based on a narration from Ibn Umar.

Women Not Performing Ramal or Running in Sa'y: Ruling and Evidence
Ruling that a woman should not walk briskly or run between the two green markers in sa'y

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for women regarding ramal in tawaf and running during sa'y, and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Women are exempt from ramal and running; they should walk calmly to preserve modesty.

This lesson addresses the specific practices of ramal (brisk walking) in tawaf and running between the two green markers during sa'y. While these acts are sunnah for men, the Hanafi school teaches that women should not perform them. The evidence is a clear hadith from Ibn Umar. We will explore the ruling, its proof, and the wisdom behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Acts in Question
Define ramal (walking with a swagger) in tawaf and running between the two green markers in sa'y.
Ramal is specific to the first three circuits of tawaf for men; running is between the two green markers in sa'y.
2
State the Ruling for Men
For men, ramal and running are sunnah muakkadah.
3
State the Ruling for Women
Women should not do ramal or run; they should walk calmly at their normal pace.
The text says 'this is against her femininity'.
4
Examine the Hadith Evidence
The hadith from Ibn Umar explicitly states: 'There is no ramal for women around the House nor between Safa and Marwah.'
The hadith is a hadith ahad with zanni thubut and dalalah, but it is relied upon.
5
Understand the Wisdom
The exemption preserves modesty and avoids attracting attention, aligning with the principles of female attire and behavior in worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا الصفا ترمل ولا تهرول فى السعى بين الميلين الاخضرين بل تمشى على هيئتها في جميع السعى بينا ترجمه : (۱۳۹۷) اور رمل نہ کرے۔ اور سعی کی حالت میں میلین اخضرین کے درمیان نہ دوڑے بلکہ صفا و مروہ کے درمیان پوری سعی میں اطمینان سے چلے۔ تشریح : مر طواف کے پہلے تین شوط میں اکڑ کر چلے گا، عورت اطمینان سے چلے گی ، اکڑ کر نہیں چلے گی، اسی طرح میلین اخضرین کے درمیان نہیں دوڑے گی بلکہ اطمینان سے چلے گی۔ یہ اس کی نسوانیت کے خلاف ہے۔ وجه (۱) عن ابن عمر قال ليس على النساء رمل بالبيت ولا بين الصفا والمروة . (دار قطني ، كتاب الحج ، ج ثانی ، ص ۲۵۸، نمبر ۲۷۴۰ / باب نمبر ۲۹۴ رسنن سبیھقی ، باب المرأة تطوف وتسعی لیلا اذا كانت مشهورة بالجمال ولا ريل عليها، ج خامس ص سے لے نمبر ۹۰۵۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت نہ رمل کرے گی اور نہ صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان دوڑے گی ۔ لغت ترمل : اکڑ کر چلنا۔ تھرول : دوڑنا۔ حدیبیہ : اطمینان سے چلنا۔
And at Safa: she should not do ramal and should not hurry in walking between the two green markers, but she should walk at her normal pace throughout the entire sa'y. Translation: (1397) And she should not do ramal. And during sa'y between the two green markers, she should not run, but between Safa and Marwah she should walk with tranquility. Explanation: A man will walk with a swagger in the first three circuits of tawaf; a woman will walk with tranquility, not with a swagger. Similarly, she will not run between the two green markers but will walk with tranquility. This is against her femininity. Evidence: (1) From Ibn Umar who said: 'There is no ramal for women around the House nor between Safa and Marwah' (Darqutni, Kitab al-Hajj, vol. 2, p. 258, no. 2740; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Mar'ah tatuf wa tas'a layla idha kanat mashhuratan bi al-jamal wa la rayl 'alayha, vol. 5, no. 9055). From this effect it is known that a woman will not do ramal and will not run between Safa and Marwah. Vocabulary: tarammul: walking with a swagger. tahrawul: running. hadhibah: walking with tranquility.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that a woman should not do ramal (walking with a swagger) in tawaf nor run between the two green markers in sa'y. The evidence is a hadith from Ibn Umar explicitly stating no ramal for women around the Kaaba nor between Safa and Marwah. The explanation adds that men do ramal in the first three circuits of tawaf, but women should walk calmly to maintain modesty. The text also defines terms: 'ramal' is walking with a swagger, 'tahrawul' is running, and 'hadhibah' is walking with tranquility.

Key Terms
رمل (ramal): Walking with a swagger or brisk pace, specifically in the first three circuits of tawaf for men.
میلین اخضرین (milayn akhdarayn): Two green markers between Safa and Marwah where men run during sa'y.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Women are exempt from ramal in tawaf and running during sa'y; they should walk calmly to maintain modesty, as per the direct hadith from Ibn Umar.

Woman's Hair Ritual in Hajj: Halq vs Taqsir
Ruling on hair removal for women in Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hair removal for women in Hajj and explain the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
A woman must only trim her hair (taqsir); shaving (halq) is prohibited for her in Hajj.

When exiting ihram, men may shave their heads or trim their hair, but women are not permitted to shave. This lesson explains the ruling based on a clear prophetic hadith and the reasoning behind it. Understanding this distinction ensures correct practice and avoids common errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage rules upon: a woman's hair removal when leaving ihram. The ruling is that she must not shave (halq) but must trim (taqsir).
Halq means complete shaving; taqsir means cutting a small length (e.g., fingertip) from each lock.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'There is no shaving for women; only trimming is for women.' This is the primary evidence.
The hadith is considered ahad but sufficient for this ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly negates shaving (halq) for women and positively commands trimming (taqsir). The imperative 'innama' emphasizes restriction.
The linguistic form indicates exclusivity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools allow women to shave if they prefer. The Hanafi school holds taqsir as the only valid method.
The difference is based on interpretation of the hadith's strength.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position relies on the literal meaning of the hadith and the principle of avoiding harm (loss of adornment). This is the mufta bihi ruling.
No intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۹۸) اور حلق نہ کرے بلکہ قصر کرے۔ وجه (۱) بال منڈوانے سے عورت گنجی ہو جائے گی جو اس کی زینت کے خلاف ہے اس لئے صرف قصر کرے گی (۲) صاحب ھدایہ کی حدیث یہ ہے۔ ان ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله ليس على النساء حلق انما على النساء التقصير . (ابو داؤ د باب الحلق والتقصیر ص ۲۷۹ نمبر ۱۹۸۴ ترمذی شریف باب ما جاء فی کراہیتہ الحلق للنساء ص۱۸۲ نمبر ۹۱۴ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت حلق نہ کرائے وہ صرف تقصیر کرائے اور پوروے بھر بال کٹوا کر حلال ہو جائے۔ لغت حلق : سرکو منڈوانا۔ قصر : کچھ بال رکھنا کچھ کو کٹوانا۔
Translation: (1398) And she should not shave but rather trim. Evidence: (1) By shaving, a woman becomes bald, which is against her adornment, so she will only trim. (2) The hadith of the author of Hidayah: That Ibn Abbas said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no shaving for women; only trimming is for women.' (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Halq wa al-Taqsir, p. 279, no. 1984; Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi karahiyat al-halq li al-nisa', p. 182, no. 914). From this hadith it is known that a woman should not get her head shaved; she should only get her hair trimmed and become halal by cutting the length of a fingertip. Vocabulary: halq: shaving the head. qasr: leaving some hair and cutting some.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that a woman should not shave her head (halq) but instead should trim her hair (taqsir). Two reasons are given: first, shaving makes a woman bald, which is against her beauty and adornment; second, the clear hadith of the Prophet (s) stating 'there is no shaving for women; only trimming is for women.' The hadith is from Ibn Abbas, recorded by Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi. The trimming involves cutting a small portion (equivalent to a fingertip length) from each lock of hair, and then she is free from ihram.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving the head completely; not prescribed for women in Hajj.
قصر (taqsir): Trimming the hair by cutting some length (about a fingertip) from each lock.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a woman do to exit ihram regarding her hair according to the Hanafi school?
A) She must shave her head completely.
B) She must trim a portion of her hair.
C) She may either shave or trim.
D) She does not need to do anything.

Key Takeaway
A woman in Hajj must only trim her hair (taqsir) and never shave (halq), based on the explicit prophetic hadith and the principle of preserving adornment.

Women Wearing Sewn Clothes in Ihram
Ruling that a woman may wear sewn clothes in ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women wearing sewn clothes in ihram and cite the hadith evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
Women may wear sewn clothes in ihram to cover their awrah.

A common misconception is that the prohibition of sewn clothes applies to both men and women in ihram. However, the Hanafi school rules that women are explicitly allowed to wear sewn garments. This lesson examines the evidence from the Sunnah that establishes this dispensation and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act of women wearing sewn clothes (makhit) during ihram. Determine the hukm level from the text.
The text states it is permissible (mubah) – not prohibited.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited by the author. It is a hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar reported in Abu Dawud.
The hadith is ahad, but it is relied upon in the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does this hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly permitted women to wear trousers (sarawil) and a shirt (qamis), which are sewn garments. This implies that sewn clothes are allowed for women.
The prohibition for men is not extended to women because of this explicit permission.
4
Analyse the Hanafi rationale
Why does the Hanafi school allow this? The text explains that a woman's entire body is 'awrah, and forcing her to wear unsewn wraps would risk exposure. The ruling is based on necessity for modesty.
This rationale is not just a deduction but is supported by the hadith.
5
Note the cross-madhhab status
Is this ruling agreed upon? It is mukhtalaf fih – some other schools may hold that women also avoid sewn clothes, but the Hanafi position is clear and mufta bihi.
The strength of the Hanafi position lies in the explicit hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۹۹) اور سلا ہوا کپڑا پہنے۔ تشریح : عورت کا پورا بدن ستر عورت ہے، اب اگر احرام کی حالت میں سلا ہوا کپڑا نہ پہنے تواس کے ستر کھلنے کا خطرہ ہے اس لئے وہ سلا ہوا کپڑا پہن سکتی ہے۔ وجه (۱) اس حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے . عن عبد الله بن عمر أنه سمع رسول الله له نهى النساء في احرامهن عن القفازين و النقاب و ما مس الورس والزعفران من الثياب و لتلبس بعد ذالك ما أحبت من الوان الثياب معصفرا أو خزا أو حليا أو سراويل أو قميصا أو خفا - (ابوداود شریف، باب ما یلبس المحر م ص ۲۶۸، نمبر ۱۸۲۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عورت قمیص پہن سکتی ہے جو سلی ہوئی ہوتی ہے اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت سلا ہوا کپڑا پہن سکتی ہے
Translation: (1399) And she should wear sewn clothes. Explanation: The entire body of a woman is 'awrah; if she does not wear sewn clothes in the state of ihram, there is risk of her 'awrah being exposed. Therefore, she can wear sewn clothes. Evidence: (1) In this hadith there is proof: From Abdullah ibn Umar that he heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade women in ihram from wearing gloves, niqab, and clothes dyed with wars or saffron, and (said) after that she may wear whatever she likes of colored clothes, like those dyed with safflower, or silk, or jewelry, or trousers, or a shirt, or khuffs. (Abu Dawud, Bab ma yalbas al-muhrim, p. 268, no. 1827). In this hadith it is that a woman may wear a shirt which is sewn, so it is known that a woman may wear sewn clothes.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that women may wear sewn clothes (like shirts, trousers) while in ihram. The reasoning is that a woman's entire body is 'awrah, and if she wore the same unsewn garments as men (two sheets), her body could be exposed. The evidence is a hadith from Ibn Umar where the Prophet (s) forbade women from wearing gloves, niqab, and certain dyed clothes, but explicitly allowed them to wear trousers, shirts, and other sewn garments. This indicates that the prohibition of sewn clothes applies only to men, not women.

Key Terms
مخيط (makhit): Sewn or stitched clothing; men are prohibited from wearing them in ihram, but women are allowed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on women wearing sewn clothes in ihram?
A) Prohibited like men.
B) Permissible.
C) Recommended but not required.
D) Makruh.

Key Takeaway
Women may wear sewn clothes in ihram because the hadith explicitly permits it, and covering the 'awrah takes priority.

Women Not Crowding Men at the Black Stone
Ruling that a woman should not crowd with men to kiss the Black Stone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women kissing the Black Stone in a crowd and apply the evidence from the Companion's saying.

Core Idea
A woman must not crowd men to kiss the Black Stone if it leads to prohibited physical contact.

Performing istilam (touching/kissing) of the Black Stone is a cherished sunnah during tawaf. However, when the area is crowded, the obligation to avoid touching non-mahram men takes precedence. This lesson examines the Hanafi position, supported by the action of Umm al-Mu'minin Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her), who forbade her slave-girl from pushing through men to reach the Stone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a woman performing istilam (kissing/touching the Black Stone) when there is crowding (izdiham) with men. The ruling is haram if it leads to touching non-mahram men.
The ruling applies specifically when physical contact with non-mahram men is inevitable.
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
The author cites the statement of Aisha (radiallahu anha) to her slave-girl: 'May Allah not reward you! You push against men...' This is a Companion's saying (qawl sahabi) used as proof.
The evidence is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi. Though zanni in transmission, it carries weight as the practice of Aisha.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Aisha's prohibition explicitly links kissing the Stone in a crowd to pushing against men, which is forbidden. This indicates that the sunnah of istilam is overridden by the prohibition of touching non-mahram.
The legal reasoning: when two rulings conflict (sunnah vs haram), the prohibition prevails.
4
Note the exception
If the place is empty (no crowding), women may kiss the Stone without restriction. The harm (touching men) is absent, so the original sunnah is permissible.
The condition for permissibility is the absence of izdiham leading to non-mahram contact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۴۰۰) اور حجر اسود کا بوسہ دینے کے لئے مردوں کے ساتھ ازدحام نہ کرے۔ تشریح : اگر حجر اسود کے پاس بھیڑ ہو تو عورت کو چاہئے کہ حجر اسود کا بوسہ نہ لے، کیونکہ اس صورت میں مرد سے مماس ہوگا اوراجنبی مردوں کو چھونا لازم آئے گا جوممنوع ہے، ہاں جگہ خالی ہو تو عورتیں حجر اسود کو چومے، اس کی اجازت ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس قول صحابیہ میں اس کا ثبوت ہے . انها كانت عند عائشة زوج النبي الله ام المؤمنين فدخلت عليها مولاة لها فقالت لها يا ام المؤمنين طفت بالبيت سبعا و استلمت الركن مرتين أو ثلاثا فقالت لها عائشة : لا أجرك الله لا أجرك الله تدافعين الرجال الاكبرت و مررت ۔ ( سنن بیہقی ، باب الاستلام في الزحام، ج خامس ص ۱۳۱، نمبر ۹۲۶۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ حضرت عائشہ نے اپنی باندی کو بھیڑ میں حجر اسود کو چومنے سے منع فرمایا۔
Translation: (1400) And she should not crowd with men to kiss the Black Stone. Explanation: If there is crowding at the Black Stone, a woman should not kiss it, because in that situation she will touch men and it becomes necessary to touch non-mahram men, which is prohibited. Yes, if the place is empty, women may kiss the Black Stone; that is allowed. Evidence: (1) In this saying of a female companion there is proof: That a client of Aisha, Umm al-Mu'minin, said: 'O Umm al-Mu'minin, I performed tawaf seven times and I touched the corner two or three times.' Aisha said to her: 'May Allah not reward you! May Allah not reward you! You push against men until you become great? and then you passed?' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Istilam fi al-Ziham, vol. 5, p. 131, no. 9268). In this effect, Aisha forbade her slave-girl from kissing the Black Stone in crowding.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage rules that a woman should not crowd with men to kiss the Black Stone (Hajr al-Aswad) when there is a crowd. The reasoning is that such crowding would lead to physical contact with non-mahram men, which is prohibited. The evidence is the story of Aisha rebuking her slave-girl for touching the Black Stone in a crowd, saying 'May Allah not reward you! You push against men...' This indicates that it is forbidden for women to push through men to perform the sunnah of istilam if it involves prohibited touching. If the area is clear, women may kiss the Stone.

Key Terms
استلام (istilam): The act of touching or kissing the Black Stone during tawaf.
ازدحام (izdiham): Crowding or pushing; prohibited if it leads to touching non-mahram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling for a woman who wants to kiss the Black Stone when there is a crowd of men?
A) She must push through gently, because istilam is sunnah.
B) She should not kiss it and avoid crowding, because it leads to touching non-mahram men.
C) She can kiss it from a distance using a hand gesture.
D) She should wait until the crowd clears, even if it takes a long time.

Key Takeaway
A woman must not crowd men to kiss the Black Stone; avoiding prohibited contact takes priority over performing the sunnah of istilam.

Women's Hajj Rulings: Shaving, Clothing, Crowding
Explains three specific rulings with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three specific Hanafi rulings for women in ihram (taqsir, stitched clothing, avoidance of crowding), cite the primary evidence for each, and explain the rationale behind the permissibility of stitched clothes and the prohibition of crowding.

Core Idea
Women in ihram must shorten hair (not shave), may wear stitched clothes, and must avoid crowding with men.

This lesson addresses three common questions about women's ihram: shaving vs. shortening hair, wearing stitched clothing, and crowding at the Black Stone. Each ruling is supported by clear hadith evidence and Hanafi reasoning that prioritizes women's modesty and ease. Understanding these distinctions is essential for anyone guiding female pilgrims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling for hair removal
The passage states that women must not shave (halq) but only shorten (taqsir). Identify the hukm level: taqsir is wajib, halq is not required.
Hanafi school considers taqsir sufficient; some schools require halq.
2
Analyze the first evidence: hadith on halq vs taqsir
The hadith from Ibn Abbas: 'There is no shaving for women; only shortening is upon women.' Note the negation of halq and affirmation of taqsir.
This is a clear nas that establishes the ruling.
3
Identify the ruling on stitched clothing
The passage permits wearing any stitched garment (makhit) during ihram for women. The hukm is mubah (permissible) with necessity.
Unlike men, women are allowed stitched clothes because their entire body is awrah.
4
Analyze the second evidence: hadith on permissible garments
The hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar lists qamis (shirt), which is stitched. This implies permission for all stitched garments.
The hadith also lists other items like trousers and socks, confirming generality.
5
Identify the prohibition of crowding with men
Women must not push with men to kiss the Black Stone. The hukm is haram if it leads to unlawful touching.
If the area is empty, kissing is allowed.
6
Analyze the third evidence: Aisha's statement
Aisha rebukes her slave-girl for crowding: 'May Allah not reward you; you push against men.' This shows disapproval and establishes the prohibition.
Though a qawl sahabi, it is strong evidence in Hanafi fiqh.

Explanation: A woman's entire body is awrah; if she does not wear stitched clothing in ihram, there is risk of exposure, so she can wear stitched clothing. Explanation: If there is a crowd at the Black Stone, a woman should not kiss it because in that case she would touch men, which is forbidden. Yes, if the place is empty, women may kiss the Black Stone; it is permissible. Commentary
This is a passage from a Hanafi commentary detailing three specific rulings for women during Hajj. The author presents each ruling with its evidence. First ruling: women must not shave their heads (halq) but only shorten their hair (taqsir). The author provides a rational reason (baldness harms beauty) and a hadith from Ibn Abbas explicitly stating that women are not to shave. Second ruling: women may wear stitched clothing (makhit) in ihram. The author explains that since a woman's entire body is awrah, stitched clothing is necessary to cover properly. Evidence is a hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar listing permissible garments including a shirt (qamis), which is stitched. Third ruling: women should not crowd with men to kiss the Black Stone. The author gives a practical reason (avoiding unlawful touch) and an effect from Aisha where she rebukes her slave-girl for doing so. The passage emphasizes protection of women's modesty and avoidance of fitna.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving the entire head completely
قصر (taqsir): Cutting a portion of the hair, about a finger's length
مخيط (makhit): Stitched clothing, such as a shirt or trousers
ازدحام (izdiham): Crowding, pushing together with others

Hajj Qiran: Definition and Superiority
Defines Qiran and ranks its virtue

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Hajj Qiran and state its superiority over Tamattu' and Ifrad according to the Hanafi school, citing the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
Qiran combines Hajj and Umrah in one ihram – the most virtuous form of Hajj per the Hanafi school.

In this passage, the author transitions from Hajj Ifrad to define and extol Hajj Qiran, the form that unites both Hajj and Umrah in a single consecration. You will learn its definition, its rank among the three types, and the Quranic evidence that supports it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of Hajj
Read the passage and distinguish between Ifrad (Hajj only), Tamattu' (Umrah then Hajj in separate ihrams), and Qiran (Hajj and Umrah together in one ihram). Note the linguistic meanings: qiran = joining, tamattu' = benefiting.
2
State the Hanafi ranking of virtue
The passage explicitly states 'Qiran is superior to Tamattu'' and that Ifrad is the least. Rank them: Qiran > Tamattu' > Ifrad.
This ranking is a distinctive Hanafi position.
3
Explain the basis of superiority
Qiran combines both acts of worship in one ihram, making it more comprehensive and rewarding. Tamattu' also combines them in one journey but not in one ihram.
4
Locate and understand the Quranic proof
The author cites Quran 2:196: 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah.' The Hanafi school interprets the conjunction 'and' as indicating that both can be performed together, thus supporting Qiran.
This verse is the primary textual evidence.
5
Note the inter-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school considers Ifrad superior. Contrast with the Hanafi view and appreciate that this is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The difference arises from how each school interprets the same verse.

Kissing the Black Stone, and this is the completion of Hajj Ifrad. (1401) And it is lower in virtue than Tamattu', and Qiran is superior to Tamattu'. Chapter: (1402) Qiran is to combine the ihram of Hajj and Umrah by saying after praying two rak'ahs of ihram: 'O Allah, I intend...' Translation: (1401) This is the complete description of Hajj Ifrad, which is lesser in virtue than Hajj Tamattu', and Qiran is superior to Tamattu'. Explanation: These were the issues of Hajj Ifrad, but many issues of Hajj Tamattu' and Qiran are the same. Hajj Qiran is the most virtuous because in it both Hajj and Umrah are together. Then Hajj Tamattu' comes because in it Hajj and Umrah are performed in one journey although not together. Then Hajj Ifrad comes because in it only Hajj is performed. Proofs will come later. Chapter: On the explanation of Qiran. Essential note: To combine both Hajj and Umrah in one journey and tie the ihram of Umrah with Hajj is called Qiran. Qiran, with kasra on qaf, means to join. Since Hajj and Umrah are joined together, it is called Qiran. The proof of Hajj Qiran is in this verse: 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah.' (Quran 2:196) In this verse it is ordered to complete Hajj and Umrah, thus Hajj Qiran is established. Translation: (1402) Qiran is to tie the ihram of Hajj and Umrah together. Then after the two rak'ahs of ihram, he says: 'O Allah, I intend Hajj and Umrah, make it easy for me and accept it,' then he recites talbiyah. Explanation: [1] If one ties ihram only for Hajj, it is called Hajj Ifrad. [2] If one first ties ihram for Umrah, completes it and opens the ihram, stays within the miqat, then ties ihram for Hajj in the months of Hajj and completes Hajj, it is called Hajj Tamattu'. Tamattu' means to benefit. Since he benefited from opening ihram after Umrah, this Hajj is called Tamattu'. (3) And if one ties ihram for Hajj and Umrah together, it is called Hajj Qiran. Qiran means joining, because Hajj and Umrah are joined together. Evidence (1) The proof of Qiran is in this verse: 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah.' (2:196) This verse commands to combine Hajj and Umrah, thus Qiran is established. (2) This hadith instructs to combine Hajj and Umrah after praying two rak'ahs: Umar heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the valley of Aqiq say, 'Last night a messenger came to me from my Lord and said...'

Commentary
This passage transitions from Hajj Ifrad to the definition and merit of Hajj Qiran. The author states that the previous rulings were for Ifrad (performing only Hajj). Now he explains that Qiran is superior to Tamattu', and Tamattu' is superior to Ifrad. The reason given is that Qiran combines Hajj and Umrah in one ihram, thus more comprehensive. The author then defines the three types: Ifrad (Hajj alone), Tamattu' (Umrah first, then Hajj in the same journey with separate ihrams), and Qiran (both together in one ihram). The evidence for Qiran is Quran 2:196, which commands completing both Hajj and Umrah, interpreted as performing them together. The author also begins to cite a hadith about praying two rak'ahs before combining. This is standard Hanafi position that Qiran is the best form.

Key Terms
قران (qiran): Combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram, intending both together.
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing Umrah first during hajj months, then opening ihram and later performing Hajj with a new ihram.
افراد (ifrad): Performing only Hajj without Umrah in the same journey.
احرام (ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj/Umrah, marked by specific garments and prohibitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Hajj Ifrad
B) Hajj Tamattu'
C) Hajj Qiran
D) All are equal

Key Takeaway
Hajj Qiran, combining both Hajj and Umrah in one ihram, is the most virtuous form of Hajj in the Hanafi school, supported by Quran 2:196.

Types of Hajj and the Superiority of Qiran
Defines Hajj al-Qiran and establishes its superiority over Ifrad and Tamattu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish Hajj al-Ifrad, al-Tamattu', and al-Qiran, state the Hanafi hierarchy of virtue, and explain the key textual evidence for the superiority of Qiran.

Core Idea
Hajj al-Qiran is the most virtuous type of Hajj in the Hanafi school, combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram.

This lesson clarifies the three types of Hajj and their ranking according to the Hanafi school. You will learn why Qiran is considered superior over Tamattu' and Ifrad, supported by the Quran and authentic hadith. This is a foundational concept for understanding the preferred practice in Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of Hajj
Read the definitions of Hajj al-Ifrad, al-Tamattu', and al-Qiran. Note the distinguishing features: ihram for Hajj alone, Umrah then Hajj with break, or combined ihram.
2
State the Hanafi hierarchy
The passage explicitly ranks Qiran as most virtuous, then Tamattu', then Ifrad. Understand the reasoning: Qiran combines both acts together, Tamattu' in one journey separately, Ifrad only Hajj.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
The verse 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' (2:196) is interpreted as a command to combine both, supporting Qiran. Note the imperative 'atimmu' and its implication.
Hanafi usul treats al-amr as wujub, but here the virtue is derived from completeness.
4
Examine the hadith proofs
The passage cites multiple hadith: the Prophet's command at al-'Aqeeq, his own talbiyah for both, and instructions to his family. These explicitly show the merit of combining Hajj and Umrah.
The hadith at al-'Aqeeq is particularly strong in Hanafi istidlal.
5
Note the inter-madhhab dispute
The Shafi'i school considers Tamattu' superior. Understand their proof (hadith of ordering companions to change to Tamattu') and the Hanafi response (that was a concession for those without sacrificial animals).
The practical difference is which type to choose for maximum reward.

فصل القرآن
استلام الحجر وهذا تمام الحج المفرد) (۱۴۰۱) وهو دون المتمتع في الفضل والقرآن افضل من التمتع.
فصل :
(۱۴۰۲) القران هو ان يجمع بين احرام الحج والعمرة فيقول بعد صلوة ركعتي الاحرام اللهم انى اريد العمرة والحج فيسّر هما لى وتقبلهما منّى ثم يُلبّى .
ترجمه : (۱۴۰۱) یہ پورابیان حج افراد کا ہے جو فضیلت میں حج تمتع سے کم ہے، اور قران تمتع سے افضل ہے۔ تشریح : یہ مسائل حج افراد کے تھے لیکن بہت سے مسائل حج تمتع اور قرآن میں یہی ہیں ۔ حج قران سب سے افضل ہے کیونکہ اس میں حج اور عمرہ دونوں ایک ساتھ ہوتے ہیں۔ اس کے بعد حج تمتع ہوتا ہے کیونکہ اس میں حج اور عمرہ ایک سفر میں ادا ہوتے ہیں اگر چہ ایک ساتھ نہیں ہوتے ۔ اس کے بعد حج افراد ہے، کیونکہ اس میں صرف حج ادا ہوتا ہے۔ دلائل بعد میں آئیں گے۔
فصل : قرآن کے بیان میں
ضروری نوٹ : حج اور عمرہ دونوں کو ایک ہی سفر میں جمع کرے اور حج کے ساتھ عمرے کا احرام باندھ لے اس کو قران کہتے ہیں۔ قران,ق، کے کسرے کے ساتھ معنی ہے ملانا، چونکہ حج اور عمرہ کو ایک ساتھ ملایا اس لئے اس کو قران کہتے ہیں۔ اس آیت میں حج قران کا ثبوت ہے۔ و اتموا الحج و العمرة لله - ( آیت ۱۹۶، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ حج اور عمرے کو پورا کرو اس سے حج قران ، ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۴۰۲) قرآن یہ ہے کہ حج اور عمرہ کا احرام ایک ساتھ باندھے۔ پس احرام کی دورکعت کے بعد یہ کہے کہ: اے اللہ میں حج اور عمرہ کا ارادہ کرتا ہوں میرے لئے آسان کیجئے اور قبول فرمائیے ، پھر تلبیہ پڑھے۔
تشریح : [1] صرف حج کا احرام باندھے تو اس کو حج افراد کہتے ہیں ۔ [۲] پہلے عمرے کا احرام باندھے اس کو پورا کر کے احرام کھول دے اور میقات کے حدود میں ٹھہرا رہے پھر اشہر حج میں حج کا احرام باندھے اور حج پورا کرے تو اس کو حج تمتع کہتے ہیں تمتع کے معنی ہیں فائدہ اٹھانا، چونکہ اس نے عمرہ کے بعد احرام کھولنے کا فائدہ اٹھایا اس لئے اس حج کو حج تمتع کہتے ہیں۔ (۳) اور حج اور عمرے کا احرام ایک ساتھ باندھے تو اس کو حج قران کہتے ہیں ، قران کا معنی ہے ملانا، چونکہ حج اور عمرے کو ملا یا اس لئے اس کو قران کہا جاتا ہے وجه (۱) اس آیت میں قرآن کا ثبوت ہے ۔ و اتموا الحج و العمرة لله - ( آیت ۱۹۶، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ حج اور عمرے کو جمع کرو اس سے حج قران ، ثابت ہوتا ہے (۲) اس حدیث میں دو رکعت پڑھنے کے بعد حج اور عمرہ کو جمع کرنے کے لئے کہا۔ سمع عمر يقول سمعت النبي له بوادي العقيق يقول أتاني الليلة آت من ربي فقال اريد العمرة والحج فيسّر هما لى وتقبلهما منّى ثم يُلبّى . (۱۴۰۳ فاذا دخل مكة بدأ بطواف العمرة صل في هذا الوادى المبارك وقل عمرة في حجة . ( بخاری شریف، باب قول النبی العقیق وادمبارک ،ص ۲۰۷، نمبر ۱۵۳۴ را ابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی القرآن، ص ۲۵۷، نمبر ۱۸۰۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آپ کو باضابطہ عمرہ کو حج کے ساتھ ملانے کا حکم دیا اس لئے قرآن افضل ہوگا (۳) عن انس بن مالک انهم سمعوه يقول سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يهل بالحج والعمرة جميعا يقول لبيك عمرة و حجا لبیک عمرة و حجا . (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب الاقران ، ص ۲۵۷ نمبر ۷۹۵ ارترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الجمع بین الحج والعمرة ص ۱۶۹ نمبر ۲۱ ۸ر مسلم شریف، باب فی الافراد والقران ص ۵۲۴ ، نمبر ۲۹۹۵/۱۲۳۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے حج اور عمرہ دونوں کا احرام باندھا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ قران افضل ہے (۵) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ فدخلت على ام سلمة . ... سمعت رسول الله الله الله يقول اهلوا يا آل محمد بعمرة في حج (سن للبیھقی ، باب العمرة قبل الج والحج قبل العمرة ج رابع ص ۵۷۹، نمبر ۸۷۸۶ ) اس حدیث میں بھی قران کی اہمیت بیان کی گئی ہے۔ اس لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک قرآن افضل ہے۔
ترجمه : (۱۳۰۳) جب مکہ میں داخل ہو تو طواف عمرہ کے سات چکر سے ابتدا کرے،صرف پہلے تین چکر میں رمل کرے۔ پھر طواف کی دو رکعت پڑھے۔
تشریح : قرآن میں چونکہ پہلے عمرہ ہے اس لئے پہلے عمرہ کے اعمال کرے۔ عمرہ کے اعمال صرف تین ہیں [1] عمرے کا احرام باندھنا [۲] سات شوط عمرے کے لئے طواف کرے۔ پہلے تین میں رمل کرے۔ اس کے بعد طواف کے لئے دو رکعت نماز پڑھے [۳] صفا و مروہ کی سات چکروں میں سعی کرے، میلین اخضرین کے درمیان دوڑے، بس یہ عمرے کے اعمال ہو گئے ، اس کے بعد بغیر احرام کھولے مکہ مکرمہ میں ٹھہرار ہے اور بعد میں حج کرے۔

Fruit of Success Volume 2
399
Section: Quran
Receiving the Stone, and this is the completion of Hajj al-Ifrad. (1401) And it is less in virtue than al-Mutamatti', and al-Qiran is more virtuous than al-Tamattu'.
Section:
(1402) Al-Qiran is that one combines the ihram of Hajj and Umrah, and says after praying two rak'ahs of ihram: 'O Allah, I intend Umrah and Hajj, so make them easy for me and accept them from me,' then he recites the talbiyah.
Translation: (1401) This is a complete explanation of Hajj al-Ifrad, which in virtue is less than Hajj al-Tamattu', and al-Qiran is more virtuous than al-Tamattu'. Explanation: These were issues of Hajj al-Ifrad, but many issues are the same for Hajj al-Tamattu' and Hajj al-Qiran. Hajj al-Qiran is the most virtuous because in it both Hajj and Umrah are performed together. After that comes Hajj al-Tamattu' because in it Hajj and Umrah are performed in one journey, even if not together. After that comes Hajj al-Ifrad, because in it only Hajj is performed. The proofs will come later.
Section: On the explanation of Quran
Essential note: He combines both Hajj and Umrah in one journey and ties the ihram of Umrah with Hajj; this is called Qiran. The word Qiran, with a kasra on the qaf, means to join. Since Hajj and Umrah are joined together, it is called Qiran. The proof of Hajj al-Qiran is in this verse: 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196). This verse indicates to complete Hajj and Umrah, thus Hajj al-Qiran is proven. Translation: (1402) Qiran is that one ties the ihram of Hajj and Umrah together. So after two rak'ahs of ihram, he says: 'O Allah, I intend Hajj and Umrah, make it easy for me and accept it,' then he recites the talbiyah.
Explanation: [1] If one ties only the ihram of Hajj, it is called Hajj al-Ifrad. [2] If one first ties the ihram of Umrah, completes it, removes ihram, stays within the miqat, then ties the ihram of Hajj in the months of Hajj and completes Hajj, this is called Hajj al-Tamattu'. The meaning of tamattu' is to benefit. Since he benefited from removing ihram after Umrah, this Hajj is called Hajj al-Tamattu'. (3) And if one ties the ihram of Hajj and Umrah together, it is called Hajj al-Qiran. The meaning of qiran is to join. Since he joined Hajj and Umrah, it is called Qiran. Reasoning (1) The proof of Qiran is in this verse: 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196). This verse indicates to combine Hajj and Umrah, thus Hajj al-Qiran is proven. (2) In this hadith, after praying two rak'ahs, he was told to combine Hajj and Umrah. 'Umar said: I heard the Prophet at the valley of al-'Aqeeq say: 'Last night a messenger came to me from my Lord and said: Pray in this blessed valley and say: 'Umrah within Hajj.'' (Bukhari, chapter on the Prophet's saying 'al-'Aqeeq, a blessed valley', p. 207, no. 1534; and Abu Dawud, chapter on al-Qiran, p. 257, no. 1800). From this hadith it is learned that he was explicitly commanded to combine Umrah with Hajj, therefore Qiran is more virtuous. (3) From Anas ibn Malik that they heard him say: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) reciting talbiyah for Hajj and Umrah together, saying: 'Labbaik 'umratan wa hajjan, labbaik 'umratan wa hajjan.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on al-Iqran, p. 257, no. 795; Tirmidhi, chapter on combining Hajj and Umrah, p. 169, no. 218?; Muslim, chapter on Ifrad and Qiran, p. 524, no. 2995/1232). This hadith states that the Prophet tied ihram for both Hajj and Umrah, from which it is understood that Qiran is superior. (5) In this hadith: 'I entered upon Umm Salamah... I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saying: 'O family of Muhammad, enter into ihram for 'Umrah within Hajj.' (Bayhaqi, chapter on 'Umrah before Hajj and Hajj before 'Umrah, vol. 4, p. 579, no. 8786). This hadith also explains the importance of Qiran. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, Qiran is superior.
Translation: (1303) When he enters Makkah, he begins with seven circuits of tawaf for Umrah, and he performs raml only in the first three circuits. Then he prays two rak'ahs of tawaf.
Explanation: In Qiran, since Umrah comes first, he performs the acts of Umrah first. The acts of Umrah are only three: [1] Tying ihram for Umrah. [2] Performing seven circuits of tawaf for Umrah. In the first three, he does raml. After that, he prays two rak'ahs for tawaf. [3] Performing sa'i between Safa and Marwah for seven circuits; he runs between the two green markers. These are the acts of Umrah. Then, without removing ihram, he stays in Makkah and later performs Hajj.
Reasoning: (a) From Jabir: He said: The Messenger of Allah came with his companions on the fourth day of Dhul-Hijjah, and when they had performed tawaf of the House and (sa'i) between Safa and Marwah, the Messenger of Allah said: 'Make it Umrah.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on Ifrad, p. 256, no. 1788). From this hadith it is learned that he should perform tawaf for Umrah and sa'i between Safa and Marwah, and the mention of tying ihram has already been made, that Umrah is not valid without ihram. (2) In this hadith: Jabir ibn 'Abdullah narrated that he performed Hajj with the Messenger of Allah on the day he brought the sacrificial animals with him, and they had entered ihram for Hajj alone. He said to them: 'Remove your ihram by performing tawaf of the House and (sa'i) between Safa and Marwah, and trim (your hair), then remain in a state of halal until the day of Tarwiyah, then enter into ihram for Hajj, and make the one you came with as Tamattu'.' (Bukhari, chapter on Tamattu', Qiran, and Ifrad in Hajj, p. 254, no. 1568). This hadith proves that the acts of Umrah are: [1] Performing tawaf of the House, [2] Performing sa'i between Safa and Marwah.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah covers the section on Hajj al-Qiran. It begins by concluding the discussion of Hajj al-Ifrad and then defines the three types of Hajj: Ifrad (Hajj alone), Tamattu' (Umrah first, then Hajj in the same journey with a break), and Qiran (Hajj and Umrah combined in one ihram). The text clearly states the order of virtue according to the Hanafi school: Qiran is the best, followed by Tamattu', then Ifrad. The reasoning is that Qiran combines both acts together, Tamattu' performs them in one journey but separately, and Ifrad only includes Hajj. The passage then provides proofs from the Quran and Sunnah. The Quranic verse 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' is interpreted as commanding the combination of both, which supports Qiran. Several hadiths are cited, including the Prophet's command to combine Umrah with Hajj at al-'Aqeeq, his own talbiyah for both, and an instruction to the family of Muhammad. The text also details the initial acts of Qiran upon entering Makkah: performing tawaf and sa'i for Umrah first, with raml in the first three circuits, and then staying in ihram for Hajj. This commentary follows the author's order, presenting the definitions, the hierarchy of virtue, and the textual evidences.

Key Terms
قران (Qiran): A type of Hajj where one enters ihram for both Hajj and Umrah together, without breaking ihram between them.
حج افراد (Hajj al-Ifrad): Performing Hajj alone without Umrah, entering ihram only for Hajj.
حج تمتع (Hajj al-Tamattu'): Performing Umrah first, then after a break, performing Hajj in the same journey, with a separate ihram for each.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, which form of Hajj is the most virtuous?
A) Hajj al-Ifrad
B) Hajj al-Tamattu'
C) Hajj al-Qiran
D) All are equal in virtue

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, Hajj al-Qiran is the most virtuous form of Hajj because it combines Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram, supported by the Quranic command and the Prophet's practice.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Virtue of Qiran: Hanafi Proofs for Combined Hajj and Umrah
Establishing the superiority of Qiran over Ifrad and Tamattu' through hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the most virtuous form of Hajj and cite the hadith evidence used to support it.

Core Idea
The Prophet performed Hajj and Umrah together — Qiran is the most virtuous form according to the Hanafis.

In this lesson, we examine a passage from Thamaratun Najah that establishes the virtue of Qiran (performing Hajj and Umrah in one ihram) over Ifrad and Tamattu. The author presents multiple hadith to support the Hanafi position. We will analyse the proofs and understand the reasoning behind the school's preference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognise that the passage focuses on the form of Hajj called Qiran (القران). The ruling is that it is afdal (most virtuous) according to the Hanafi school.
Qiran involves one ihram for both Hajj and Umrah without breaking ihram between them.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites three hadith: the first from Bukhari and Abu Dawud (command to combine), the second from Muslim (Prophet's talbiyah for both), and the third from Bayhaqi (instruction to the Prophet's family).
All are ahad hadith, so thubut is zanni, but the multiplicity strengthens the proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Each hadith either explicitly shows the Prophet performing both together or commands doing so. This indicates the legitimacy and virtue of Qiran.
The Hanafi argument: the Prophet's action is the best evidence of virtue.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school prefers Tamattu' (Umrah then Hajj with separate ihrams), citing other hadith. Some Hanbalis prefer Ifrad (Hajj only).
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf among the schools.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text concludes that the Hanafi position (Qiran is afdal) is the mufta bihi, based on the strength and clarity of the hadith.
The later Hanafi masters adopt this as the relied-upon position.

فصل القرآن
اريد العمرة والحج فيسّر هما لى وتقبلهما منّى ثم يُلبّى . (۱۴۰۳ فاذا دخل مكة بدأ بطواف العمرة صل في هذا الوادى المبارك وقل عمرة في حجة . ( بخاری شریف، باب قول النبی العقیق وادمبارک ،ص ۲۰۷، نمبر ۱۵۳۴ را ابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی القرآن، ص ۲۵۷، نمبر ۱۸۰۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آپ کو باضابطہ عمرہ کو حج کے ساتھ ملانے کا حکم دیا اس لئے قرآن افضل ہوگا (۳) عن انس بن مالک انهم سمعوه يقول سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يلبى بالحج والعمرة جميعا يقول لبيك عمرة و حجا لبیک عمرة و حجا . (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب الاقران ، ص ۲۵۷ نمبر ۷۹۵ ارترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الجمع بین الحج والعمرة ص ۱۶۹ نمبر ۲۱ ۸ر مسلم شریف، باب فی الافراد والقران ص ۵۲۴ ، نمبر ۲۹۹۵/۱۲۳۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے حج اور عمرہ دونوں کا احرام باندھا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ قران افضل ہے (۵) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ فدخلت على ام سلمة . ... سمعت رسول الله الله الله يقول اهلوا يا آل محمد بعمرة في حج (سن للبیھقی ، باب العمرة قبل الج والحج قبل العمرة ج رابع ص ۵۷۹، نمبر ۸۷۸۶ ) اس حدیث میں بھی قران کی اہمیت بیان کی گئی ہے۔ اس لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک قرآن افضل ہے۔
Chapter of Qiran. 'I intend Umrah and Hajj, so make them easy for me and accept them from me.' Then he says the talbiyah. (1403) When he enters Makkah, he begins with the tawaf of Umrah... 'Pray in this blessed valley and say: Umrah within Hajj.' (Bukhari, Bab Qawl al-Nabi al-Aqiq wa Adam Mubarak, p. 207, no. 1534; Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Qiran, p. 257, no. 1800) From this hadith it is understood that he was commanded to combine Umrah with Hajj, so Qiran is better. (3) From Anas ibn Malik that they heard him say: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) reciting the talbiyah for Hajj and Umrah together, saying: 'Labbaik Umratan wa Hajjan, Labbaik Umratan wa Hajjan.' (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Iqran, p. 257, no. 795; Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a fi al-Jam' bayn al-Hajj wa al-Umrah, p. 169, no. 821; Muslim, Bab al-Ifrad wa al-Qiran, p. 524, no. 2995/1232) In this hadith, the Prophet (peace be upon him) assumed ihram for both Hajj and Umrah, indicating that Qiran is better. (5) In this hadith: 'I entered upon Umm Salamah... I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saying: O family of Muhammad, proclaim Umrah within Hajj.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Umrah qabl al-Hajj wa al-Hajj qabl al-Umrah, vol. 4, p. 579, no. 8786) This hadith also emphasizes the importance of Qiran. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, Qiran is better.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil naqli). It presents several authentic hadith to establish that performing Hajj and Umrah together in one ihram (Qiran) is the most virtuous form of pilgrimage. The Hanafi school holds this position. The first hadith (from Bukhari) is a command to combine Umrah with Hajj, indicating Qiran's superiority. The second hadith (from Muslim) shows the Prophet himself performing Qiran. The third hadith (from Bayhaqi) emphasizes it for his family. The author concludes that Qiran is afdal (better) according to the Hanafi school. Note that this is a matter of ikhtilaf; other schools may prefer Ifrad or Tamattu'.

Key Terms
قران (qiran): Performing Hajj and Umrah with one ihram, without breaking ihram between them.
افراد (ifrad): Performing only Hajj with ihram, separate from Umrah.
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing Umrah first, then breaking ihram, and later assuming ihram for Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Ifrad
B) Tamattu'
C) Qiran
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
Qiran (combined Hajj and Umrah in one ihram) is the most virtuous form of Hajj according to the Hanafi school, supported by multiple hadith of the Prophet's practice and command.

Actions of Umrah for the Qarin
Detailed description of Umrah actions for a qarin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three actions of Umrah for a qarin and identify the hadith proofs that establish them.

Core Idea
A qarin performs Umrah first with three actions: ihram, tawaf (with ramal), and sa'i.

This passage guides a person performing Hajj Qiran on the sunnah sequence of Umrah actions. It also cites two hadiths from Bukhari and Abu Dawud as proof that tawaf and sa'i are the core actions of Umrah. Understanding these actions ensures that the Qiran is performed correctly according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
List the three actions of Umrah
Read the passage and identify the three actions described: assuming ihram (with niyyah and talbiyah), performing tawaf (seven circuits with ramal in first three), and performing sa'i between Safa and Marwah (seven circuits, running between the green milestones).
The passage explicitly states 'The actions of Umrah are only three'.
2
Understand the order for Qiran
Why is Umrah performed first? In Qiran, Umrah precedes Hajj because the Umrah is the first part of the combined pilgrimage. The pilgrim remains in ihram after Umrah until the Hajj rituals begin.
The commentary says 'because in Qiran, Umrah comes first'.
3
Examine the details of each action
For tawaf: seven circuits, ramal only in first three, followed by two rak'ahs. For sa'i: seven circuits, running between the two green milestones (al-milayn al-akhdharayn). For ihram: already assumed before entering Makkah.
These details are sunnah; omission may affect completeness but not validity of the rukn.
4
Connect actions to their proofs
The passage cites two hadiths: (1) Abu Dawud: The Prophet arrived on 4th Dhul Hijjah and told companions to make their tawaf and sa'i for Umrah. (2) Bukhari: The Prophet instructed companions to exit ihram after tawaf and sa'i. These prove that tawaf and sa'i are essential Umrah actions.
The proofs are from ahad hadith, providing zanni evidence for the sunnah practice.
5
Note the consequence after Umrah
After completing Umrah actions, the qarin remains in ihram and stays in Makkah until the 8th of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm al-Tarwiyah), when he performs the Hajj rituals. He does not shave or cut his hair.
This distinguishes Qiran from Tamattu', where one leaves ihram after Umrah.

Commentary: This is the third action of Umrah: at Safa he says takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, salawat, and supplicates; similarly at Marwah, and runs between the two green milestones. He completes seven circuits of sa'i. The rest of the details and proofs have passed earlier.

This passage is a practical guide with proof (dalil naqli). It details the three actions of Umrah for someone performing Qiran: (1) ihram for Umrah, (2) tawaf of seven circuits (ramal in first three), followed by two rak'ahs, (3) sa'i between Safa and Marwah (running between the green milestones). The commentary reminds that after Umrah, one remains in ihram for Hajj. The proofs (from Abu Dawud and Bukhari) establish these actions as sunnah from the Prophet's practice. This is a key passage for understanding the sequence of Qiran.

Key Terms
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Ka'bah seven times, an essential action of Umrah.
سعی (sa'i): Walking between Safa and Marwah seven times, an essential action of Umrah.
رمل (ramal): Walking briskly with short steps in the first three circuits of tawaf (for men).

The Hanafi Ruling on Umrah: Sunnah Mu'akkadah
Stating that Umrah is sunnah with Quranic and hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Umrah and cite the Quranic and hadith evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
Umrah is sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard; the command in the Quran is interpreted as recommendation.

This passage establishes the Hanafi position on the legal status of Umrah. While some schools consider it obligatory, the Hanafi school deems it a confirmed sunnah based on the evidence from the Quran and Sunnah. Understanding the distinction between fard and sunnah is crucial for proper fiqh application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the passage and note the explicit statement: 'Umrah is sunnah.' Determine what category of legal ruling this falls under.
The ruling is a hukm taklifi: sunnah.
2
Analyze the Quranic Evidence
Examine the verse: 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah.' Identify how the Hanafi school uses this verse to support sunnah rather than obligation.
The command 'atammu' is interpreted in light of other evidences.
3
Examine the Hadith Evidence
Read the hadith from Abu Hurayrah. Understand that it emphasizes the virtue of Umrah without imposing it as a duty.
The hadith is from Bukhari and is sahih.
4
Understand the Hanafi Usul Principle
The Hanafi school holds that a command (amr) normally indicates obligation, but that default can be overridden by context or other proofs. Here, the absence of definitive evidence for obligation and the encouraging tone of the hadith lead to the ruling of sunnah.
This is a key distinction in Hanafi legal theory.
5
Compare with Other Schools
Note that the Shafi'i and Hanbali schools consider Umrah obligatory. Understand that this ikhtilaf arises from different usul principles regarding the interpretation of commands.
This highlights the role of usul al-fiqh in shaping fiqh rulings.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۴۰۵) اور عمرہ سنت ہے۔ وجه : (1) اس آیت میں عمرہ کا ثبوت ہے ۔ و اتموا الحج و العمرة لله - ( آیت ۱۹۶ ،سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں عمرہ کو حج کے ساتھ بیان کیا ہے اس سے عمرہ کے سنت ہونے کا پتہ چلتا ہے۔ عـن ابـی هــيـرة ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال العمرة الى العمرة كفارة لما بينهما ، و الحج المبرور ليس له جزاء الا الجنة - ( بخاری شریف ، باب وجوب العمرة وفضلها ، ص ۲۸۵، نمبر ۱۷۷۳) اس حدیث میں عمرہ کے سنت ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔
Translation: (1405) And Umrah is sunnah. Proof: (1) In this verse there is evidence for Umrah: 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196). This verse mentions Umrah alongside Hajj, indicating that Umrah is sunnah. From Abu Hurayrah that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Umrah to Umrah is expiation for what is between them, and the accepted Hajj has no reward but Paradise.' (Bukhari, Bab Wujub al-Umrah wa Fadliha, p. 285, no. 1773) This hadith is evidence that Umrah is sunnah.
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil naqli). It establishes that Umrah is sunnah (recommended) in the Hanafi school, not obligatory. The proof is from Quran 2:196, which commands completing Umrah, and the hadith that Umrah expiates sins between them. The Hanafi interpretation of 'command' here is that it indicates sunnah, not wujub (obligation), because the context and other evidences show it is not fard. The hadith further encourages it.

Key Terms
سنت (sunnah): A confirmed recommended act; performing it is rewardable, leaving it is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Obligation of Hadi for the Qarin
Stating that a qarin must sacrifice a hadi on Yawm al-Nahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on hadi for the qarin, explain the qiyas proof from tamattu', and apply the ruling to a scenario.

Core Idea
A qarin must sacrifice a hadi because qiran is analogous to tamattu'—the same Quranic obligation applies.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling that a qarin must offer a hadi (sacrificial animal) on Yawm al-Nahr. The proof is based on a clear analogy (qiyas) with the tamattu' pilgrim, for whom the Quran explicitly commands a hadi. Understanding this ruling clarifies an essential duty for those performing qiran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sacrificing a hadi by a qarin on Yawm al-Nahr after ramy. The ruling is wajib (obligatory).
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse 2:196 commands hadi for tamattu'; the proof for qiran is qiyas.
Quran 2:196: فمن تمتع بالعمرة الى الحج فما استيسر من الهدى
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The illa (effective cause) is that both qarin and mutamatti' combine Umrah and Hajj in one journey, enjoying the benefits.
This is a jaliyy (clear) qiyas.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no major ikhtilaf; all schools agree hadi is wajib on qarin.
The ruling is muttafaq alayh.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah, supported by jumhur.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : ( ۱۴۰۷) جب یوم نحر میں جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کرے تو اس پر ایک بکری یا بد نہ کا ساتواں حصہ ذبح کرنا واجب ہے۔ تشریح : قارن اور تتمتع پر ہدی لازم ہے۔ اور ہدی کی صورت یہ ہے کہ ایک بکری ہو یا ایک گائے ہو یا ایک اونٹ ہو یا گائے کا ساتواں حصہ یا اونٹ کا ساتواں حصہ ہو۔ وجه : (۱) قرآن تمتع کے درجے میں ہے اور تمتع کے بارے میں اس آیت میں ہے کہ ہدی لازم ہے اس لئے قرآن میں بھی ہدی لا زم ہوگی ۔ فمن تمتع بالعمرة الى الحج فما استيسر من الهدى فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلثة ايام في الحج وسبعة اذا رجعتم تلک عشرة کاملة ذلك لمن لم يكن اهله حاضرى المسجد الحرام. (آیت ١٩٦ سورة البقرة ٢)
Translation: (1407) When on Yawm al-Nahr he throws the stones at Jamrat al-Aqabah, then upon him is wajib to slaughter one goat or one-seventh of a camel. Commentary: Hadi is obligatory upon the qarin and the mutamatti'. The form of hadi is: one goat, or one cow, or one camel, or one-seventh of a cow, or one-seventh of a camel. Proof: (1) Qiran is in the degree of Tamattu', and regarding Tamattu' this verse says that hadi is obligatory: '...And whoever performs Tamattu' by Umrah to Hajj, then [offer] whatever is easy of hadi...' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196) So for Qiran, hadi is also obligatory.
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil naqli). It establishes that a qarin must slaughter a hadi (sacrificial animal) on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) after stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah. The hadi can be a goat, or a share in a cow or camel (one-seventh). The proof is based on analogy: Qiran is likened to Tamattu', for which Quran 2:196 prescribes a hadi. Therefore, the same obligation applies to the qarin. This is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
ہدی (hadi): The sacrificial animal offered by a qarin or mutamatti' during Hajj.
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing Umrah first, then breaking ihram, and later assuming ihram for Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling regarding hadi for a qarin according to this passage?
A) It is sunnah
B) It is wajib
C) It is haram
D) It is optional

Key Takeaway
The qarin must offer a hadi on Yawm al-Nahr; this obligation is proven by qiyas to tamattu'.

Rulings of 'Umrah and Hady for Qiran Hajj
Ruling-with-proof: 'Umrah acts, its sunnah status, and Hady obligation for Qarin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the acts of 'Umrah for a Qarin, explain why 'Umrah is sunnah in the Hanafi school, and apply the obligation of Hady and its fasting substitute when unable.

Core Idea
A Qarin must perform complete 'Umrah and Hajj; Hady is wajib, substituted by 10 days of fasting.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh work details the rituals of 'Umrah for a person performing Qiran Hajj and then establishes two key rulings: first, that 'Umrah is sunnah (not fard), and second, that a Qarin must slaughter a sacrificial animal (hady) and, if unable, fast instead. The author cites the Quran and several hadiths to support these positions, and also addresses a cross-madhhab difference with the Shafi'i school regarding the status of 'Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts of 'Umrah
List the specific actions: 7 circuits of tawaf with raml in first three, two rak'ahs, then sa'i between Safa and Marwah with running between the green markers.
These are the core acts; halq/taqsir is assumed but not mentioned here.
2
Determine the ruling of 'Umrah
The text states 'wal-'umratu sunnah'. Understand that in Hanafi fiqh this means sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard. Note the evidence: Quran 2:196 and the hadith on 'Umrah expiating sins.
Shafi'i school differs: they hold 'Umrah is fard.
3
Recognize the obligation of Hady
After throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah on 10th Dhul-Hijjah, a Qarin (and Mutamatti') must slaughter a sheep or share a cow/camel (1/7 each).
This is wajib, not fard, due to zanni evidence.
4
Learn the substitute fasting
If unable to sacrifice, fast 3 days before the Day of Nahr during Hajj months (but not on Arafah or Tashriq) and 7 days after returning, even in Makkah after Tashriq.
The 3+7=10 days are clearly specified in the Quran.
5
Analyze the proofs
The author uses Quran 2:196, hadith of Ibn Abbas linking Tamattu' to Hady, hadith of Jabir on sharing, and hadith prohibiting fasting on Tashriq. Identify the dalil type (Quran, ahad hadith) and its epistemological weight.
The Quranic verse is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalalah regarding obligation.

(1405) والعمرة سنة (1406) ثم يطوف طواف القدوم للحج ثم يتم افعال الحج كما تقدّم (1407) فاذا رمى يوم النحر جمرة العقبة وجب عليه ذبح شاة او سُبُع بدنة (1408) فاذا لم يجد فصيام ثلاثة ايام قبل مجئ يوم النحر من اشهر الحج وسبعة ايام بعد الفراغ من الحج ولو بمكة بعد مضى ايام التشريق ولو فرّقها جاز.
ترجمه : (1404) پھر صفا کی طرف نکلے، اور اس کے اوپر کھڑا ہو دعا کرتے ہوئے، تکبیر تہلیل ، تلبیہ، نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم پر درود پڑھتے ہوئے۔ پھر مروہ کی طرف اترے اور میلین کے درمیان دوڑے اس طرح سات چکر پورے کرے۔ یہ عمرہ کے افعال ہوئے۔ تشریح : یہ عمرہ کا تیسر اعمل ہے کہ صفا پر آکر تکبیر و تہلیل کرے تلبیہ پڑھے، حضور پر درود شریف پڑھے، اور دعا کرے، پھر اسی طرح مروہ پر کرے اور صفا سے مروہ پر جاتے ہوئے میلین اخضرین کے درمیان دوڑے۔ اور سعی کے سات چکر پورا کرے۔ باقی تفصیل اور دلائل پہلے گزر چکے ہیں وہاں دیکھیں۔
ترجمه : (1405) اور عمرہ سنت ہے۔ وجه : (1) اس آیت میں عمرہ کا ثبوت ہے ۔ و اتموا الحج و العمرة لله - ( آیت 196 ،سورۃ البقرۃ 2) اس آیت میں عمرہ کو حج کے ساتھ بیان کیا ہے اس سے عمرہ کے سنت ہونے کا پتہ چلتا ہے۔ عـن ابـی هــيـرة ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال العمرة الى العمرة كفارة لما بينهما ، و الحج المبرور ليس له جزاء الا الجنة - ( بخاری شریف ، باب وجوب العمرة وفضلها ، ص 285، نمبر 1773) اس حدیث میں عمرہ کے سنت ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔
ترجمه : (1406) پھر حج کا طواف قدوم کرے، پھر حج کے افعال پورے کرے جیسا پہلے بیان کیا۔ تشريح عمرے کے اعمال سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد حج کے لئے طواف قدوم کرے اور آٹھویں ذی الحجہ سے حج کے اعمال پورے کرے۔ البتہ چونکہ عمرے میں طواف قدوم ادا ہو چکا ہے اس لئے اب طواف قدوم اتنا ضروری نہیں، البتہ کرلے تو اچھا ہے۔
ترجمه : (1407) جب یوم نحر میں جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کرے تو اس پر ایک بکری یا بد نہ کا ساتواں حصہ ذبح کرنا واجب ہے۔ تشریح : قارن اور تتمتع پر ہدی لازم ہے۔ اور ہدی کی صورت یہ ہے کہ ایک بکری ہو یا ایک گائے ہو یا ایک اونٹ ہو یا گائے کا ساتواں حصہ یا اونٹ کا ساتواں حصہ ہو۔ وجه : (1) قرآن تمتع کے درجے میں ہے اور تمتع کے بارے میں اس آیت میں ہے کہ ہدی لازم ہے اس لئے قرآن میں بھی ہدی لا زم ہوگی ۔ فمن تمتع بالعمرة الى الحج فما استيسر من الهدى فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلثة ايام في الحج وسبعة اذا رجعتم تلک عشرة کاملة ذلك لمن لم يكن اهله حاضرى المسجد الحرام. (آیت 196 سورة البقرة 2) (2) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس انه سئل عن متعة الحج فقال ... ثم امرنا عشية التروية ان نهل بالحج فاذا فرغنا من المناسک جئنا فـطـفـنـا بالبيت وبالصفا والمروة فقد تم حجنا وعلينا الهدى كما قال الله عز وجل فما استيسر من الهدى. (بخاری شریف ، باب قول الله عز وجل ذلك لمن لم يكن اصله حاضری المسجد الحرام ص 213 نمبر 1572) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ متمتع اور قارن پر ہدی لازم ہے۔ (3) اور گائے یا اونٹ کے ساتویں حصے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله قال نـحـر نـامـع رســول اللـه الا الله عام الحديبية البدنة عن سبعة والبقرة عن سبعة۔ (مسلم شریف، باب جواز الاشتراک فی الھدی واجزاء البدنة والبقرة كل واحد منهما عن سبعه ،ص 553، نمبر 1318/ 3185 را بو داؤد شریف، باب البقرة والجزور عن كم تجربی ص 409 نمبر 2809) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ گائے اور اونٹ سات آدمیوں کی جانب سے کافی ہے۔
ترجمه : (1408) اور اگر ہدی کی طاقت نہ رکھتا ہو تو تین روزے ہیں دسویں ذی الحجہ آنے سے پہلے حج کے مہینوں میں ، اور سات دن حج سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد چاہے مکہ مکرمہ میں ہو ایام تشریق گزرنے کے بعد ۔ وجه : (1) پہلے آیت گزرگئی کہ ہدی نہ ہو تو روزے رکھے، فمن تمتع بالعمرة الى الحج فما استيسر من الهدى فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلثة ايام فى الحج و سبعة اذا رجعتم تلك عشرة كاملة ( آیت 96 اسورۃ البقرۃ 2) اس آیت میں ہے کہ ہدی نہ دے سکو تو روزے رکھو۔ (2) اور ایام تشریق میں روزہ نہ رکھے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عقبة بن عامر قال قال رسول الله يوم عرفة ويوم النحر وايام التشريق عيدنا اهل الاسلام وهى ايام اكل و شرب (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب صیام ايام التشريق ص 1338، نمبر 2419 / مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم صوم ايام التشريق، ص 360 ، نمبر 1141 سے 267) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ یوم عرفہ اور ایام تشریق سے پہلے پہلے تین روزے رکھ لے (3) مکہ میں بھی روزہ رکھ سکتا ہے اور راستے میں بھی رکھ سکتا ہے۔ عن عطاء قال وسبعة اذا رجعتم (الآية) قال ان شاء صامها في الطريق وان شاء بمكة۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة 45 في قضاء السبعة الفرق او الوصل ج ثالث ، ص 151 نمبر 12995) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مکہ مکرمہ میں بھی روزہ رکھ سکتا ہے اور راستے میں بھی رکھ سکتا ہے۔
Chapter of Qiran: Seven circuits, he walks quickly in the first three only, then prays two rak'ahs of tawaf (1404). Then he goes to as-Safa and stands upon it supplicating, saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, sending blessings on the Prophet (PBUH). Then he descends towards al-Marwah and runs between the two markers, completing seven circuits. These are the acts of 'Umrah (1405). And 'Umrah is sunnah (1406). Then he performs Tawaf al-Qudum for Hajj, then completes the acts of Hajj as previously mentioned (1407). When he throws the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr, it becomes obligatory upon him to slaughter a sheep or a seventh of a badanah (1408). If he cannot find [an animal], then fasting three days before the Day of Nahr from the months of Hajj, and seven days after completing Hajj, even if in Makkah after the days of Tashriq have passed, and even if he does them separately, it is permissible.
Translation: (1404) Then he goes towards Safa, and stands upon it making supplication, saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, sending blessings on the Prophet (PBUH). Then he descends towards Marwah and runs between the two green markers, thus completing seven circuits. These are the acts of 'Umrah. Explanation: This is the third act of 'Umrah: that upon coming to Safa he says takbir and tahlil, recites talbiyah, sends salawat on the Prophet, and makes supplication; then similarly at Marwah; and while going from Safa to Marwah he runs between the two green markers. And he completes seven circuits of Sa'i. The remaining details and proofs have passed earlier; see them there.
Translation: (1405) And 'Umrah is sunnah. Evidence: (1) This verse proves 'Umrah: 'And complete the Hajj and 'Umrah for Allah' (Al-Baqarah 2:196). In this verse, 'Umrah is mentioned with Hajj; this indicates that 'Umrah is sunnah. From Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) said: 'The 'Umrah to the next 'Umrah is expiation for what is between them, and the accepted Hajj has no reward except Paradise' (Bukhari, Chapter on Obligation and Virtue of 'Umrah, p.285, no.1773). This hadith is evidence for 'Umrah being sunnah.
Translation: (1406) Then he performs Tawaf al-Qudum for Hajj, then completes the acts of Hajj as previously described. Explanation: After finishing the acts of 'Umrah, he performs Tawaf al-Qudum for Hajj and completes the acts of Hajj from the eighth of Dhul-Hijjah. However, since Tawaf al-Qudum has already been performed in 'Umrah, now Tawaf al-Qudum is not so necessary; but if he does it, it is good.
Translation: (1407) When he throws the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr, slaughtering a sheep or a seventh of a badanah becomes wajib upon him. Explanation: Hady is obligatory upon the Qarin and the Mutamatti'. The form of Hady is a sheep, or a cow, or a camel, or a seventh of a cow, or a seventh of a camel. Evidence: (1) Qiran is in the same category as Tamattu', and regarding Tamattu' this verse states that Hady is obligatory, so Hady is also obligatory for Qiran: '...then whoever performs 'Umrah and Hajj consecutively, then offer whatever sacrificial animal is easy. And whoever cannot find [an animal] then fast three days during Hajj and seven when you return; that is ten complete days. That is for those whose family is not present at al-Masjid al-Haram' (Al-Baqarah 2:196). (2) There is a hadith: from Ibn Abbas that he was asked about Mut'ah of Hajj... then he said: 'Then he commanded us on the eve of Tarwiyah to assume ihram for Hajj, and when we finished the rituals we came and performed tawaf of the House and between Safa and Marwah, so our Hajj was complete and upon us was the Hady as Allah said: '...then whatever sacrificial animal is easy'' (Bukhari, Chapter on the Saying of Allah: 'That is for those whose family is not present at al-Masjid al-Haram', p.213, no.1572). From this hadith it is also known that Hady is obligatory upon the Mutamatti' and Qarin. (3) And the evidence for the seventh of a cow or camel is this hadith: from Jabir ibn Abdullah that he said: 'We sacrificed with the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) in the year of Hudaybiyyah a camel for seven and a cow for seven' (Muslim, Chapter on Permissibility of Sharing in Hady and Sufficiency of Camel and Cow for Seven each, p.553, no.1318/3185; also Abu Dawood, Chapter on Cow and Camel for how many are sufficient, p.409, no.2809). From this hadith it is known that a cow and a camel are sufficient on behalf of seven persons.
Translation: (1408) And if he does not have the ability for Hady, then three fasts are [due] before the coming of the Day of Nahr from the months of Hajj, and seven days after finishing Hajj, even if in Makkah after the days of Tashriq have passed, and even if he does them separately, it is permissible. Evidence: (1) The verse has already passed: '...then whoever cannot find then fast three days during Hajj and seven when you return' (Al-Baqarah 2:196). (2) And he should not fast on the days of Tashriq; the evidence for this is the hadith from Uqbah ibn Amir that the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) said: 'The Day of Arafah, the Day of Nahr, and the days of Tashriq are our festivals, O people of Islam, and they are days of eating and drinking' (Abu Dawood, Chapter on Fasting the Days of Tashriq, p.1338, no.2419; Muslim, Chapter on Prohibition of Fasting the Days of Tashriq, p.360, no.1141-267). This hadith proves that he should fast the three fasts before the Day of Arafah and the days of Tashriq. (3) He may fast in Makkah or on the road. From Ata that: 'And seven when you return' (the verse) he said: 'If he wishes, he may fast them on the road, and if he wishes, in Makkah' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 45, in 'Qada' al-Sab'ah al-Farq aw al-Wasl', vol.3, p.151, no.12995). This tradition shows that he may fast in Makkah or on the road.
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section from the chapter on Qiran in a Hanafi fiqh work. It begins by describing the acts of 'Umrah for the Qarin: seven circuits of tawaf (with raml in the first three), two rak'ahs after tawaf, then going to Safa and Marwah for sa'i (seven circuits with running between the green markers). The text then states (1405) that 'Umrah is sunnah, not fard, citing the Quranic verse 'And complete the Hajj and 'Umrah for Allah' and the hadith where the Prophet says that 'Umrah to 'Umrah expiates sins. Following 'Umrah, the Qarin performs Tawaf al-Qudum for Hajj (1406) and then completes all Hajj rituals. The key ruling (1407-1408) is that after throwing the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr, the Qarin (and similarly the Mutamatti') must slaughter a sacrificial animal (hady) — either a sheep, or a seventh share of a camel or cow. If unable, the alternative is fasting: three days before the Day of Nahr (during the months of Hajj, but not on Arafah or the days of Tashriq) and seven days after returning from Hajj (even in Makkah after Tashriq). The author provides proofs: the Quranic verse (2:196) linking tamattu' and qiran to hady, hadith from Ibn Abbas, hadith of Jabir about sharing a camel/cow for seven, and the prohibition of fasting on Eid days. The passage follows the author's own order: first the acts, then the rulings with evidence. It is typical of a sharh (commentary) that expands on a matn by giving detailed legal reasoning and supporting proofs from primary sources.

Key Terms
قارن (qarin): A person who performs Hajj and 'Umrah combined in a single ihram.
هدي (hady): The sacrificial animal offered by a Qarin or Mutamatti' during Hajj.
عمرة (umrah): The minor pilgrimage consisting of tawaf, sa'i, and halq or taqsir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what must a Qarin do after throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah if he cannot find a sacrificial animal?
A) He must slaughter a sheep regardless of cost.
B) He must fast 10 consecutive days immediately.
C) He must fast 3 days during Hajj before the Day of Nahr and 7 days after completing Hajj.
D) He must fast 7 days during Hajj and 3 days after returning.

Key Takeaway
A Qarin must offer Hady (sacrifice); if unable, the substitute is 3 fasts before 10th Dhul-Hijjah and 7 fasts after Hajj, not on Tashriq days.

The Obligation of Hadi for Tamattu' and Qiran
Ruling on Hadi for mutamatti' and qarin, with fasting alternative and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of Hadi for the Mutamatti' and Qarin, explain the alternative fasting rules, and identify the Quranic and hadith evidence supporting the ruling.

Core Idea
Hadi is wajib for Tamattu' and Qiran; if unaffordable, ten fasts with specific timings fulfill the obligation.

This lesson unpacks the ruling on the sacrificial offering (hadi) for two specific types of Hajj pilgrims: the Mutamatti' and the Qarin. According to the Hanafi school, this offering is wajib based on clear Quranic and Prophetic evidence. If the pilgrim cannot afford it, a defined fasting schedule becomes the required substitute. By studying this passage, you will learn the precise obligations, their proofs, and the details of timing and location.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage addresses the obligation of Hadi for Mutamatti' and Qarin. What is the ruling? (Wajib).
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic verse (2:196) is cited. Identify the key phrase indicating obligation: 'fayastaysir min al-hadi' and the conditional alternative 'faman lam yajid fasiyam'.
3
Trace the substitute ruling
If unable to afford a sacrifice, what is the alternative? How many fasts, when, and where? (Three days before Nahr, seven after Hajj, can be in Makkah or on road, need not be consecutive).
Pay attention to the prohibition of fasting on days of Tashriq.
4
Examine the supporting hadith
Two hadiths support the ruling: the hadith of Ibn Abbas showing the Prophet's practice and the hadith of Jabir on sharing a camel/cow among seven.
5
Synthesize the full picture
Combine the evidence to state the complete rule: who (Mutamatti'/Qarin), what (sacrifice or fast), when (timing), where (location), and what if unable.
