وجـب عـلـيـه ذبح شاة او سُبُع بدنة (۱۴۰۸ ) فاذا لم يجد فصيام ثلاثة ايام قبل مجئ يوم النحر من اشهر الحج وسبعة ايام بعد الفراغ من الحج ولو بمكة بعد مضى ايام التشريق ولو فرّقها جاز. اس آیت میں ہے کہ قارن اور متمتع پر ہدی ہے اور وہ نہ دے سکے تو اس پر دس دن کے روزے ہیں۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس انه سئل عن متعة الحج فقال ... ثم امرنا عشية التروية ان نهل بالحج فاذا فرغنا من المناسک جئنا فـطـفـنـا بالبيت وبالصفا والمروة فقد تم حجنا وعلينا الهدى كما قال الله عز وجل فما استيسر من الهدى. (بخاری شریف ، باب قول الله عز وجل ذلك لمن لم یکن اصله حاضری المسجد الحرام ص ۲۱۳ نمبر ۱۵۷۲) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ متمتع اور قارن پر ہدی لازم ہے۔ (۳) اور گائے یا اونٹ کے ساتویں حصے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله قال نـحـر نـامـع رســول اللـه الا الله عام الحديبية البدنة عن سبعة والبقرة عن سبعة۔ (مسلم شریف، باب جواز الاشتراک فی الھدی واجزاء البدنة والبقرة كل واحد منهما عن سبعه ،ص ۵۵۳، نمبر ۱۳۱۸/ ۳۱۸۵ را بو داؤد شریف، باب البقرة والجزور عن كم تجربی ص ۴۰۹ نمبر ۲۸۰۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ گائے اور اونٹ سات آدمیوں کی جانب سے کافی ہے۔ ترجمه : ( ۱۴۰۸) اور اگر ہدی کی طاقت نہ رکھتا ہو تو تین روزے ہیں دسویں ذی الحجہ آنے سے پہلے حج کے مہینوں میں ، اور سات دن حج سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد چاہے مکہ مکرمہ میں ہو ایام تشریق گزرنے کے بعد ۔ وجه : (۱) پہلے آیت گزرگئی کہ ہدی نہ ہو تو روزے رکھے، فمن تمتع بالعمرة الى الحج فما استيسر من الهدى فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلثة ايام فى الحج و سبعة اذا رجعتم تلك عشرة كاملة ( آیت ۹۶ اسورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ ہدی نہ دے سکو تو روزے رکھو۔ (۲) اور ایام تشریق میں روزہ نہ رکھے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عقبة بن عامر قال قال رسول الله يوم عرفة ويوم النحر وايام التشريق عيدنا اهل الاسلام وهى ايام اكل و شرب (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب صیام ايام التشريق ص ۱۳۳۸، نمبر ۲۴۱۹ / مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم صوم ايام التشريق، ص ۳۶۰ ، نمبر ۱۱۴۱ سے ۲۶۷) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ یوم عرفہ اور ایام تشریق سے پہلے پہلے تین روزے رکھ لے (۳) مکہ میں بھی روزہ رکھ سکتا ہے اور راستے میں بھی رکھ سکتا ہے۔ عن عطاء قال وسبعة اذا رجعتم (الآية) قال ان شاء صامها في الطريق وان شاء بمكة۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۴۵ في قضاء السبعة الفرق او الوصل ج ثالث ، ص ۱۵۱ نمبر ۱۲۹۹۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مکہ مکرمہ میں بھی روزہ رکھ سکتا ہے اور راستے میں بھی رکھ سکتا ہے۔
Section on Qiran. It is obligatory upon him to slaughter a sheep or a seventh of a camel (1408). If he does not find it, then fasting three days before the coming of Yawm al-Nahr from the months of Hajj, and seven days after completing Hajj, even if in Makkah after the days of Tashriq have passed, and if he separates them it is permissible. In this verse it is said that on the Qarin and Mutamatti' there is Hadi, and if he cannot give it, then upon him are ten days of fasting. (2) In a hadith: from Ibn Abbas that he was asked about Tamattu' of Hajj... then he said: then he commanded us on the evening of Tarwiyya to enter into Ihram for Hajj, and when we finished the rites we came and circumambulated the House and between Safa and Marwa, so our Hajj was complete and upon us was the Hadi as Allah said: 'whatever is affordable of the sacrificial animal.' (Bukhari, chapter on the saying of Allah: 'that is for the one whose family is not present at the Sacred Mosque' p. 213 no. 1572). From this hadith it is also known that Hadi is obligatory on the Mutamatti' and Qarin. (3) And the evidence for the seventh part of a cow or camel is this hadith: from Jabir ibn Abdullah said: we sacrificed with the Messenger of Allah in the year of Hudaybiyya a camel for seven and a cow for seven. (Muslim, chapter on permissibility of joining in Hadi and that a camel and a cow suffice for seven each, p. 553 no. 1318/3185; Abu Dawud, chapter on the cow and camel: how many do they suffice for? p. 409 no. 2809). From this hadith it is known that a cow and a camel are sufficient on behalf of seven persons. Translation: (1408) And if he does not have the ability to offer Hadi, then three fasts are due before the 10th of Dhul Hijjah in the months of Hajj, and seven days after completing Hajj, even if in Makkah after the days of Tashriq have passed. Explanation: (1) The verse has already passed that if Hadi is not available then fast, 'Whoever performs Tamattu' of Umrah to Hajj, then whatever is affordable of the sacrificial animal, and whoever does not find it, then fasting three days in Hajj and seven when you return, that is ten complete' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:96). In this verse it is that if you cannot give Hadi then fast. (2) And do not fast on the days of Tashriq, its evidence is this hadith: from Uqba ibn Amir said: the Messenger of Allah said: the day of Arafa, the day of Nahr, and the days of Tashriq are our 'Eid, O people of Islam, and they are days of eating and drinking. (Abu Dawud, chapter on fasting the days of Tashriq p. 1338 no. 2419; Muslim, chapter on prohibition of fasting days of Tashriq p. 360 no. 1141/267). From this hadith it is proven that he should fast three days before Yawm Arafa and the days of Tashriq. (3) He can fast in Makkah and on the road. From Ata said: 'and seven when you return' (the verse) said: if he wishes he fasts them on the road, and if he wishes in Makkah. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 45 on making up the seven: separation or joining, vol. 3 p. 151 no. 12995). From this effect it is known that he can fast in Makkah and on the road.
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the sacrifice (Hadi) required for those performing Hajj as Qiran or Tamattu'. The ruling states that if a person cannot afford a sheep or a seventh share of a camel, they are obligated to fast three days before the 10th of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm al-Nahr) during the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, first ten days of Dhul Hijjah) and seven days after completing the Hajj rituals, even if they do so in Makkah after the days of Tashriq have passed. It is permissible to fast these days separately, i.e., the three before and the seven after need not be consecutive. The passage then provides three proofs. First, the Quranic verse (2:196) which explicitly states the alternative of fasting for those who cannot find a sacrificial animal. Second, a hadith from Ibn Abbas (r) where the Prophet (s) commanded them to perform Hajj after Umrah and that Hadi is obligatory. Third, a hadith from Jabir (r) that a camel or cow suffices for seven persons in sacrifice, indicating that a seventh share is acceptable. The explanation adds that fasting during the days of Tashriq (11th-13th Dhul Hijjah) is prohibited, as these are 'Eid days of eating and drinking, so the three fasts must be completed before the 10th. The seven fasts can be done in Makkah or on the return journey, based on the narration from Ata. The ruling is clear that the Hadi is obligatory (wajib) upon the Mutamatti' and Qarin, and fasting is a substitute only when one cannot afford it.

Key Terms
هدی (hadiy): The sacrificial animal (camel, cow, or sheep) offered during Hajj as an act of worship and due obligation for Mutamatti' and Qarin.
متمتع (mutamatti'): A person who performs Umrah first in the months of Hajj, then performs Hajj in the same year without returning to the miqat, thus enjoying the interim ihram-free period.
قارن (qarin): A person who combines Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram from the miqat.
ايام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The three days following Yawm al-Nahr: 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, if a Mutamatti' cannot afford the Hadi, how many fasts must he observe and when?
A) Three fasts before 'Eid and seven after, all in Makkah
B) Three fasts before 'Eid and seven after, can be done in Makkah or on the return
C) Ten fasts continuously after Hajj
D) Seven fasts before 'Eid and three after

Key Takeaway
The obligation of hadi for Tamattu' and Qiran is wajib; if unaffordable, ten fasts with specific timings completely fulfill the duty.

Tamattu' in Hajj: Definition and Two Types
Definition of Tamattu' and its two types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Tamattu', distinguish it from Qiran, and identify the two types based on bringing Hadi.

Core Idea
Tamattu': performing Umrah then Hajj in one journey, with two types depending on Hadi.

This lesson parses the classical Hanafi definition of Tamattu', clarifying its linguistic root and its two operational forms. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly performing Hajj al-Tamattu' and knowing when Hadi becomes due.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its linguistic origin
Locate the word 'Tamattu'' and note its derivation from 'mata'' meaning benefit. Understand why this form is called 'Tamattu''.
The pilgrim benefits from both Umrah and Hajj in one journey.
2
Extract the core definition
Find the sentence that defines Tamattu': entering ihram for Umrah only from the miqat in the months of Hajj, then performing Umrah, becoming halal, and later entering ihram for Hajj.
The definition is: 'al-tamattu' huwa an yuhrima bi al-umrati faqat min al-miqat...'
3
Distinguish from Qiran
Read the explanation that contrasts Tamattu' with Qiran. Note that in Qiran, both Hajj and Umrah are combined in one ihram, while in Tamattu' they are in separate ihrams.
Key difference: one ihram vs two separate ihrams.
4
Parse the two types based on Hadi
Identify the two scenarios: (1) bringing Hadi – then the pilgrim does not become halal after Umrah but remains in ihram until after Hajj; (2) not bringing Hadi – then the pilgrim becomes halal after Umrah and later re-enters ihram for Hajj.
The Hadi determines the timing of becoming halal.
5
Identify the proof from hadith
Find the hadith of Ibn Umar describing the Prophet's Tamattu' in the Farewell Hajj. Note that the hadith also distinguishes between those with and without Hadi.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.

فصل التمتع
(۱۴۰۹) التمتع هو ان يحرم بالعمرة فقط من الميقات فيقول بعد صلوة ركعتي الاحرام اللهم انى
فصل: تمتع کے بیان میں
ضروری نوٹ: حج کے مہینے شوال، ذی قعدہ اور ذی الحجہ کی دس تاریخ میں عمرے کا احرام باند ھے پھر عمرہ کر کے حلال ہو جائے اور حج کے زمانے میں حج کا احرام باندھ کر حج پورا کرے اس کو تمتع کہتے ہیں۔ تمتع متع سے مشتق ہے، اس کا ترجمہ ہے فائدہ اٹھانا، چونکہ ایک سفر میں عمرہ اور حج دونوں سے فائدہ اٹھاتا ہے، اور عمرے کا احرام کھول کر حلال ہونے کا فائدہ اٹھاتا ہے اس لئے اس کو تمتع کہتے ہیں۔ اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ فمن تمتع بالعمرة الى الحج فما استيسر من الهدى . ( آيت ٩٦اسورة البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے تمتع ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۴۰۹) تمتع یہ ہے کہ میقات سے صرف عمرہ کا احرام باندھے ، اور احرام کی دورکعت کے بعد کہے: اے اللہ میں عمرہ کا ارادہ کرتا ہوں میرے لئے آسان فرمادیجئے اور میری طرف سے قبول فرمائیے۔
تشریح : قرآن اور تمتع میں فرق یہ ہے کہ قرآن میں حج اور عمرے دونوں کا احرام ایک ساتھ باندھتے ہیں۔ اور دسویں تاریخ کو ایک ساتھ دونوں احراموں سے حلال ہوتے ہیں۔ اور تمتع میں میقات سے پہلے عمرے کا احرام باندھتے ہیں اور اس سے حلال ہونے کے بعد پھر آٹھ ذی الحجہ کو حج کا احرام باندھتے ہیں۔ اس کے لئے عمرے کا طریقہ بتا رہے ہیں کہ عمرے کے لئے احرام کا کپڑا پہننے کے بعد دو رکعت نماز پڑھے اور کہے میں عمرے کا ارادہ کرتا ہوں ، ائے اللہ اس کو آسان کر دیجئے ، اور قبول کیجئے تمتع کے لئے عمرے کی دو قسمیں ہوتیں ہیں [1] ایک یہ ہے کہ ساتھ ھدی لیجائے ، اس صورت میں عمرے کے بعد حلال نہیں ہوگا، بلکہ حج مکمل کرنے کے بعد دونوں احراموں سے ایک ساتھ حلال ہوگا ۔ [۲] اور دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ ہدی ساتھ نہ لیجائے اس صورت میں عمرہ کرنے کے بعد حلال ہو جائے ، پھر آٹھ ذی الحجہ کو حج کا احرام باندھے۔
وجه : (1) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ ان ابن عمر قال تمتع رسول الله الله الله في حجة الوداع بالعمرة الى الحج و أهدى فساق معه الهدى من ذي الحليفة و بدأ رسول الله له فأهل بالعمرة ثم اهل بالحج ، فكان من الناس من أهدى فساق الهدى و منهم من لم يهد . فلما قدم النبي الله مكة قال للناس من كان منكم أهدى فانه لا يحل من شيء حرم منه حتى يقضى حجه، و من لم يكن منكم أهدى فليطف بالبيت و بالصفا و المروة و يقصر و ليحلل ثم ليهل بالحج ( بخاری شریف، باب من ساق البدن معه ص ۲۷۴، نمبر ۱۹۹۱ار مسلم شریف ، باب وجوب الدم على امتع وانه اذ اعد مه لزمه صوم ثلاثۃ ایام فی الجی بص ۵۲۱، نمبر ۲۹۸۲/۱۲۲۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عمرے کا احرام باندھا
Section on Tamattu' (1409) Tamattu' is that one enters ihram only for Umrah from the miqat and says after the two rak'ahs of ihram: 'O Allah, I intend Umrah, make it easy for me and accept it from me.' Section: On the explanation of Tamattu'. Essential Note: In the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten of Dhu al-Hijjah) he ties the ihram for Umrah, then performs Umrah and becomes halal, and then in the time of Hajj he ties ihram for Hajj and completes Hajj; this is called Tamattu'. Tamattu' is derived from mata', meaning to take benefit. Since he benefits from both Umrah and Hajj in one journey, and benefits from opening the ihram of Umrah and becoming halal, it is called Tamattu'. Its proof is this verse: 'Whoever performs Tamattu' of Umrah to Hajj, then whatever is affordable of the sacrificial animal' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:96). From this verse Tamattu' is established. Translation: (1409) Tamattu' is that he ties ihram only for Umrah from the miqat, and after the two rak'ahs of ihram says: 'O Allah, I intend Umrah, make it easy for me and accept from me.' Explanation: The difference between Qiran and Tamattu' is that in Qiran he ties ihram for both Hajj and Umrah together, and on the 10th he becomes halal from both ihrams together. In Tamattu', he ties ihram for Umrah from the miqat first, and after becoming halal from it, he ties ihram for Hajj on the 8th of Dhu al-Hijjah. For this, he explains the method of Umrah: after wearing the ihram garment, he prays two rak'ahs and says 'I intend Umrah, O Allah make it easy for me and accept it.' For Tamattu', there are two types of Umrah: [1] One is that he brings Hadi with him; in this case he will not become halal after Umrah, but will become halal from both ihrams together after completing Hajj. [2] The second type is that he does not bring Hadi; in this case he becomes halal after performing Umrah, then ties ihram for Hajj on the 8th of Dhu al-Hijjah. Proof: (1) In this hadith: Ibn Umar said: The Messenger of Allah performed Tamattu' in the Farewell Hajj, performing Umrah to Hajj, and he offered Hadi, he drove the sacrificial animals from Dhu al-Hulayfah. The Messenger of Allah began by entering ihram for Umrah, then entered ihram for Hajj. Among the people, some brought Hadi and some did not. When the Prophet arrived in Makkah, he said to the people: 'Whoever among you has brought Hadi, he should not become halal from anything that was prohibited until he completes his Hajj. And whoever among you has not brought Hadi, let him circumambulate the House and between Safa and Marwa, shorten (his hair), and become halal, then enter ihram for Hajj.' (Bukhari, chapter on one who drives sacrificial animals with him, p. 274 no. 1991; Muslim, chapter on the obligation of blood (sacrifice) for the Mutamatti' and that if he does not bring it, fasting three days in Hajj is obligatory, p. 521 no. 2982/1227). In this hadith, he tied ihram for Umrah.
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage defines Tamattu' in Hajj and explains its two types. Linguistically, Tamattu' derives from mata' (benefit), as the pilgrim benefits from performing both Umrah and Hajj in one journey and also benefits from being in a state of halal between them. The definition states that one enters ihram only for Umrah from the miqat, reciting the intention after two rak'ahs. The author then distinguishes Qiran from Tamattu': in Qiran, both Hajj and Umrah are combined in one ihram and become halal together on the 10th; in Tamattu', Umrah is performed first, then after becoming halal, one enters a new ihram for Hajj on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah. Two types of Tamattu' are outlined: (1) If one brings Hadi with them, they do not become halal after Umrah but remain in ihram until after completing Hajj and then become halal from both simultaneously. (2) If one does not bring Hadi, they become halal after Umrah and then enter ihram for Hajj separately. The proof is provided from the hadith of Ibn Umar describing the Prophet's Tamattu' in Hajjat al-Wada', where he brought Hadi and did not become halal after Umrah, while those without Hadi were instructed to perform Umrah, become halal, and then enter ihram for Hajj. This hadith also establishes the ruling that the Mutamatti' who does not bring Hadi must fast three days in Hajj (as mentioned in the previous lesson).

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): A form of Hajj where one first performs Umrah in the months of Hajj, then becomes halal, and later performs Hajj in the same journey.
قران (qiran): Combining Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram from the miqat.
احرام (ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah, marked by specific clothing and prohibitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the key difference between Qiran and Tamattu'?
A) In Qiran, Hadi is not required; in Tamattu' it is
B) In Qiran, both Hajj and Umrah are performed in one ihram; in Tamattu', they are in separate ihrams
C) In Qiran, one fasts ten days; in Tamattu', one offers sacrifice
D) In Qiran, Umrah is performed after Hajj; in Tamattu', before

Key Takeaway
Tamattu' is performing Umrah first then Hajj in separate ihrams, with two forms depending on whether one brings Hadi.

Definition and Procedure of Hajj at-Tamattu'
Defines Tamattu' and explains its procedure with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Tamattu', outline its step-by-step procedure, and identify the hadith evidence that establishes its validity and rule regarding the sacrificial animal.

Core Idea
Tamattu' means performing 'Umrah during Hajj months, becoming halal, then performing Hajj — with a sacrifice required.

Hajj can be performed in three forms: Ifrad, Qiran, and Tamattu'. The Hanafi school permits Tamattu' and considers it a recommended form, though Ifrad is superior. This passage from our text defines Tamattu' precisely and walks through the entire ritual sequence, from ihram at the miqat to shaving the head, backed by the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) during the Farewell Pilgrimage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and ruling
Read the opening lines: Tamattu' means assuming ihram only for 'Umrah from the miqat during Hajj months. The school’s ruling is that Tamattu' is mustahabb (recommended), and for those who perform it, offering a sacrificial animal (hady) becomes wajib if they have the means.
If one does not bring hady, they become halal after 'Umrah and must fast three days during Hajj and seven after returning.
2
Outline the procedure step by step
Walk through each action: (1) ihram with intention, (2) talbiyah until tawaf, (3) tawaf with raml, (4) two rak‘ahs, (5) sa‘y, (6) halq/taqsir. If the pilgrim has brought hady, they skip step 6 and remain in ihram.
The text emphasizes cutting talbiyah at the start of tawaf.
3
Locate the hadith evidence
The proof begins with ‘face’ (وجه) and quotes Ibn ‘Umar: the Prophet performed Tamattu‘ and brought his hady from Dhu al-Hulayfah. The instructions to those with and without hady are given. Also, Jabir’s hadith shows the Prophet ordered the Companions to change their intention from Hajj to ‘Umrah.
These are sahih hadith from Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Understand the implication of hady vs. no hady
The hadith clearly distinguishes: those who brought hady remain in ihram until Hajj; those without become halal after ‘Umrah and then re-enter ihram for Hajj. This is the key practical difference.
This distinction is critical for the pilgrim's actions.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
While Hanafis prefer Ifrad, Shafi‘is and Hanbalis consider Tamattu‘ superior. The validity of Tamattu‘ is agreed upon, but the preference differs.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different evaluations of the same hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل التمتع
(۱۴۰۹) التمتع هو ان يحرم بالعمرة فقط من الميقات فيقول بعد صلاة ركعتي الاحرام اللهم انى اريد العمرة فيسرها لي وتقبلها منى ( ۱۴۱۰ ) ثم يُلبّى حتى يدخل مكة فيطوف لها ويقطع التلبية باوّل طوافه (۱۴۱۱) ويرمل فيه ثم يصلّى ركعتي الطواف ثم يسعى بين الصفا والمروة بعد الوقوف على الصفا كما تقدّم سبعة اشواط ( ۱۴۱۲) ثم يحلق رأسه ويقصر اذا لم يسق الهدى .

وجه : (1) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ ان ابن عمر قال تمتع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في حجة الوداع بالعمرة الى الحج و أهدى فساق معه الهدى من ذي الحليفة و بدأ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فأهل بالعمرة ثم اهل بالحج ، فكان من الناس من أهدى فساق الهدى و منهم من لم يهد . فلما قدم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مكة قال للناس من كان منكم أهدى فانه لا يحل من شيء حرم منه حتى يقضى حجه، و من لم يكن منكم أهدى فليطف بالبيت و بالصفا و المروة و يقصر و ليحلل ثم ليهل بالحج ( بخاری شریف، باب من ساق البدن معه ص ۲۷۴، نمبر ۱۹۹۱ و مسلم شریف ، باب وجوب الدم على المتمتع وانه اذا اعدم منه لزمه صوم ثلاثۃ ایام فی الحج ص ۵۲۱، نمبر ۲۹۸۲/۱۲۲۷)

حدثنا جابر بن عبد الله قدمنا مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم و نحن نقول لبيك اللهم لبيك بالحج فامرنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فجعلناها عمرة - ( بخاری شریف، باب من لبی بالحج و سماه ص ۲۵۵، نمبر ۱۵۷۰)

عن ابن عباس عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال يلبى المعتمر حتى يستلم الحجر ۔(ابو داؤد شریف، باب متى يقطع المعتمر التلبية ص ۲۵۹، نمبر ۱۸۱۷ و ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء متى يقطع التلبية في العمرة ،ص ۱۸۵، نمبر ۹۱۹)
Chapter of Tamattu': (1409) Tamattu' is to assume ihram for 'Umrah only from the miqat, saying after praying two rak'ahs of ihram: O Allah, I intend 'Umrah, so make it easy for me and accept it from me. (1410) Then he recites talbiyah until he enters Mecca, then performs tawaf for it and cuts off the talbiyah at the beginning of his tawaf. (1411) And he does raml in it, then prays two rak'ahs of tawaf, then performs sa'y between Safa and Marwah after standing on Safa, as previously mentioned, seven circuits. (1412) Then he shaves his head or shortens his hair if he did not bring a sacrificial animal. Evidence: (1) In this hadith: Ibn 'Umar said: The Messenger of Allah performed Tamattu' in the Farewell Pilgrimage by performing 'Umrah to Hajj, and he brought the sacrificial animal with him from Dhu al-Hulayfah, and he began by pronouncing talbiyah for 'Umrah, then pronouncing talbiyah for Hajj. Among the people, some brought the sacrificial animal and others did not. When the Prophet arrived in Mecca, he said to the people: Whoever among you brought a sacrificial animal, he should not become halal from anything that was prohibited for him until he completes his Hajj. And whoever did not bring a sacrificial animal, let him perform tawaf of the House, and sa'y between Safa and Marwah, and shorten his hair, and become halal, then pronounce talbiyah for Hajj. (Bukhari, Muslim) (2) Jabir ibn 'Abdullah narrated: We arrived with the Messenger of Allah saying 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk bi al-hajj', so the Messenger of Allah ordered us and we made it 'Umrah. (Bukhari) (3) Ibn 'Abbas from the Prophet: The one performing 'Umrah continues reciting talbiyah until he touches the Black Stone. (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi)
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage is a legal ruling with proof on the definition and procedure of Hajj at-Tamattu'. The author begins by defining Tamattu' linguistically and technically. Technically, Tamattu' is when a pilgrim enters the state of ihram only for 'Umrah from the miqat during the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qi'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah), performs the 'Umrah, then becomes halal, and later on the 8th of Dhu al-Hijjah enters ihram for Hajj. The text notes that if the pilgrim brings a sacrificial animal (hady), he does not become halal after 'Umrah but remains in ihram until after completing Hajj. If he does not bring hady, he becomes halal after 'Umrah. The author then provides the specific procedure: after wearing ihram garments, one prays two rak'ahs and states the intention. Then one recites talbiyah until starting tawaf, performs tawaf with raml (quick walking with small steps) in the first three circuits, prays two rak'ahs of tawaf, then performs sa'y between Safa and Marwah seven times, and finally shaves or shortens hair. The evidence includes the famous hadith of Ibn 'Umar describing the Prophet's Tamattu' in Hajjat al-Wada', and the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet ordered the Companions to change their intention from Hajj to 'Umrah. The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, and it is the relied-upon position of the Hanafi school that Tamattu' is valid and recommended when one is not bringing a sacrificial animal from the miqat.

Key Terms
التمتع (at-tamattu'): A form of Hajj where one performs 'Umrah during Hajj months, becomes halal, then performs Hajj in the same year, bringing a sacrificial animal (hady) or fasting.
الهدي (al-hady): A sacrificial animal (camel, cow, sheep, or goat) offered in the Haram during Hajj or 'Umrah.
التلبية (at-talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited by a pilgrim in ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct ruling for a pilgrim who performs Tamattu' without bringing a sacrificial animal?
A) He must fast three days during Hajj and seven after returning.
B) He must remain in ihram until after Hajj.
C) His Tamattu' is invalid.
D) He must repeat the 'Umrah.

Key Takeaway
Tamattu' is a valid, recommended form of Hajj where one performs 'Umrah during Hajj months, becomes halal (if no hady), and then performs Hajj, with the requirement of a sacrifice or fasting.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
12 min
Rulings for the 'Umrah of Tamattu' with Their Proofs
Rules for 'Umrah in Tamattu' with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sequence of actions for the 'Umrah of Tamattu' and state the Hanafi ruling regarding when a pilgrim becomes halal based on the presence or absence of a sacrificial animal (hady).

Core Idea
The Tamattu' pilgrim with no hady becomes halal after 'Umrah; with hady, remains in ihram until Hajj is complete.

This passage from the chapter on Tamattu' details the practical steps and proofs for the 'Umrah performed as part of the Tamattu' Hajj. The rulings are derived from the Prophet's practice and multiple authentic hadith. Understanding this sequence is essential for correctly performing Tamattu' and distinguishing when the pilgrim may exit ihram after 'Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The actions of the 'Umrah in Tamattu' (talbiyah, tawaf, raml, sa'y, halq/taksir) and the status of becoming halal. The ruling level is wajib for the described actions.
The text uses imperative forms indicating obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
Each action is supported by a hadith. For example, cutting talbiyah at tawaf from Ibn 'Abbas; raml and sa'y from general practice; halq/taksir and the hady distinction from Ibn 'Umar and Jabir.
The author cites Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Bayhaqi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? For instance, the Prophet's command to those without hady to perform tawaf, sa'y, trim and become halal indicates obligation. The imperative 'ليحلل' shows wujub.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that the Tamattu' pilgrim must complete Hajj before becoming halal, regardless of hady. The Hanafis differentiate based on the presence of hady.
The ikhtilaf affects whether one can enjoy all halal things between 'Umrah and Hajj.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: a Tamattu' pilgrim without hady can have marital relations and wear sewn clothes after 'Umrah according to Hanafis, but remains in ihram according to Shafi'is until Hajj.
This difference impacts travel and daily life during the days between 'Umrah and Hajj.

فصل التمتع
صلى الله
اريد الـعــمــرة فيسرها لي وتقبلها منى ( ۱۴۱۰ ) ثم يُلبّى حتى يدخل مكة فيطوف لها ويقطع التلبية باوّل طوافه (۱۴۱۱) ويرمل فيه ثم يصلّى ركعتي الطواف ثم يسعى بين الصفا والمروة بعد الوقوف على الصفا كما تقدّم سبعة اشواط ( ۱۴۱۲) ثم يحلق رأسه ويقصر اذا لم يسق الهدى ، اور جن لوگوں نے ہدی ہانکی وہ عمرے سے حلال نہیں ہوئے ، اور جن کے پاس ہدی نہیں تھی وہ عمرے سے حلال ہوئے ۔ (۲) عمرے کے لئے لبیک کہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ حدثنا جابر بن عبد قدمنا مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم و نحن نقول لبیک اللهم لبيك بالحج فامرنا رسول الله الا الله فجعلناها عمرة - ( بخاری شریف، باب من لبی با لج وسماه ص ۲۵۵، نمبر ۱۵۷۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ لبیک کے ساتھ عمرے کی نیت کرے۔ تـــرجـمـه : (۱۴۱۰) پھر تلبیہ پڑھے یہاں تک کہ مکہ مکرمہ میں داخل ہو پھر اس کے لئے طواف کرے، اور پہلے طواف پر تلبیہ ختم کردے۔
تشریح : پھر مکہ مکرمہ آئے اور جب عمرے کا طواف شروع کرے تو اب تلبیہ پڑھنا ختم کر دے۔ وجه : (۱) لبیک کے معنی ہیں میں حاضر ہوں۔ اور وہ حاضر ہو گیا تو اب دوبارہ میں حاضر ہوں کہنا اچھا نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اب تلبیہ پڑھنا چھوڑ دے(۲) حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابن عباس عن النبي و قال يلبى المعتمر حتى يستلم الحجر ۔(ابو داؤد شریف، باب متى يقطع المعتمر التلبية ص ۲۵۹، نمبر ۱۸۱۷ر ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء متى يقطع التلبية في العمرة ،ص ۱۸۵، نمبر ۹۱۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حجر اسود کا بوسہ دے اور طواف شروع کرے تو تلبیہ پڑھنا چھوڑ دے۔ ترجمه : (۱۴۱۱) اور اس میں رمل کرے، پھر طواف کی دورکعت پڑھے، پھر پہلے بیان کئے گئے طریقے پر صفا پر وقوف کے بعد صفا و مروہ کی سعی کرے سات چکر سے۔ تشریح تاعدہ یہ ہے کہ ہر عمرے میں ایک مرتبہ رمل ہے اور ایک سعی ہے اور یہ بھی عمرہ ہے اس لئے اس میں ایک سعی سات چکر کرے اور طواف کے پہلے تین شوط میں اکثر کر چلے۔ اور طواف کے بعد طواف کے لئے دورکعت بھی پڑھے، باقی تفصیل گزرچکی ہے ترجمه : (۱۴۱۲) پھر حلق کرائے یا قصر کرائے اگر ہدی ساتھ نہ ہو۔
صلى الله
تشریح : ہدی ساتھ نہ لے گیا ہو تو عمرہ کر کے حلال ہوگا ، اس لئے احترام سے حلال ہونے کے لئے سرمنڈوائے یا قصر کرائے۔ وجه : (1) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ ان ابن عمر قال تمتع رسول الله له في حجة الوداع بالعمرة الى الحج و أهدى فساق معه الهدى من ذي الحليفة و بدأ رسول الله له فأهل بالعمرة ثم اهل بالحج ، فكان من الناس من أهدى فساق الهدى و منهم من لم يهد . فلما قدم النبي الله مكة قال للناس من كان منكم أهدى

(۱۴۱۳) وحـل لـه كل شيء من الجماع وغيره ويستمر حلالا (۱۴۱۴) وان ساق الهدى لا يتحلل فانه لا يحــل مـن شـيء حرم منه حتى يقضى حجه و من لم يكن منكم أهدى فليطف بالبيت و بالصفا و المروة و يقصر و ليحلل ثم ليهل بالحج ( بخاری شریف ، باب من ساق البدن ، معه، ص ۲۷۴، نمبر ۱۶۹ر مسلم شریف ، باب وجوب الدم على التجمع وانه اذ اعدمه از مر صوم ثلاثۃ ایام فی الحج ص ۵۲۱، نمبر ۲۹۸۲/۱۲۲۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہدی ساتھ نہ ہو تو حلق یا قصر کرا کے حلال ہو جائے ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال لما قدم النبي الا الله مكة أمر اصحابه أن يطوفوا بالبيت وبالصفا والمروة ثم يحلوا و يحلقوا أو يقصروا . (بخارى شريف، باب ) تقصير المتمتع بعد العمر ة ص ۲۷۹، نمبر (۱۷۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حلال ہو جائے۔
ترجمه : (۱۴۱۳) اب اس کے لئے جماع وغیرہ تمام چیزیں حلال ہو گئیں ، حلال ہی کی حالت میں ٹھہرا رہے۔ تشریح : اس نے بیت اللہ کا طواف کیا اور حلق یا قصر بھی کرایا اس لئے اب حلال ہو گیا ، یعنی اس کے لئے عورت حلال ہوگئی اور باقی احرام کی وجہ سے جو چیزیں حرام ہو ئیں تھیں وہ سب حلال ہو گئیں
وجه : (۱) چونکہ یہ عمرہ سے حلال ہو چکے ہیں اس لئے اب مکہ مکرمہ میں حلال ہو کر ٹھہرے رہیں (۲) حدیث میں ہے ۔حدثنی جابر بن عبد الله انه حج مع رسول الله له يوم ساق البدن معه وقد اهلوا بالحج مفردا فقال لهم اهلوا من احـرامـكـم بـطـواف البيت وبين الصفا والمروة وقصروا ثم اقيموا حلالا حتى اذا كان يوم التروية فاهلوا
.
بالحج واجعلوا التي قدمتم بها متعة (بخاری شریف، باب التمتع والقران والا فراد بالج ص۲۱۲، نمبر ۱۵۶۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عمرہ کرنے کے بعد حلال ہو کر ٹھہرے۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عورت بھی حلال ہوگئی۔ ان عبد الـلـه بـن عمر قال فذكر الحديث ... حتى قضى حجه و نحر هديه يوم النحر وافاض فطاف بالبيت ثم حل من كل شيء حرم هنه - (سن لليهقى ، باب التخلل بالطواف اذا كان قد سعی عقب طواف القدوم ، ج خامس ص ۲۳۷ نمبر ۹۶۴۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف زیارت کے بعد عورت بھی حلال ہو جائے گی اسی طرح عمرہ میں حلال ہونے کے بعد عورت بھی حلال ہو جائے گی ترجمه : (۱۴۱۴) اگر ہدی ساتھ لے گیا ہو تو عمرہ کرنے سے حلال نہیں ہوگا۔ وجه : (1) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ ان ابن عمر قال تمتع رسول الله له في حجة الوداع بالعمرة الى الحج و أهدى فساق معه الهدى من ذي الحليفة و بدأ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فأهل بالعمرة ثم اهل بالحج ، فكان من الناس من أهدى فساق الهدى و منهم من لم يهد. فلما قدم النبي الله مكة قال للناس من كان منكم أهدى فانه لا يــحــل مــن شيء حرم منه حتى يقضى حجه و من لم يكن منكم أهدى فليطف بالبيت و بالصفا و المروة ويقصر و ليحلل ثم ليهل بالحج ( بخاری شریف، باب من ساق البدن معه، ص ۲۷۴، نمبر ۱۹۹۱ار مسلم شریف ، باب
صلى الله
Chapter of Tamattu' (Performing 'Umrah before Hajj). May Allah bless him. I intend 'Umrah, so make it easy for me and accept it from me. (1410) Then he recites the talbiyah until he enters Makkah, then performs tawaf for it and stops talbiyah at the beginning of his tawaf. (1411) And he performs raml in it, then prays two rak'ahs of tawaf, then performs sa'y between Safa and Marwah after standing on Safa as previously mentioned, seven circuits. (1412) Then he shaves his head or trims if he did not bring a sacrificial animal. And those who brought a sacrificial animal do not become halal from 'Umrah, and those who did not have a sacrificial animal become halal from 'Umrah. (2) For 'Umrah he recites talbiyah. For this there is a hadith: Jabir ibn 'Abdullah narrated: We arrived with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saying 'Labbaik Allahumma labbaik' for Hajj, then the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) commanded us...so we made it 'Umrah. (Bukhari, Chapter of one who recites talbiyah for Hajj and specifies it, p.255, no.1570) This hadith indicates that he intends 'Umrah with the talbiyah. Translation: (1410) Then he recites talbiyah until he enters Makkah, then performs tawaf for it, and stops talbiyah at the first tawaf. Explanation: Then when he comes to Makkah and begins the tawaf of 'Umrah, he stops reciting talbiyah. Reason: (1) The meaning of 'labbaik' is 'I am present'. Since he is now present, saying 'I am present' again is not good. Therefore he stops reciting talbiyah. (2) There is a hadith: Ibn 'Abbas narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: The one performing 'Umrah recites talbiyah until he touches the Black Stone. (Abu Dawud, Chapter on when does the one performing 'Umrah stop talbiyah, p.259, no.1817; Tirmidhi, Chapter on when to stop talbiyah in 'Umrah, p.185, no.919) This hadith indicates that when he kisses the Black Stone and begins tawaf, he stops reciting talbiyah. Translation: (1411) And in it he performs raml, then prays two rak'ahs of tawaf, then performs sa'y between Safa and Marwah after standing on Safa as previously explained, seven circuits. Explanation: The principle is that in every 'Umrah there is one raml and one sa'y. This is also an 'Umrah, so he performs one sa'y of seven circuits and hurries in the first three circuits of tawaf. And after tawaf he prays two rak'ahs for tawaf. The rest of the details have passed. Translation: (1412) Then he shaves or trims if he did not bring a sacrificial animal. Explanation: If he did not bring a sacrificial animal, he becomes halal after performing 'Umrah. Therefore, out of respect, to become halal he shaves his head or trims. Reason: (1) In this hadith: Ibn 'Umar said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed Tamattu' in the Farewell Hajj from 'Umrah to Hajj, and he brought sacrificial animals with him from Dhul Hulaifa. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) began and raised his voice with 'Umrah, then with Hajj. Among the people were those who brought sacrificial animals and those who did not. When the Prophet (peace be upon him) arrived in Makkah, he said to the people: 'Whoever among you has brought a sacrificial animal, he should not become halal from anything that was prohibited to him until he completes his Hajj. And whoever among you has not brought a sacrificial animal, let him perform tawaf of the House and sa'y between Safa and Marwah, then trim and become halal, then raise his voice with Hajj.' (Bukhari, Chapter of one who brought sacrificial animals with him, p.274, no.169; Muslim, Chapter on the obligation of blood sacrifice for Tamattu'...) ... (1413) And everything becomes permissible for him, including intercourse and other things, and he remains in a state of halal. (1414) And if he brought a sacrificial animal, he does not become halal, for he does not become halal from anything that was prohibited to him until he completes his Hajj. And whoever among you has not brought a sacrificial animal, let him perform tawaf of the House and sa'y between Safa and Marwah, trim and become halal, then raise his voice with Hajj. (Bukhari, Chapter of one who brought sacrificial animals with him, p.274, no.169; Muslim, Chapter on the obligation of blood sacrifice...) ... Translation: (1413) Now for him everything including intercourse becomes permissible, and he remains in a state of halal. Explanation: He performed tawaf of the House and also shaved or trimmed, so now he becomes halal. That is, for him women become permissible and all other things that were prohibited due to ihram become permissible. Reason: (1) Since he has become halal from 'Umrah, he now remains in Makkah in a state of halal. (2) There is a hadith: Jabir ibn 'Abdullah narrated that he performed Hajj with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) when he brought sacrificial animals with him and they had raised their voices with Hajj individually. He said to them: 'Become halal from your ihram by performing tawaf of the House and sa'y between Safa and Marwah and trim, then remain in a state of halal until the day of Tarwiyah, then raise your voices with Hajj and make the one you came with as Tamattu'.' (Bukhari, Chapter of Tamattu', Qiran, and Ifrad, p.212, no.1568) This hadith indicates that after performing 'Umrah, they become halal and remain. (2) This hadith indicates that women also become halal. 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar narrated the hadith... until he completed his Hajj and sacrificed his animal on the day of Nahr and performed Ifada and tawaf of the House, then he became halal from everything that was prohibited to him. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter of becoming halal by tawaf if he has performed sa'y after tawaf of arrival, vol.5, p.237, no.9647) This hadith indicates that after tawaf of Ziyarah, women also become halal. Similarly, after becoming halal in 'Umrah, women also become halal. Translation: (1414) If he brought a sacrificial animal, he does not become halal by performing 'Umrah. Reason: (1) In this hadith: Ibn 'Umar said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed Tamattu' in the Farewell Hajj from 'Umrah to Hajj, and he brought sacrificial animals with him from Dhul Hulaifa. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) began and raised his voice with 'Umrah, then with Hajj. Among the people were those who brought sacrificial animals and those who did not. When the Prophet (peace be upon him) arrived in Makkah, he said to the people: 'Whoever among you has brought a sacrificial animal, he should not become halal from anything that was prohibited to him until he completes his Hajj. And whoever among you has not brought a sacrificial animal, let him perform tawaf of the House and sa'y between Safa and Marwah, trim and become halal, then raise his voice with Hajj.' (Bukhari, Chapter of one who brought sacrificial animals with him, p.274, no.1991; Muslim, Chapter...) May Allah bless him.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Tamattu' explains the rulings for someone performing 'Umrah as part of Tamattu' Hajj. The text begins with the intention for 'Umrah, then outlines the sequence: after entering ihram for 'Umrah, the pilgrim recites talbiyah until he begins tawaf in Makkah, at which point he stops (ruling 1410, with proofs from the meaning of labbaik and the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas). Next, in the tawaf he performs raml (brisk walking) in the first three circuits, then prays two rak'ahs after tawaf, then performs sa'y between Safa and Marwah (ruling 1411, with the principle that each 'Umrah has one raml and one sa'y). Then, if he did not bring a sacrificial animal (hady), he shaves his head or trims his hair to exit ihram (ruling 1412, with proof from the hadith of Ibn 'Umar about the Prophet's practice in the Farewell Hajj). After that, everything prohibited in ihram becomes permissible, including marital relations (ruling 1413, with proofs from the hadith of Jabir and the hadith of Ibn 'Umar from Bayhaqi). However, if he brought a sacrificial animal, he remains in ihram and does not become halal until after completing the Hajj and sacrificing (ruling 1414, citing the same hadith of Ibn 'Umar where the Prophet distinguishes between those with and without hady). The author uses multiple hadith from Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, and Bayhaqi to support each ruling, following the Hanafi position that the one performing Tamattu' who does not have a sacrificial animal becomes halal after 'Umrah, while the one with hady remains in ihram.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing 'Umrah during the Hajj season, then becoming halal, then performing Hajj in the same year.
هَدي (hady): Sacrificial animal brought by the pilgrim.
رمَل (raml): Brisk walking with short steps in the first three circuits of tawaf.
تلبیہ (talbiyah): Uttering 'Labbaik Allahumma labbaik...' to express presence and response to Allah's call.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the performer of Tamattu' (who did not bring a sacrificial animal) stop reciting the talbiyah?
A) Upon entering the Haram of Makkah
B) At the beginning of the first tawaf of 'Umrah
C) After completing sa'y
D) After shaving or trimming the hair

Key Takeaway
In Tamattu', the presence of a sacrificial animal (hady) determines whether the pilgrim becomes halal after 'Umrah: without hady, he becomes halal; with hady, he remains in ihram until Hajj is complete.

Mutamatti' Becomes Halal After Umrah
Ruling with proofs for the mutamatti' becoming halal after Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that the mutamatti' becomes halal after Umrah, identify the exception when a hadi is brought, and cite the hadith proofs.

Core Idea
The mutamatti' who has not brought a hadi becomes fully halal after Umrah, including marital relations.

In this passage, the author presents the rule that the mutamatti' (one performing tamattu' Hajj) becomes halal after completing his Umrah, with the key exception of those who brought a hadi. The proofs from the Sunnah are cited to establish this permissibility, clarifying that the halal status includes all prohibitions of ihram, such as marital relations, until assuming ihram for Hajj on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the mutamatti' completing his Umrah. The ruling is that he becomes halal, meaning everything prohibited in ihram becomes permissible.
This is the default ruling.
2
Note the exception regarding hadi
If the pilgrim brought a hadi (sacrificial animal), he does not become halal until he completes his Hajj. This exception is explicitly stated in the text.
The hadi is driven with the pilgrim.
3
Trace the hadith proof
The author quotes the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded those without hadi to perform tawaf, sa'i, and halq or taqsir, and then become halal. This establishes the procedure.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Understand the fiqh implication
The halal status includes all aspects: wearing sewn clothes, using perfume, shaving, and marital relations. This is a release from the restrictions of ihram.
The text explicitly mentions 'جماع وغيره'.

Chapter on Tamattu'. (1413) And everything becomes permissible for him, including intercourse and other things, and he remains in a state of halal. (2) Also in this hadith: From Ibn Abbas, he said: When the Prophet (peace be upon him) came to Mecca, he commanded his companions to perform tawaf of the House, and between Safa and Marwa, then become halal, and shave or shorten. Explanation: He performed tawaf of the House of Allah and also performed halq or taqsir, therefore he is now halal, meaning his wife becomes permissible for him and all other things that were prohibited due to ihram become permissible. Proof: (1) Since they have become halal from Umrah, they now remain in Mecca as halal. (2) There is a hadith: Jabir ibn Abdullah narrated that he performed Hajj with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) while he was driving his sacrificial animals and they had assumed ihram for Hajj alone, so he said to them: 'Release yourselves from your ihram with tawaf of the House and between Safa and Marwa and shorten (your hair), then remain in a state of halal until Yawm al-Tarwiyah, then assume ihram for Hajj and make the one you entered with a tamattu'.' (Bukhari, chapter on tamattu', qiran, and ifrad, p. 212, no. 1568) This hadith indicates that after performing Umrah they became halal and remained. (2) Another hadith states that the wife also becomes halal. Abdullah ibn Umar said... until he completed his Hajj and sacrificed his hadi on Yawm al-Nahr, and performed ifada, and performed tawaf of the House, then became halal from everything that was prohibited to him. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on becoming halal by tawaf when one has run after the Tawaf of Arrival, vol. 5, p. 237, no. 9647) This hadith shows that after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, the wife becomes halal, and similarly after becoming halal in Umrah, the wife becomes halal.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs for the rule that the mutamatti' (one performing tamattu' Hajj) becomes halal after completing his Umrah. The Arabic matn states: 'And everything becomes permissible for him, including intercourse and other things, and he remains in a state of halal.' The author then immediately gives the exception: if he brought a hadi (sacrificial animal), he does not become halal until after Hajj. This is supported by the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Jabir which show that the Prophet commanded the companions who did not bring a hadi to perform tawaf, sa'i, and halq/taqsir, and then become halal. The proof (wajh) explains that after Umrah they are halal and may stay in Mecca in that state. A second hadith from Jabir narrates that the Prophet told those who did not bring a hadi to release themselves from ihram and remain halal until Yawm al-Tarwiyah. Then a third hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar shows that even intercourse becomes permissible after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, and analogically after Umrah in tamattu'. The explanation (tashrih) clarifies that the halal status includes everything forbidden during ihram, including marital relations. This is a standard Hanafi ruling, based on the Quran (2:196) and Sunnah, and it is the established position in the school. Note that this ruling applies only to those who do not bring a hadi; if one brings a hadi, he remains in ihram until after Hajj (as will be discussed in the next lesson).

Key Terms
متعة (tamattu'): A type of Hajj where one first performs Umrah during the Hajj season, becomes halal, then assumes ihram for Hajj on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah.
هدي (hadi): A sacrificial animal brought by the pilgrim, especially in tamattu' and qiran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Marital relations become permissible immediately after Umrah
C) Marital relations are never permitted in Hajj
D) Marital relations depend on whether a hadi is brought

Key Takeaway
The mutamatti' becomes fully halal after completing his Umrah rites unless he has brought a hadi, in which case he remains in ihram until after Hajj.

Exception: One Who Brings a Hadi Does Not Become Halal
Ruling that if the mutamatti' brought a hadi, he remains in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a mutamatti' who brings a hadi and explain the proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
A mutamatti' who brings a hadi must remain in ihram until Hajj is complete — the hadi itself imposes this restriction.

This lesson examines a crucial exception in the rules of tamattu'. While the usual mutamatti' becomes halal after Umrah, the Prophet's practice shows that bringing a sacrificial animal (hadi) changes the ruling. We will analyze the hadith evidence and its legal implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the act being ruled upon (mutamatti' who brings a hadi) and the hukm level (wajib to remain in ihram).
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Ibn Umar describing the Prophet's Farewell Hajj is the primary proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's explicit words 'la yahillu' (he will not become halal) indicate a prohibition of becoming halal until Hajj is completed.
This is a direct command from the Prophet, making it binding.
4
Note the practical consequence
The mutamatti' with a hadi cannot perform halq or taqsir after Umrah and remains in full ihram restrictions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۴۱۴) اگر ہدی ساتھ لے گیا ہو تو عمرہ کرنے سے حلال نہیں ہوگا۔ وجه : (1) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ ان ابن عمر قال تمتع رسول الله له في حجة الوداع بالعمرة الى الحج و أهدى فساق معه الهدى من ذي الحليفة و بدأ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فأهل بالعمرة ثم اهل بالحج ، فكان من الناس من أهدى فساق الهدى و منهم من لم يهد. فلما قدم النبي الله مكة قال للناس من كان منكم أهدى فانه لا يــحــل مــن شيء حرم منه حتى يقضى حجه و من لم يكن منكم أهدى فليطف بالبيت و بالصفا و المروة ويقصر و ليحلل ثم ليهل بالحج ( بخاری شریف، باب من ساق البدن معه، ص ۲۷۴، نمبر ۱۹۹۱ار مسلم شریف ، باب وجوب الدم على التمتع وانه اذاعد مرالزمر صوم ثلاثۃ ایام فی الجی ص ۵۲۱ نمبر ۲۹۸۲/۱۲۲۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہدی ساتھ ہو تو حلال نہیں ہوگا، ایک ہی مرتبہ حج کر کے حلال ہوگا۔
Translation: (1414) If he brought a hadi, he will not become halal from Umrah. Proof: (1) In this hadith: Ibn Umar said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed tamattu' in his Farewell Pilgrimage with Umrah to Hajj, and he brought a hadi and drove it with him from Dhul Hulaifa. He began by assuming ihram for Umrah, then assumed ihram for Hajj. Among the people, some brought a hadi and drove it, and some did not. When the Prophet (peace be upon him) came to Mecca, he said to the people: 'Whoever among you brought a hadi, he will not become halal from anything that was prohibited until he completes his Hajj. And whoever among you did not bring a hadi, let him perform tawaf of the House, and between Safa and Marwa, and shorten (his hair), and become halal, then later assume ihram for Hajj.' (Bukhari, chapter on one who drives sacrificial animals, p. 274, no. 1691; Muslim, chapter on the obligation of blood sacrifice for tamattu' and that if he cannot find, then fasting three days during Hajj, p. 521, no. 2982/1227) This hadith states that if the hadi is with him, he will not become halal, he will become halal only after completing Hajj once.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the exception to the general rule: if the mutamatti' brings a hadi (sacrificial animal), he does not become halal after Umrah. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar describing the Prophet's Farewell Pilgrimage. In this hadith, the Prophet distinguished between those who brought a hadi and those who did not. For those with a hadi, they remain in ihram until after completing Hajj. This is a clear textual evidence (dalil naqli) supporting the Hanafi position. The tashrih (explanation) is implicit: the mutamatti' who brings a hadi must remain in ihram and cannot perform halq/taqsir after Umrah. Consequently, he does not become halal for the things prohibited in ihram (such as marital relations, wearing stitched clothes, etc.) until after completing all rituals of Hajj. This ruling is based on the specific action of the Prophet and his command. In the Hanafi school, this is the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
هدي (hadi): A sacrificial animal brought by the pilgrim, especially in tamattu' and qiran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) He does not become halal until after completing Hajj
C) He becomes halal only after sacrificing the hadi
D) He must stay in ihram for the entire lifetime

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's command in the hadith of Ibn Umar makes it clear: a mutamatti' with a hadi does not become halal until completing Hajj.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Procedure on Yawm al-Tarwiyah: Entering Ihram from the Haram
Ruling with proof on when and where the mutamatti' enters ihram for Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the location and timing for the mutamatti' to assume ihram for Hajj and identify the proofs from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
The mutamatti' becomes like a Makkan, so his miqat for Hajj is from within the Haram.

This lesson focuses on a key procedural rule for those performing tamattu' Hajj. After completing Umrah and becoming halal, the mutamatti' must re-enter ihram for Hajj on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm al-Tarwiyah) from a location within the Haram, preferably the Masjid al-Haram or al-Abtah. The ruling is based on clear prophetic traditions and a qiyas (analogy) that the mutamatti' is like a resident of Mecca.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is assuming ihram for Hajj on Yawm al-Tarwiyah. The Hanafi school rules it as wajib (required) for the mutamatti'.
Wajib here means obligatory; omission without valid reason is sinful.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadiths are cited: the hadith of Ibn Abbas in Bukhari about miqats, and the hadith of Jabir in Muslim about assuming ihram from al-Abtah.
These ahadith are the primary textual evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith of Ibn Abbas establishes that Makkans assume ihram from Mecca. The mutamatti', after becoming halal and staying in Mecca, is analogous to a Makkan. The hadith of Jabir provides direct precedent: the companions assumed ihram from al-Abtah (within Mecca).
The qiyas is based on the illa (effective cause) of being a resident of the Haram.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools may allow assuming ihram from outside the Haram. The Hanafi position is that the miqat must be from within the Haram.
This ikhtilaf stems from differing views on whether the mutamatti' truly becomes like a Makkan.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is clear: the mutamatti' assumes ihram from the Haram on Yawm al-Tarwiyah. This is supported by strong textual evidence and qiyas.
The Hanafi school gives weight to the manifest practice of the companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : ( ۱۴۱۵) جب یوم ترویه ( ۸ / تاریخ) آئے تو حرم سے حج کا احرام باندھے اور منی کی طرف نکلے۔ تشریح تمتع کرنے والا عمرہ کر کے حلال ہوا تھا، اب وہ ۸ رذی الحجہ کو حرم سے حج کا احرام باندھے، اور پھر وہ منی کی طرف جائے وجه : (۱) مسجد حرام سے یا حرم سے احرام باندھنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال وقت رسول الله الله لاهل المدينة ذا الحليفة ولاهل الشام الجحفة ولاهل نجد قرن المنازل ولاهل اليمن يلملم فهن لهن ولمن اتي عليهن من غير اهلهن لمن كان يريد الحج والعمرة فمن كان دونهن فمهله من اهله و کذلک حتی اهل مكة يهلون منها ( بخاری شریف، باب محل اهل الشام، ص ۱۲۴۸، نمبر ۱۵۲۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اہل مکہ مکہ سے احرام باندھیں گے اور متمتع احرام کھولنے کے بعد مکی کی طرح ہو گئے اس لئے وہ بھی مکہ سے احرام باندھیں گے(۲) حدیث میں ہے۔عن جابر بن عبد الله قال امرنا النبي الله لما احللنا ان نحرم اذا توجهنا الى منى قال فاهللنا من الابطح (مسلم شریف ، باب بیان وجوه الاحرام وانه يجوز افراد الج والتمتع والقران الخ ص ۳۹۲ نمبر ۲۹۴۱/۱۲۱۴) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ صحابہ کرام نے حجتہ الوداع میں ابطح جو مکہ مکرمہ میں ایک جگہ ہے وہاں سے حج کا احرام باندھا۔
Translation: (1415) When Yawm al-Tarwiyah (8th [of Dhul Hijjah]) comes, he should assume ihram for Hajj from the Haram and exit towards Mina. Explanation: The mutamatti' had become halal after Umrah. Now on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah, he should assume ihram for Hajj from the Haram, and then go towards Mina. Proof: (1) The evidence for assuming ihram from the Masjid al-Haram or the Haram is this hadith: Ibn Abbas said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) set the miqat for the people of Madinah as Dhul Hulaifa, for the people of Syria as Juhfah, for the people of Najd as Qarn al-Manazil, for the people of Yemen as Yalamlam. These are for them and for those who come from outside their regions intending Hajj or Umrah. And whoever is within these boundaries, his miqat is from his own home, and likewise the people of Mecca assume ihram from it. (Bukhari, chapter on the miqat of the people of Syria, p. 1248, no. 1526) From this hadith it is understood that the people of Mecca assume ihram from Mecca, and the mutamatti', after releasing ihram, becomes like a Makkan, so he too should assume ihram from Mecca. (2) In another hadith: Jabir ibn Abdullah said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded us when we had become halal to assume ihram when we head towards Mina, so we assumed ihram from al-Abtah. (Muslim, chapter on the explanation of the types of ihram and permissibility of ifrad, tamattu', and qiran, p. 392, no. 2941/1214) From this hadith we also learn that the companions at the Farewell Pilgrimage assumed ihram for Hajj from al-Abtah, which is a place in Mecca.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the procedure on Yawm al-Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah). The mutamatti', having become halal after Umrah, must now re-enter ihram for Hajj from within the Haram (preferably from the Masjid al-Haram or al-Abtah) and then go to Mina. The proof (wajh) includes two hadiths: one from Ibn Abbas establishing that the miqat for Makkans is Mecca itself, and since the mutamatti' is now like a Makkan (having been released from ihram and residing in Mecca), his miqat is also from Mecca. The second hadith from Jabir explicitly narrates that the companions assumed ihram from al-Abtah when proceeding to Mina. The tashrih (explanation) clarifies the sequence: after Umrah, the pilgrim stays halal until Yawm al-Tarwiyah, then re-enters ihram for Hajj. This is a standard Hanafi ruling and is part of the tamattu' procedure.

Key Terms
یوم الترویة (Yawm al-Tarwiyah): The 8th of Dhul Hijjah, the day when pilgrims proceed to Mina and those doing tamattu' re-enter ihram for Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
From where should the mutamatti' assume ihram for Hajj on Yawm al-Tarwiyah?
A) From the miqat of his original location
B) From within the Haram (e.g., Masjid al-Haram or al-Abtah)
C) From the place where he performed Umrah
D) From Mina itself

Key Takeaway
The mutamatti' must assume ihram for Hajj from within the Haram on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah, following the practice of the companions and qiyas to the people of Mecca.

Obligation of Sacrifice After Throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah
Ruling with proof on hadi obligation for mutamatti'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of hadi for the mutamatti' and identify the required animal (sheep or seventh of cow/camel) along with its proof from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
The mutamatti' must sacrifice a sheep or a seventh of a cow/camel after throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah.

After completing the major rites of Hajj, the mutamatti'—one who performs Umrah and Hajj in the same journey—is required to offer a thank offering (hadi). This lesson examines the ruling, its timing, and the specific animals prescribed, based on the Quranic command and the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (sacrifice after Jamrat al-Aqabah) and the level of obligation (wajib).
The ruling is specifically for the mutamatti' pilgrim.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the Quranic verse (2:196) that commands the hadi for tamattu' and note the alternative of fasting.
The verse is cited as the main proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the Quranic phrase 'fama' istaysara min al-hadi' establishes the obligation of a sacrifice that is easy, and the conditional structure indicates wujub.
The word 'faman' indicates a conditional obligation in Hanafi usul.
4
Confirm the type of animal from Sunnah
Refer to the hadith of Jabir (ra) showing that a camel or cow can be shared by seven, so a seventh is sufficient.
This hadith supplies the detail not explicit in the Quran.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position: sacrifice a sheep or a seventh of a cow/camel; if unable, fast three days during Hajj and seven after returning home.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۴۱۶) پس جب یوم النحر [۰ ارذی الحجہ کو جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کر چکے تو اس پر ایک بکری یا بد نہ کا ساتواں حصہ قربانی کرنا لازم ہے۔ تشريح : جب دسویں ذی الحجہ کو جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کرے تو حج بھی پورا ہو گیا، اور چونکہ ایک سفر میں عمرہ اور حج دونوں کئے ہیں اس لئے شکرانہ کے طور پر ایک بکری دے، یا بڑے جانور کا ساتواں حصہ قربانی کرے۔ وجه : (۱) آیت یہ ہے فمن تمتع بالعمرة الى الحج فما استيسر من الهدى فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلثة ايام في الحج و سبعة اذا رجعتم تلك عشرة كاملة ذلك لمن لم يكن اهله حاضرى المسجد الحرام ( آیت ١٩٦ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ جس نے تمتع کیا اس پر ہدی لازم ہے اور ہدی نہ دے سکا تو تین روزے حج سے پہلے رکھے اور سات روزے حج سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد رکھے ۔ (۲) اور گائے یا اونٹ کے ساتویں حصے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله قال نحرنا مع رسول الله الا الله عام الحديبية البدنة عن سبعة والبقرة عن سبعة - (مسلم شريف، باب جواز الاشتراك فى الهدى واجزاء البدنة والبقرة كل واحد منهما عن سبعة، ص ۵۵۳ نمبر ۱۳۱۸/ ۳۱۸۵ را بو داؤد شریف، باب
Translation: (1416) Then when he has thrown the Jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr (10th of Dhul Hijjah), upon him is obligated to slaughter a sheep or a seventh of a sacrificial camel (badana). Explanation: When he throws the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the Hajj is completed. And because he performed both Umrah and Hajj in one journey, as a thank offering he gives a sheep, or sacrifices a seventh of a large animal. Proof: (1) The verse: 'Whoever performs tamattu' of Umrah to Hajj, then [sacrifice] whatever is easy of the hadi. But whoever cannot find [or afford], then fast three days during Hajj and seven when you return, that is ten complete.' (Surah al-Baqarah, verse 196) This verse states that for the mutamatti', a hadi is obligatory, and if he cannot offer it, then three fasts before Hajj and seven after. (2) The evidence for the seventh of a cow or camel is this hadith: Jabir ibn Abdullah said: We sacrificed with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in the year of Hudaybiyyah, a camel (badana) for seven [persons] and a cow for seven. (Muslim, chapter on permissibility of sharing in hadi and sufficiency of a camel and a cow each for seven, p. 553, no. 1318/3185; also Abu Dawud)
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the obligation of a sacrifice (hadi) upon the mutamatti'. After throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), he must slaughter a sheep or a seventh share of a cow or camel. The tashrih (explanation) clarifies that this is a thank offering for combining Umrah and Hajj in one journey. The first proof (wajh) is the Quranic verse (2:196) which directly commands the hadi for tamattu', and provides the alternative of fasting. The second proof is the hadith from Jabir showing that a camel or cow suffices for seven persons, thus a seventh of one is acceptable. This ruling is a wajib obligation in the Hanafi school; if one cannot afford it, fasting is required as specified. The proof is clear and the practice is based on the Sunnah of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Key Terms
هدي (hadi): A sacrificial animal offered as a thank offering for tamattu' Hajj.
بدنة (badana): A camel or cow offered as sacrifice; a seventh of it suffices for one person in hadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A full camel
B) A sheep or one-seventh of a cow or camel
C) A full cow
D) No sacrifice is required

Key Takeaway
The mutamatti' must sacrifice a sheep or a seventh of a cow/camel after throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah; if unable, fasting is required.

The Mutamatti's Ihram for Hajj: Timing and Location
Ruling with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exact timing and location for a mutamatti to enter ihram for Hajj according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The mutamatti enters ihram for Hajj from the Haram on the Day of Tarwiyah.

This lesson clarifies the specific requirement for a mutamatti: after completing Umrah and becoming halal, he must enter a new ihram for Hajj on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah from within the Haram. This ruling is supported by Prophetic practice and is a wajib condition for the validity of his Hajj according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is the mutamatti's entry into ihram for Hajj after completing Umrah.
The mutamatti is one who performs Umrah and then Hajj in the same journey.
2
Determine the time
The time is the Day of Tarwiyah, i.e., the 8th day of Dhul Hijjah.
This is the day when pilgrims depart to Mina.
3
Determine the location
The location is from within the Haram (the sacred precincts of Mecca). The text mentions al-Abtah as a specific place.
The entire Haram is valid; al-Abtah is just an example.
4
Note the consequence of violation
If the mutamatti enters ihram for Hajj from outside the Haram, the Hajj is valid but he has left a wajib and must sacrifice a dam.
This shows the ruling is wajib, not a condition of validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل التمتع من عمرته (١٤١٥) فإذا جاء يوم التروية يحرم بالحج من الحرم ويخرج إلى منى. الوجه: (١) حديث: عن ابن عباس قال وقت رسول الله لأهل المدينة ذا الحليفة ولأهل الشام الجحفة ولأهل نجد قرن المنازل ولأهل اليمن يلملم فهن لهن ولمن أتى عليهن من غير أهلهن لمن كان يريد الحج والعمرة فمن كان دونهن فمهله من أهله وكذلك حتى أهل مكة يهلون منها. (٢) وعن جابر بن عبد الله قال أمرنا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لما أحللنا أن نحرم إذا توجهنا إلى منى قال فأهللنا من الأبطح.
Chapter on Tamattu'. From his Umrah (1415): When the day of Tarwiyah comes, he enters ihram for Hajj from the Haram and goes out to Mina. Evidence: (1) Hadith: Ibn Abbas said: 'The Messenger of Allah appointed for the people of Medina Dhul-Hulayfah, for the people of Syria Juhfah, for the people of Najd Qarn al-Manazil, and for the people of Yemen Yalamlam; these are for them and for anyone who comes upon them from other than their people, for those who intend Hajj and Umrah. Whoever is within these boundaries, his miqat is from his dwelling, and likewise the people of Makkah start their ihram from there.' (2) And from Jabir ibn Abdullah: 'The Prophet, peace be upon him, commanded us when we had become halal to enter ihram when we set out for Mina, so we began the talbiyah from al-Abtah.'
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the chapter on Tamattu'. It states that a mutamatti (one who performs Umrah and then Hajj in the same journey) should, after completing his Umrah and becoming halal, enter ihram for Hajj on the day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah) from the Haram (Mecca) and proceed to Mina. The author provides two hadith proofs. The first, from Ibn Abbas, establishes the miqat boundaries for various regions and affirms that the people of Makkah enter ihram from Makkah itself—since the mutamatti is now residing in Makkah after Umrah, he takes the same rule. The second, from Jabir, directly shows that the Companions entered ihram from al-Abtah (a place in Makkah) when heading to Mina for Hajj. Thus, the ruling is clear: the mutamatti must begin his Hajj ihram from within the Haram, specifically from Makkah.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): A type of Hajj where one performs Umrah first, then after breaking ihram, enters ihram for Hajj in the same year.
يوم التروية (yawm al-tarwiyah): The 8th day of Dhul Hijjah, when pilgrims go to Mina and prepare for the standing at Arafah.
الأبطح (al-Abtah): A place in Makkah between the mountains, near the Masjid al-Haram, where the Prophet camped during the Farewell Pilgrimage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Before stoning the Jamrat al-Aqabah.

Key Takeaway
The mutamatti must enter ihram for Hajj on the Day of Tarwiyah from within the Haram; this is a wajib, not a rukn.

Proofs for the Mutamatti's Ihram from the Haram
Ruling with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Jabir support the Hanafi ruling on the mutamatti's ihram.

Core Idea
The hadith establish that people of Makkah start ihram from Makkah; the mutamatti is treated like a Makkan.

This lesson delves into the two hadith proofs provided in the text. The first from Ibn Abbas defines the miqat boundaries and concludes that residents of Makkah begin ihram from Makkah. The second from Jabir directly records the Prophet commanding the Companions to enter ihram from al-Abtah when leaving for Mina. The Hanafi school uses these to derive the obligation for the mutamatti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first hadith (Ibn Abbas)
The hadith lists miqats for various regions and ends with 'and likewise the people of Makkah start their ihram from there (Makkah).'
This establishes a general principle: the miqat for a person is his place of residence if he is within the miqat boundaries.
2
Extract the principle
The principle: residents of Makkah begin ihram from Makkah.
The mutamatti, after Umrah, becomes halal and resides in Makkah for the days before Hajj.
3
Apply to mutamatti
By analogy (qiyas), the mutamatti is like a resident of Makkah, so his miqat is also Makkah.
This is strengthened by the fact that the mutamatti is not traveling from outside; he is already in Makkah.
4
Identify the second hadith (Jabir)
Jabir reports: 'The Prophet commanded us when we had become halal (after Umrah) to enter ihram when we set out for Mina, so we began the talbiyah from al-Abtah.'
The command (amr) indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
5
Determine the juridical indication
The command 'an nahrima' (that we enter ihram) shows the action is wajib. The location 'from al-Abtah' is a specific place in the Haram.
Thus, the mutamatti must enter ihram from the Haram.

Fasting as Substitute for Dam for the Mutamatti
Ruling on fasting as substitute for dam when a mutamatti cannot afford a sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fasting in place of the dam for a mutamatti and explain the evidence from Quran 2:196.

Core Idea
Fasting 3+7 days replaces the sacrifice when a mutamatti cannot afford it.

In this lesson, we examine the Quranic alternative for the mutamatti who cannot find a sacrificial animal. The Hanafi school derives a clear ruling from Surah al-Baqarah 2:196, specifying ten days of fasting split into three before the 10th of Dhul Hijjah and seven after returning. Understanding this substitution is essential for completing the Hajj obligation correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is fasting as a substitute for the dam (sacrifice) when a mutamatti cannot afford it. The ruling is wajib (obligatory) as a concession.
The ruling applies to both mutamatti and qarin.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quran 2:196, which states: 'فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلاثة أيام في الحج وسبعة إذا رجعتم تلك عشرة كاملة'.
The ayah is directly quoted in the source.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'صيام' indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul. The conditional 'فمن لم يجد' establishes that inability to offer an animal triggers the fasting alternative.
The ayah is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalalah, so the ruling is definitive.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on timing
While all schools agree on the fasting alternative, there are differences on details. Hanafis hold that the three days must be completed before the day of Nahr and need not be consecutive; the seven days can be after returning home.
Some schools require the three days to be consecutive.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position
The Hanafi position is based on the literal reading of the ayah ('during Hajj' means before Nahr) and the practice of the Companions. The mufta bihi is to fast three days before the 10th and seven days after returning.
This is the relied-upon position in the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١٤١٧) فإن لم يجد صام ثلاثة أيام قبل مجيء يوم النحر وسبعة إذا رجع كالقارن. الوجه: الآية السابقة: فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلاثة أيام في الحج وسبعة إذا رجعتم تلك عشرة كاملة.
(1417): And if he does not find (a sacrificial animal), he fasts three days before the coming of the day of Nahr and seven days when he returns, like the Qarin. Evidence: The previous ayah: 'And whoever cannot find (an offering), then a fast of three days during Hajj and seven when you return, that is ten complete.'
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This ruling provides the alternative for a mutamatti who cannot afford or find a sacrificial animal (hady). In place of the dam, he must fast ten days: three days before the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), i.e., during the Hajj season, and seven days after he returns home or completes the Hajj. The text notes this is the same as the rule for a Qarin (one who does Hajj and Umrah together). The proof is Quran 2:196 which explicitly mentions the fasting alternative. The three fasts must be completed before the day of Nahr; they can be done on the 7th, 8th, and 9th or any three days before the 10th. The seven fasts can be done after the Hajj, either in Makkah or after returning home, as per the ayah 'when you return'.

Key Terms
قارن (qarin): One who performs Hajj and Umrah together in a single ihram.
صيام (siyam): Fasting as a substitute for the dam when unable to sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many days must a mutamatti fast if he cannot afford a sacrifice?
A) 10 days: 3 before the day of Nahr and 7 after returning.
B) 7 days: all after returning home.
C) 3 days: all during Hajj.
D) 10 days: all while in Makkah after Hajj.

Key Takeaway
A mutamatti who cannot sacrifice must fast three days before the 10th of Dhul Hijjah and seven days after returning, based on Quran 2:196.

Missed Three-Day Fast Before Nahr: Consequence
Ruling on missed three-day fast before Nahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a mutamatti misses the three-day fast before the day of Nahr and identify the evidence from the Salaf.

Core Idea
Missing the three-day fast before Day of Nahr makes dam wajib; neither fasting nor charity suffices.

The mutamatti (one performing tamattu' Hajj) is obligated to fast three days during Hajj. But what if these days pass without fasting? This lesson examines the decisive Hanafi ruling: once the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) arrives without the fast, sacrifice becomes mandatory and no substitute is accepted. We will trace the evidence from the early authorities that establish this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the act
The ruling applies to a mutamatti who failed to fast the three days intended to be observed during the Hajj season, before the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah).
The three-day fast is an obligatory (wajib) option for those who cannot afford a sacrifice, but if missed before the deadline, the option lapses.
2
Recognize the consequence of missing the deadline
Once the day of Nahr arrives without completing the three fasts, the original obligation of a sacrifice (dam) becomes fixed (ta'ayyana).
The term 'ta'ayyana' indicates that the alternative is no longer valid.
3
Confirm that substitutes are invalid
The text explicitly states that neither fasting nor charity will take the place of the required sacrifice.
This rules out the idea of making up the fast later or giving sadaqah instead.
4
Examine the evidence from the Salaf
The ruling is supported by the sayings of Ibn Abbas and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, which are treated as authoritative precedents in the Hanafi school.
Ibn Abbas said: 'If the mutamatti does not fast, then he must offer blood.' Ibrahim said: 'There is no option but to offer blood, even if he sells his garment.'
5
Differentiate from other schools (optional)
Unlike the Shafi'i school, which permits making up the missed fast after Hajj, the Hanafi view is categorical: sacrifice is the only valid option once the deadline passes.
This highlights the strictness of the Hanafi position regarding fixed alternatives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١٤١٨) فإن لم يصم الثلاثة حتى جاء يوم النحر تعين عليه ذبح شاة ولا يجزئه صوم ولا صدقة. الوجه: (١) قول ابن عباس: إذا لم يصم المتمتع فعليه الدم. (٢) قول إبراهيم النخعي: لا بد من دم ولو يبيع ثوبه. (رواه ابن أبي شيبة)
(1418): And if he did not fast the three (days) until the day of Nahr came, then sacrificing a sheep becomes obligatory upon him, and neither fasting nor charity will suffice. Evidence: (1) Saying of Ibn Abbas: 'If the mutamatti does not fast, then he must offer blood.' (2) Saying of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: 'There is no option but to offer blood, even if he sells his garment.'
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This final ruling addresses the case where the mutamatti fails to fast the three days before the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). In this situation, the option of fasting is no longer available; the original obligation of a sacrifice (dam) becomes fixed and cannot be replaced by fasting or charity (sadaqah). The author supports this with two athar (sayings of the Salaf). Ibn Abbas, the great Companion and cousin of the Prophet, explicitly states that if the mutamatti does not fast, he owes the blood sacrifice. Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, a prominent Tabi'i, emphasizes the necessity even to the extent of selling one's garment to obtain the animal. This shows the seriousness of missing the fast. Thus, the mufta bihi is that once the day of Nahr arrives without completing the three fasts, the dam is wajib and no substitute is accepted.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial offering (sheep) required when the mutamatti fails to fast before the day of Nahr.
تعين (ta'ayyana): Becomes fixed and obligatory; the alternative (fasting) is no longer valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a mutamatti do if he fails to fast the three days before the day of Nahr?
A) He may fast the three days after the day of Nahr.
B) He must sacrifice a sheep; fasting or charity will not be accepted.
C) He can give sadaqah instead of fasting or sacrificing.
D) He is excused and no action is required.

Key Takeaway
Once the day of Nahr arrives without completing the three-day fast, the mutamatti's obligation becomes fixed as a sheep sacrifice; no other compensation is valid.
