Basic Ruling: Fasting as Substitute for the Hady (Tamattu')
Basic ruling for tamattu' without hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a mutamatti' who cannot afford a hady must fast three days before the Day of Nahr and seven days after returning, and identify the key conditions.

Core Idea
Fasting substitutes for the hady when unaffordable; timing is strict: three before Nahr, seven after return.

In this lesson, we examine the first ruling from the Tamattu' section: when a mutamatti' pilgrim cannot find or afford a sacrificial animal (hady), the obligation shifts to fasting. The passage provides precise timing and conditions, drawing on Quranic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tamattu' without a hady. The ruling is that fasting becomes wajib (obligatory) as a substitute.
This substitution is based on Quran 2:196.
2
Determine the timing
Three days must be completed before the Day of Nahr (10th Dhu al-Hijjah). Seven days are fasted after returning from Hajj (or after the days of tashriq).
The fast may be observed in Makkah or after returning home.
3
Note the analogy to the qarin
The ruling is the same for a qarin pilgrim (who performs Hajj and 'Umrah together).
This analogy is explicit in the text.
4
Understand the evidence
The author refers to a previous verse (Quran 2:196) which commands fasting for those who cannot afford a hady in tamattu'.
No explicit citation is given here; the verse is assumed known.

تشریح : اگر دسویں ذی الحجہ سے پہلے پہلے روزہ نہ رکھ سکا تو اب ذبح کرنا ہی لازم ہوگا، صدقہ کرنا اور روزہ رکھنا کافی نہیں ہے۔ وجه : (۱) قول صحابی میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال اذا لم يصم المتمتع فعليه الدم (۲) قول تابعی میں ہے ۔وعن ابراهيم قال لا بد من دم ولو يبيع ثوبه - مصنف ابن ابی هیپه ۴۳ فی استمتع اذا فاته الصوم، ج ثالث ، ص ۱۵۰، نمبر ۷/۱۲۹۸۳ ۱۲۹۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ دسویں ذی الحجہ تک روزے نہ رکھ سکا تو اس پر اب دم ہی لازم ہے۔
Section on Tamattu'. (1417) If he does not find [a sacrificial animal], he fasts three days before the arrival of the Day of Nahr and seven when he returns, like the qarin. (1418) If he did not fast the three until the Day of Nahr came, slaughtering a sheep becomes obligatory upon him, and neither fasting nor charity suffices for him. The cow and the camel are sufficient for how many? Page 409, number 2809) From this hadith it is understood that a cow and a camel are sufficient on behalf of seven people. Translation: (1417) And if he does not find a hady, then he fasts three days before the tenth of Dhu al-Hijjah comes, and seven days when he returns, like the qarin. Explanation: If the one performing tamattu' does not have a hady, then before the tenth of Dhu al-Hijjah he fasts three days, and after the days of tashriq he fasts seven days, whether he fasts in Makkah al-Mukarramah or after returning home. The above verse has already passed for this. Translation: (1418) And if he did not fast the three days until the tenth of Dhu al-Hijjah came, then slaughtering a goat becomes determined upon him, and fasting will not suffice, nor will charity suffice. Explanation: If he could not fast before the tenth of Dhu al-Hijjah, then now slaughtering is necessary, and giving charity and fasting are not sufficient. Evidence: (1) It is in the saying of a companion: From Ibn Abbas, he said: If the mutamatti' does not fast, then blood is due from him. (2) It is in the saying of a tabi'i: And from Ibrahim, he said: Blood is unavoidable even if he sells his garment. - Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, section on mutamatti' when fasting eludes him, volume 3, page 150, number 12983/12998. From this athar it is understood that if he could not fast until the tenth of Dhu al-Hijjah, then blood is necessary upon him.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings from the section on Tamattu' in Hajj. The author first states the basic ruling (1417): if a mutamatti' cannot afford a sacrificial animal (hady), he must fast three days before the Day of Nahr (10th Dhu al-Hijjah) and seven days after returning from Hajj (or after the days of Tashriq), analogous to a qarin. The second ruling (1418) addresses the case where he fails to fast the three days before the Day of Nahr; in that case, fasting or charity no longer suffice, and slaughtering a sheep becomes compulsory. The author then provides evidence from the sayings of Ibn Abbas (a companion) and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (a tabi'i) to reinforce that slaughtering is mandatory if the fast is missed. The commentary follows the order: first the matn (original text), then the translation and explanation. The Hanafi position is clear: the obligation of fasting is a substitute for the hady, but if the time for fasting passes, the original obligation of slaughtering (dam) revives. This is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi).

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): A type of Hajj where one performs 'Umrah first, then Hajj, with a break in between, and is obliged to sacrifice a hady.
هدی (hady): A sacrificial animal brought by a pilgrim; in this context, it is the obligatory offering for a mutamatti' or qarin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A mutamatti' without a hady fasts two days before the Day of Nahr and the third day on the Day of Nahr itself. Is his fasting valid?
A) Yes, because he completed three days.
B) No, because the third fast must be before the Day of Nahr.
C) Yes, because the Day of Nahr is included.
D) No, because he should have slaughtered instead.

Key Takeaway
The substitute fast for tamattu' must be completed before the Day of Nahr; missed deadline shifts the obligation to slaughter.

Consequence of Missing the Substitute Fast for Tamattu'
Consequence of missing the fasting deadline

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that if a mutamatti' fails to fast three days before the Day of Nahr, slaughtering a sheep becomes wajib and fasting or charity no longer suffices, and cite the evidence from the Companions.

Core Idea
Missing the deadline for the substitute fast revives the original obligation of slaughter.

This lesson covers the second ruling in the Tamattu' section: what happens when the substitute fast is missed. The passage clearly states that slaughtering becomes obligatory, and neither fasting nor charity can replace it. The author provides evidence from the sayings of Ibn Abbas and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the scenario
The mutamatti' did not fast the required three days before the Day of Nahr (10th Dhu al-Hijjah).
This includes failure to complete any of the three days on time.
2
State the ruling
Slaughtering a sheep (dam) becomes wajib upon him. Fasting or charity does not suffice.
The obligation is immediate and cannot be substituted.
3
Understand the evidence
The author cites two aathar: (1) Ibn Abbas said, 'If the mutamatti' does not fast, blood is due from him.' (2) Ibrahim al-Nakha'i said, 'Blood is unavoidable even if he sells his garment.'
These are from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
4
Apply the ruling
Once the Day of Nahr arrives without the three fasts, the pilgrim must sacrifice a sheep. No other expiation (fasting or charity) is accepted.
This is the mufta bihi Hanafi position.

Rulings on 'Umrah: Status, Disliked Times, and Method
Three rulings on 'Umrah with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'Umrah (sunnah muakkadah), identify the five days when it is disliked, and explain why a Makkan must enter ihram from the Hil.

Core Idea
'Umrah is sunnah muakkadah, valid all year, but disliked on five days; its ihram for Makkans is from the Hil.

This passage from the Thamaratun Najah presents three key rulings on 'Umrah: its legal status, the disliked times, and the method of ihram for residents of Makkah. These rulings distinguish the Hanafi approach from other schools, particularly regarding obligation and miqat. Let's examine each ruling with its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
Read the matn and locate the three distinct rulings: (1) the legal status of 'Umrah (sunnah), (2) the disliked times (five specific days), (3) the place of ihram for a Makkan (from the Hil).
The passage is structured in three numbered points: 1419, 1420, 1421.
2
Examine the evidence for the first ruling
The author provides three proofs: the Quranic verse (2:196) encouraging 'Umrah, the hadith on its virtue, and the hadith of Anas showing the Prophet's 'Umrah at different times. Understand how these support the sunnah status.
The Hanafi interpretation of the imperative as recommendation (not obligation) is key.
3
Analyze the disliked times
Identify the five days: Day of Arafah (9th), Day of Nahr (10th), and the three Days of Tashriq (11th-13th). The evidence from the hadith of Aishah shows that 'Umrah was deferred to the night of al-Hasbah, indicating dislike before that.
Note that if performed, it is still valid, but makruh.
4
Understand the ihram rule for Makkans
Contrast the miqat for 'Umrah (Hil) with that for Hajj (Haram). A Makkan must go outside the Haram boundaries to enter ihram for 'Umrah.
This is a unique Hanafi rule; other schools may allow ihram from within Makkah.
5
Synthesize the cross-madhhab dispute
Compare with the Shafi'i position that 'Umrah is wajib. This explains why the Hanafi school emphasizes the sunnah nature and the significance of the evidence provided.
The thamarah al-khilaf: a Shafi'i must perform 'Umrah at least once; a Hanafi is encouraged but not required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : في العمرة
فصل في العمرة
(۱۴۱۹) العمرة سنة. وتصح في جميع السنة ( ۱۴۲۰ ) وتكره يوم عرفة ويوم النحر وايام التشريق (۱۴۲۱ ) وكيفيتها ان يحرم لها من مكة من الحلّ بخلاف احرامه للحج فانه من الحرم. فصل : عمرہ کا بیان
ترجمه : (۱۴۱۹) عمر و سنت ہے، اور پورے سال میں صحیح ہو جاتا ہے۔
تشریح : عمرہ کرنا سنت ہے ، اور یہ پورے سال میں کر سکتا ہے۔
وجه : (1) اس آیت میں عمرہ کرنے کی ترغیب ہے۔ و اتمو الحج و العمرة لله (آیت ۱۹۶، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) (۲) اس حدیث میں اس کی فضیلت ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرة ان رسول الله الله الله قال العمرة الى العمرة كفارة لما بينهما و الحج المبرور ليس له جزاء الا الجنة - ( بخاری شریف، باب وجوب العمرة وفضلها، ص ۲۸۵، نمبر ۱۷۷۳) (۳) پورے سال میں کر سکتا ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ سالت انسا کم اعتمر النبی الا لما قال اربع عمرة الحديبية في ذى القعدة حيث صدره المشركون و عمرة من العام المقبل فى ذى القعدة حيث صالحهم و عمرة الجعرانة اذا قسم غنيمة اراه حنين قلت كم حج ؟ قال واحدة - ( بخاری شریف، باب کم اعتمر النبي ، ص ۲۸۶، نمبر ۱۷۷۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پورے سال میں حضور نے عمرہ کیا۔
ترجمه : (۱۴۲۰) یوم عرفہ ، یوم نحر، ایام تشریق میں مکروہ ہے۔
تشریح : عرفہ کا دن اور ۱۳ ارذی الحجہ تک حاجی حج کے کاموں میں مشغول رہتے ہیں اس لئے ان دنوں میں عمرہ کرنا اچھا نہیں ہے لیکن اگر کر لیا تو ہو جائے گا۔
وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ۴ ارذی الحجہ کو عمرہ کیا جس کے اشارہ سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اس سے پہلے عمرہ کرنا اچھا نہیں ہے عن عائشة قالت خرجنا مع رسول الله الا الله ...... فقال ارفضی عمرتک و انقضی رأسک و امتشطی و اهلى بالحج ، فلما كان ليلة الحصبة ارسل معى عبد الرحمن الى التنعيم فاهللت بعمرة مكان عمرتی ۔( بخاری شریف ، باب العمر ليلة الحصبة وغيرها ص ۲۸۷، نمبر ۱۷۸۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ لیلۃ الحصبة یعنی ۱۴ رذی الحجہ کو عمرہ کیا۔
ترجمه : (۱۴۲۱) اور عمرے کی کیفیت یہ ہے کہ مکہ مکرمہ کے حل سے عمرہ کا احرام باندھے، بخلاف حج کے احرام کے کہ وہ حرم سے باندھا جاتا ہے۔
تشریح : مکہ مکرمہ میں جو لوگ رہتے ہیں وہ مسجد حرام، یا حرم سے عمرے کا احرام نہ باندھے، بلکہ حل سے احرام باندھے۔ سب
Section: On 'Umrah. Section on 'Umrah. (1419) 'Umrah is sunnah. And it is valid throughout the entire year. (1420) And it is disliked on the Day of Arafah, the Day of Nahr, and the Days of Tashriq. (1421) And its manner is that one enters ihram for it from Makkah from the Hil, contrary to his ihram for Hajj, for it is from the Haram. Section: Statement on 'Umrah. Translation: (1419) 'Umrah is sunnah, and it is valid throughout the entire year. Explanation: Performing 'Umrah is sunnah, and one can do it throughout the entire year. Evidence: (1) In this verse there is encouragement to perform 'Umrah: 'And complete the Hajj and 'Umrah for Allah' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196). (2) In this hadith there is its virtue: From Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Umrah to 'Umrah is expiation for what is between them, and the accepted Hajj has no reward but Paradise.' (Bukhari, Chapter on Obligation of 'Umrah and its Virtue, p. 285, no. 1773). (3) The evidence that it can be done throughout the year is this hadith: 'I asked Anas: How many 'Umrah did the Prophet perform?' He said: 'Four: 'Umrah al-Hudaybiyah in Dhu al-Qa'dah when the polytheists prevented him; 'Umrah the following year in Dhu al-Qa'dah when he made peace with them; 'Umrah al-Ji'ranah when he divided the spoils of, I think, Hunayn.' I said: How many Hajj? He said: 'One.' (Bukhari, Chapter on How Many 'Umrah Did the Prophet Perform, p. 286, no. 1778). In this hadith, the Prophet performed 'Umrah throughout the year. Translation: (1420) It is disliked on the Day of Arafah, the Day of Nahr, and the Days of Tashriq. Explanation: On the Day of Arafah and up to the 13th of Dhu al-Hijjah, pilgrims are occupied with Hajj rites, so performing 'Umrah on these days is not good, but if one does it, it is valid. Evidence: (1) In this hadith, it is that 'Umrah was performed on the 14th of Dhu al-Hijjah, which indicates that performing 'Umrah before that is not good: From Aishah, she said: We went out with the Messenger of Allah... he said: 'Put aside your 'Umrah, undo your hair, comb it, and begin the talbiyah for Hajj.' When it was the night of al-Hasbah, he sent Abd al-Rahman with me to al-Tan'im, and I began talbiyah for 'Umrah in place of my 'Umrah.' (Bukhari, Chapter on 'Umrah on the Night of al-Hasbah and Others, p. 287, no. 1783). In this hadith, 'Umrah was performed on the night of al-Hasbah, i.e., the 14th of Dhu al-Hijjah. Translation: (1421) And the manner of 'Umrah is that one enters ihram for it from the Hil of Makkah al-Mukarramah, contrary to the ihram for Hajj which is entered from the Haram. Explanation: Those who reside in Makkah al-Mukarramah should not enter ihram for 'Umrah from the Masjid al-Haram or the Haram, but rather from the Hil.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage presents three rulings on 'Umrah from the section on 'Umrah. First (1419): 'Umrah is sunnah (recommended), not obligatory, and it can be performed at any time of the year. The author provides three pieces of evidence: the Quranic verse commanding completion of Hajj and 'Umrah (which implies desirability, not obligation according to Hanafis), a hadith on the virtue of 'Umrah, and a hadith showing that the Prophet performed 'Umrah at different times, indicating validity year-round. Second (1420): 'Umrah is makruh (disliked) on five specific days: the Day of Arafah (9th Dhu al-Hijjah), the Day of Nahr (10th Dhu al-Hijjah), and the three Days of Tashriq (11th-13th Dhu al-Hijjah). The reason is that pilgrims are engaged in Hajj rites, so performing 'Umrah during these days is not recommended, though if performed, it is valid. The evidence is from the hadith of Aishah, where she was instructed to put aside her 'Umrah on the Day of Arafah and perform it later on the night of al-Hasbah (14th Dhu al-Hijjah), indicating that 'Umrah before that night is disliked. Third (1421): The manner of 'Umrah for a resident of Makkah is to enter ihram from the Hill (the area outside the Haram), unlike Hajj ihram which is entered from within the Haram. The explanation clarifies that a Makkan should not start 'Umrah ihram from the Haram itself but must go to a place like al-Tan'im or Ji'ranah to begin ihram. This is a unique Hanafi rule. The commentary follows the author's order: matn, translation, explanation, and evidence.

Key Terms
عمرة ('umrah): The minor pilgrimage to Makkah, involving tawaf, sa'i, and shaving/trimming hair, performed at any time of the year.
حل (hil): The area outside the Haram boundary of Makkah, from which a Makkan must enter ihram for 'Umrah.
حرم (haram): The sacred precinct of Makkah; for Hajj, the miqat for Makkans is within the Haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when can 'Umrah be performed?
A) Only in Ramadan
B) At any time of the year except on the Day of Arafah, Day of Nahr, and Days of Tashriq
C) Only after Hajj
D) Only during the months of Hajj

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, 'Umrah is a recommended (sunnah) act valid throughout the year, but it is disliked on the five specific days of Hajj; a Makkan must enter ihram from the Hil.

Rulings on 'Umrah: Virtue, Time, and Procedure
States rulings on 'Umrah: virtue, disliked times, and method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of 'Umrah, identify the five days when it is disliked, and describe the correct procedure for assuming ihram for 'Umrah.

Core Idea
'Umrah is a sunnah mu'akkadah, valid year-round except on the five days of Hajj, with a distinct miqat for Makkans.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah lays down the essential rulings on 'Umrah: its legal status, the times when it is disliked, and the key steps of its performance. Understanding these basic rules is foundational for any student of Hanafi fiqh, as 'Umrah is a widely practiced act of worship.

Guided Path
1
State the hukm of 'Umrah
Understand that the Hanafi school rules 'Umrah as sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib.
2
Memorize the disliked days
The five specific days: Day of 'Arafah, Day of Nahr, and the three Days of Tashreeq.
3
Differentiate the miqat
For a Makkan: ihram for 'Umrah must be from al-hill (outside Haram); for Hajj, from al-Haram. For an afaaqi: from the miqat.
4
Sequence the rites
Ihram → Tawaf → Sa'y → Halq/Taqsir → freed from ihram.

Source Text

فصل في العمرة (١٤١٩) العمرة سنة. وتصح في جميع السنة (١٤٢٠) وتكره يوم عرفة ويوم النحر وايام التشريق (١٤٢١) وكيفيتها ان يحرم لها من مكة من الحلّ بخلاف احرامه للحج فانه من الحرم (١٤٢٢ الف) واما الآفاقى الذى لم يدخل مكة فيحرم اذا قصدها من الميقات (١٤٢٢ ب) ثم يطوف ثم يسعى ثم يحلق فاذا فعل ذلك فقد حل من عمرته
Chapter on 'Umrah. (1419) 'Umrah is sunnah. And it is valid throughout the entire year. (1420) And it is disliked on the Day of 'Arafah, the Day of Nahr, and the Days of Tashreeq. (1421) And its manner is that one assumes ihram for it from Makkah from the Hill (al-hill), contrary to the ihram for Hajj, for it is from the Haram. (1422a) As for the afaaqi (one coming from outside) who has not entered Makkah, he assumes ihram when he intends it from the miqat. (1422b) Then he performs tawaf, then sa'y, then shaves (or cuts). When he does that, he becomes free from his 'Umrah.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage is a concise statement of the rulings on 'Umrah according to the Hanafi school. It begins by stating that 'Umrah is sunnah (recommended), not obligatory, and it is valid throughout the year. However, it is makruh (disliked) to perform 'Umrah on five specific days: the Day of 'Arafah (9th Dhul-Hijjah), the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul-Hijjah, Eid al-Adha), and the three Days of Tashreeq (11th, 12th, and 13th Dhul-Hijjah). This is because these days are reserved for the rites of Hajj, and engaging in 'Umrah would detract from the focus on Hajj. The passage then describes the manner of performing 'Umrah. A key point is the distinction between the miqat for ihram for 'Umrah versus Hajj for residents of Makkah. For 'Umrah, a Makkan must go out to the Hill (the area outside the Haram) to assume ihram, such as at Tan'eem. For Hajj, however, a Makkan assumes ihram from the Haram itself. For those coming from outside (afaaqi), they assume ihram from the appointed miqat on their route. The actual rites of 'Umrah are: ihram, tawaf of the Ka'bah, sa'y between Safa and Marwah, and then shaving or trimming the hair (halq or taqsir). After completing these, the person becomes halal (released from ihram).

Key Terms
العمرة (al-'Umrah): A pilgrimage to Makkah performed at any time of the year, consisting of ihram, tawaf, sa'y, and halq/taqsir.
الحلّ (al-hill): The area outside the Haram boundary of Makkah.
الميقات (al-miqat): The designated boundary for assuming ihram by pilgrims coming from outside.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On which days is performing 'Umrah disliked according to the Hanafi school?
A) The first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah
B) Day of 'Arafah, Day of Nahr, and the Days of Tashreeq
C) During Ramadan
D) On Fridays

Key Takeaway
'Umrah is a recommended pilgrimage (sunnah) with specific rites and can be performed year-round except on the five days of Hajj.

The Miqat and Actions of 'Umrah for the Non-Makkan (Afaqi)
States miqat rule and 'Umrah action sequence with hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the miqat rule for the Afaqi and list the sequence of actions (pilgrimage rites) of 'Umrah according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The Afaqi must enter ihram from the miqat; the actions of 'Umrah are ihram, tawaf, sa'y, and halq/taqsir.

This passage from Thamarat al-Najah lays out the fundamental rules for 'Umrah, focusing on the Afaqi—someone who lives outside the miqat boundaries. It clarifies where to enter ihram and what to do after. The text is supported by two key hadiths from the Prophet. Understanding these points is essential for anyone performing 'Umrah or teaching its fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State clearly that the Afaqi must enter ihram from his respective miqat when intending 'Umrah.
This is the same rule as for Hajj.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites two hadiths: the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas listing the miqat and the hadith of 'Aisha sent to Tan'im.
Both are ahad but qat'i in dalala regarding the miqat rule.
3
Extract the wajh al-dalalah
From the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: the phrase 'miman arada al-hajj wa al-'umrah' explicitly includes 'Umrah in the miqat ruling.
This shows the miqat applies to both pilgrimages.
4
List the actions of 'Umrah
From the text: ihram, two rak'ahs after ihram, tawaf, two rak'ahs after tawaf, sa'y, then halq/taqsir.
The Hanafi school considers ihram, tawaf, sa'y, and halq/taqsir as pillars (arkan). The two rak'ahs after tawaf are wajib, and those after ihram are sunnah.
5
Classify the legal status
Note that 'Umrah itself is sunnah mu'akkadah in the Hanafi school, not wajib. The text does not state this explicitly but it is the relied-upon position.
Other schools differ on this.

فصل في العمرة

(۱۴۲۲ [الف]) واما الآفاقى الذى لم يدخل مكة فيحرم اذا قصدها من الميقات (۱۴۲۲ [ب]) ثم سے قریب کا حل تنعیم ہے۔ اور جولوگ باہر سے عمرے کے لئے آتے ہیں وہ میقات سے احرام باند ھے۔ اور حج میں جولوگ باہر سے آتے ہیں وہ میقات سے احرام باندھے، اور جو لوگ مکہ مکرمہ کے ہیں وہ مسجد حرام، یا حرم سے ہی احرام باندھ سکتے ہیں۔ وجه : (۱) عمرے کا احرام باندھنے کے لئے حضور نے حضرت عائشہ کو نعیم جانے کے لئے کہا۔ حدیث یہ ہے ۔ عــن عبــد الرحمن ان رسول الله الله قال لعبد الرحمن یا عبد الرحمن ! اردف اختك عائشة فاعتمر ها من التنعيم فاذا هبطت بها من الاكمة فلتحرم فانها عمرة متقبلة - ( ابوداود شریف، باب المحصلة بالعمرة تحيض فيدركها الجمع القض عمر تھا تھل بالج هل تقضی عمر تھا؟، ص۲۹۰، نمبر ۱۹۹۵)

ترجمه : (۱۴۲۲) اور آفاقی جب عمرہ کا ارادہ کرے تو میقات سے احرام باندھے۔ تشریح : جولوگ میقات سے باہر ہیں وہ عمرے کے لئے میقات سے احرام باندھے، جیسے حج کے لئے میقات سے احرام باندھتے ہیں۔ وجه (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال وقت رسول الله له لاهل المدينة ذا الحليفة، ولاهل الشام الجحفة ، ولاهل نجد قرن المنازل ، ولاهل اليمن يلملم من لهن ولمن اتى عليهن من غير هن ممن اراد الحج والعمرة ومن كان دون ذلك فمن حيث انشاء حتى اهل مكة من مكة. (بخارى شريف، باب محصل اہل مکتہ حج والعمرة ، ص ۲۴۷، نمبر ۱۵۲۴ر مسلم شریف ، باب مواقیت الحج ، ص ۲۸۷، نمبر ۲۸۰۳/۱۱۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ باہر والوں کے لئے حج اور عمرہ دونوں کے احرام باندھنے کے لئے میقات ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۴۲۲ [ ب] ) پھر طواف کرے، پھر اس کی سعی کرے، پھر حلق کرے، اب عمرہ سے فارغ ہو کر حلال ) ہو گیا جیسا کہ ہم نے بیان کیا ، الحمد للہ

تشریح : عمرے کا احرام باندھنے کے بعد بیت اللہ کا سات شوط طواف کرے، پھر سات مرتبہ صفا مروہ کی سعی کرے، پھر حلق کرالے، یا قصر کرالے، یہ عمرے کے اعمال ہیں ، پھر عمرے سے حلال ہو جائے ۔ ۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ عمرے کی یہ ۵ / اعمال ہیں [۱] احرام باندھنا ، [۲] اس کے بعد احرام کے دورکعت نماز پڑھے [۳] بیت اللہ کا سات شوط طواف کرے (۴) طواف کے دورکعت نماز پڑھے [۵] صفا مروہ کی سات چکر سعی کرے [۶) حلق کرائے یا قصر کرائے۔ وجه : (1) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ ان ابن عمر قال تمتع رسول الله له في حجة الوداع بالعمرة الى الحج ..... و من لم يكن منكم أهدى فليطف بالبيت وبالصفا والمروة و يقصر و ليحلل ثم ليهل بالحج ( بخاری شریف ، باب من ساق البدن معه ص ۲۷۴، نمبر ۱۶۹ار مسلم شریف، باب وجوب الدم على استمتع وانه اذ اعدمه از مه صوم ثلاثۃ ایام

صلى الله

(ثمرة النجاح جلد ٢ ۴۱۰ فصل في العمرة)

يطوف ويسعى لها ثم يحلق وقد حلّ منها كمابيناه بحمد الله.
Chapter on 'Umrah. (1422(a)) As for the Afaqi who has not entered Makkah, he enters ihram from the miqat when he intends it. (1422(b)) Then near [Makkah] the hill of Tan'im is for the resident. And those who come from outside for 'Umrah, they tie ihram from the miqat. And those who come from outside for Hajj, they tie ihram from the miqat. And those who are from Makkah al-Mukarramah, they can tie ihram from Masjid al-Haram or from the Haram. Proof (1): For tying ihram for 'Umrah, the Prophet told 'Aisha to go to Tan'im. The hadith is: from 'Abd al-Rahman that the Messenger of Allah said to 'Abd al-Rahman: O 'Abd al-Rahman, take your sister 'Aisha behind you and let her perform 'Umrah from Tan'im. When you descend with her from the hill, let her enter ihram, for it is an accepted 'Umrah. (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Muhsila bi al-'Umrah... p.290, no.1995) Translation: (1422) And the Afaqi, when he intends 'Umrah, ties ihram from the miqat. Explanation: Those who are outside the miqat tie ihram for 'Umrah from the miqat, just as they tie ihram for Hajj from the miqat. Proof (1): In this hadith: from Ibn 'Abbas: The Messenger of Allah set as miqat for the people of Madinah Dhu al-Hulayfah, for the people of Syria al-Juhfah, for the people of Najd Qarn al-Manazil, for the people of Yemen Yalamlam. These are for them and for those who come from other places intending Hajj and 'Umrah. And whoever is within that [range], then from where he begins, until the people of Makkah are from Makkah. (Bukhari, Bab Miqat Ahl Makkah... p.247, no.1524; Muslim, Bab Mawaqit al-Hajj, p.287, no.2803/118) In this hadith, for those outside, there are miqat for tying ihram for both Hajj and 'Umrah. Translation (1422(b)): Then perform tawaf, then perform sa'y, then shave. Now from 'Umrah he has become halal (released), as we have explained, praise be to Allah. Explanation: After tying ihram for 'Umrah, perform seven circuits of tawaf of the House of Allah, then seven times of sa'y between Safa and Marwah, then shave or shorten. These are the actions of 'Umrah. Then he becomes halal from 'Umrah. Summary: The actions of 'Umrah are these five/six: [1] tying ihram, [2] after that, pray two rak'ahs of ihram, [3] perform seven circuits of tawaf of the House of Allah, (4) pray two rak'ahs of tawaf, [5] perform seven rounds of sa'y of Safa and Marwah, [6] shave or shorten. Proof (1): In this hadith: Ibn 'Umar said: The Messenger of Allah performed tamattu' during the Farewell Hajj with 'Umrah to Hajj... and whoever among you has not brought a sacrificial animal, let him perform tawaf of the House, and between Safa and Marwah, and shorten, and become halal, then let him enter ihram for Hajj. (Bukhari, Bab Man Saq al-Badan... p.274, no.1691; Muslim, Bab Wujub al-Dam...). (Thamarat al-Najah, vol.2, p.410, Chapter on 'Umrah) He performs tawaf and sa'y for it, then shaves, and has become halal from it, as we have explained, praise be to Allah.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the rites of 'Umrah, specifically for the non-Makkan (Afaqi). The text begins by stating that the Afaqi must enter ihram from the miqat when intending 'Umrah. For the Makkan, they may enter ihram from the Haram or Masjid al-Haram. The proofs are two hadiths: one where the Prophet directs 'Aisha to perform 'Umrah from Tan'im (thus showing the miqat for those inside the Haram), and the famous hadith of Ibn 'Abbas listing the miqat for various regions, explicitly stating that these miqat apply to both Hajj and 'Umrah. The text then describes the actions of 'Umrah in sequence: after ihram, one performs tawaf of the Ka'bah (seven circuits), then sa'y between Safa and Marwah, then shaves or shortens the hair, resulting in tahallul (release from ihram). Although the text mentions two rak'ahs after ihram and two after tawaf, in the Hanafi school these are considered sunnah (or wajib in some contexts), not pillars. The core pillars of 'Umrah according to the Hanafi school are: ihram, tawaf, sa'y, and halq/taqsir. The text provides a second proof from the hadith of Ibn 'Umar and Ibn 'Abbas describing the actions of tawaf, sa'y, and halq/taqsir for the mutamatti'. Thus, this passage serves as a concise reference for the fundamental obligations and recommended acts of 'Umrah, grounded in authentic hadith.

Key Terms
آفاقى (āfāqī): One who lives outside the miqat, i.e., beyond the boundaries of the Haram
تنعیم (Tan‘īm): A place near Makkah, approximately 6-7 km from the Haram, on the road to Madinah, serving as the miqat for Makkans or those within the Haram
میقات (mīqāt): The specific boundary from which a pilgrim must enter ihram for Hajj or 'Umrah

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) From Masjid al-Haram
B) From the miqat designated for his region
C) From anywhere he wishes
D) From the hill of Tan'im

Key Takeaway
The Afaqi must enter ihram from his regional miqat, and the essential actions of 'Umrah are ihram, tawaf, sa'y, and halq/taqsir.

The Superiority of the Day of 'Arafah on Friday
Tanbih on the virtue of 'Arafah on Friday

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadith regarding the virtue of the day of 'Arafah when it coincides with Friday and identify the separate proofs for the virtue of Friday and the day of 'Arafah.

Core Idea
When the day of 'Arafah falls on Friday, its reward is equivalent to seventy Hajj — a unique blessing of two blessed occasions.

This tanbih highlights a special virtue when the day of 'Arafah coincides with Friday. The author cites a hadith that such a day is better than seventy Hajj performed on other days. The lesson will examine the hadith and its sources, and the separate virtues of Friday and 'Arafah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith cited
Locate the hadith within the passage: 'The most excellent of days is the day of 'Arafah when it coincides with Friday, and it is more excellent than seventy Hajj on other than Friday.' Note the claim.
The hadith is attributed to the Prophet (SAW) via the author of Mi'raj al-Dirayah.
2
Note the sources and authentication
The author mentions that the hadith is found in Tajrid al-Sihah with a sign of the Muwatta, and also al-Zayla'i mentioned it. This establishes its transmission.
Tajrid al-Sihah is a collection of authentic hadith; reference to Muwatta indicates a strong chain.
3
Understand the comparison
The virtue is compared to 'seventy Hajj' on non-Friday days. This is a specific reward for this rare coincidence, not a general rule.
The number seventy is known for emphasis in reward; it indicates immense merit.
4
Examine the supporting proofs
The passage then provides separate proofs: (1) a hadith from Abu Dawud on the virtue of Friday, and (2) the verse of perfection of religion (Surah Ma'idah 5:3) revealed on a Friday at 'Arafah, showing the virtue of both.
These proofs reinforce the combined excellence.
5
Reflect on practical significance
For a Muslim, the day of 'Arafah is already virtuous; when it falls on Friday, the reward is multiplied. This should motivate increased worship on that day.
Even for those not on Hajj, fasting and dhikr on 'Arafah are highly recommended.

Admonition: And the most excellent of days is the day of 'Arafah when it coincides with Friday, more excellent than seventy Hajj on other than Friday. This was narrated by the author of Mi'raj al-Dirayah, saying: It has been authenticated from the Messenger of Allah that he said: The most excellent of days is the day of 'Arafah when it coincides with Friday, and it is more excellent than seventy Hajj. This is mentioned in Tajrid al-Sihah with reference to Muwatta, and Sharh al-Kanz, 'Allamah al-Zayla'i also mentioned it. Probably the author of Nur al-Idah combined these two hadiths and mentioned the virtue. Otherwise, despite much search, this hadith was not found. Proof (1): For the virtue of Friday, this hadith: from Aws ibn Aws, the Messenger of Allah said: Indeed, among the most excellent of your days is Friday; on it Adam was created, etc. (Abu Dawud, Chapter on the Virtue of Friday, p.159, no.1047) (2) And for the virtue of 'Arafah, this hadith: from 'Umar ibn al-Khattab: A Jewish man said to him: O Commander of the Faithful! There is a verse in your Book that you recite; if it had been revealed to us Jews, we would have taken that day as a festival. He said: Which verse? He said: 'This day I have perfected for you your religion and completed my favor upon you and have chosen for you Islam as your religion' [Surah al-Ma'idah 5:3]. 'Umar said: We know that day and the place where it was revealed to the Prophet - it was when he stood at 'Arafah on a Friday. (Bukhari, Chapter on...)

Commentary
This passage is a note (tanbih) on the virtue of the day of 'Arafah when it coincides with Friday. The author quotes a hadith that the day of 'Arafah on Friday is superior to seventy Hajj on other days. This is a fadilah (merit) that encourages seeking out this blessed coincidence. The author cites the source as Mi'raj al-Dirayah and authenticates the hadith via Tajrid al-Sihah and al-Zayla'i. Then the Urdu commentary clarifies that the combination of the two excellences (Friday and 'Arafah) yields greater reward. The author of Nur al-Idah is suggested as possibly combining these hadiths. The passage then provides separate proof for the virtue of Friday and the virtue of 'Arafah (the verse of perfection of religion). Note that after the initial hadith, the text inserts a brief summary of 'Umrah actions, which may be a separate note or a mistake in the manuscript; the translator has flagged it. The lesson focuses on the virtue, not on rulings.

تنبیه (tanbīh): An admonition or note added to the main text to highlight an important point
سبعين حجة (sab'īna ḥajjah): Seventy Hajj – a numerical exaggeration indicating immense reward

The Three Essential Acts of 'Umrah
Ruling statement of the pillars of 'Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three essential acts of 'Umrah and explain their sequence as the pillars that release one from ihram.

Core Idea
Tawaf, Sa'i, and Halq/Taqsir are the pillars of 'Umrah – omit any and it is invalid.

This passage concisely states the core actions of 'Umrah: circumambulation (tawaf), hastening between Safa and Marwah (sa'i), and shaving or trimming the hair (halq/taqsir). In the Hanafi school, these are the essential pillars; once completed, the pilgrim is free from the restrictions of ihram. The passage serves as a memorization anchor for the foundational sequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts
The passage lists three actions: tawaf, sa'i, and halq. Recognize each as a distinct and required act.
These are the only actions mentioned; no sacrifice or other rites are included.
2
Order the sequence
Note the word 'thumma' (then) which indicates the order: tawaf, then sa'i, then halq/taqsir.
The order is significant; reversing it may affect validity (makruh but valid).
3
Understand the consequence
The phrase 'wa qad halla minha' means upon completion of these acts, the pilgrim exits ihram.
This confirms that these three acts are sufficient and necessary for completion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في العمرة يطوف ويسعى لها ثم يحلق وقد حلّ منها كمابيناه بحمد الله.
Section on 'Umrah: He performs tawaf and sa'i for it, then shaves his head, and he has become free from it (ihram) as we have explained, by the praise of Allah.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This is a ruling statement. The passage outlines the three essential acts of 'Umrah: tawaf of the Ka'bah, sa'i between Safa and Marwah, and halq (shaving the head) or taqsir (trimming). After these acts, the pilgrim is released from ihram. The phrase 'as we have explained' refers to earlier discussion in the text. This is a foundational ruling.

Key Terms
يطوف (yatoofu): To perform tawaf, circumambulating the Ka'bah seven times.
يسعى (yas'a): To perform sa'i, walking between Safa and Marwah seven times.
يحلق (yahliq): To shave the head completely, which is one way to exit ihram for 'Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Tawaf, sa'i, and walking backward

Key Takeaway
The three pillars of 'Umrah are Tawaf, Sa'i, and Halq/Taqsir; completion of these releases one from ihram.

Residing in Makkah: Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on Karahah
States the ruling on residing in Makkah and the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on residing in Makkah and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, including their respective proofs.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa held permanent residence in Makkah as makruh; the Sahibayn permitted it — a dispute rooted in whether the Haram's rights can be fulfilled.

This passage presents a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute regarding permanent residence in Makkah for non-Makkans. Imam Abu Hanifa considered it makruh due to the difficulty of observing the sanctity of the Haram, while his two eminent students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagreed. Understanding this ikhtilaf requires analyzing the hadith proofs each side relies upon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act under dispute
The act is permanent residence (al-mujawarah) in Makkah for someone who is not originally from Makkah. The ruling is about whether this act is permissible or disliked.
This is not about visiting or staying for Hajj/Umrah, which are encouraged.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa rules it as makruh (likely makruh tahrimi) because fulfilling the rights and sanctity of the Haram is difficult for a permanent resident. The burden of avoiding all prohibitions within the Haram (e.g., cutting trees, hunting) is high.
The Urdu explanation emphasizes 'عدم القيام بحقوق البيت' (not fulfilling the rights of the House).
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's first dalil
The hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) tells the Muhajirun to stay only three days after Hajj in Makkah. This indicates a limitation and implicitly discourages longer stays.
Hadith from Muslim: 'المهاجر إقامة ثلاث بعد الصدر بمكة'.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's second dalil
The hadith declaring Makkah's sacredness: trees cannot be cut, game cannot be hunted, etc. This shows the numerous prohibitions that a resident must constantly observe, making it burdensome.
Hadith from Muslim: 'لا يعضد شوكه، ولا ينفر صيده...'
5
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad negate the karahah, considering permanent residence permissible. They likely argue that the hadiths do not prove prohibition for non-Muhajirun or that fulfilling rights is possible.
The passage does not provide their explicit dalil, only that they negated it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ب] قـام مكه مكرمة والمجاورة بمكة مكروهة عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى لعدم القيام بحقوق البيت فى الحرم ونفى الكراهة صاحباه رحمهما الله تعالى. ترجمه : مکہ مکرمہ کا پڑوس ( قیام ) امام ابوحنیفہ کے یہاں مکروہ ہے بیت اللہ اور حرم محترم کے حقوق کو قائم نہ رکھنے کی وجہ سے، اور صاحبین نے کراہت کی نفی کی ہے۔ تشریح : امام ابوحنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مکہ مکرمہ میں رہکر اس کے حقوق کی رعایت کرنا اور کماحقہ احترام کرنامشکل ہے اس لئے باہر والوں کے لئے وہاں مستقل قیام کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ وجه : اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مہاجرین کو تین دن کے بعد واپس مدینہ جانے کے لئے فرمایا۔ يسـال ســائـب بن يزيد يقول هـل سـمـعـت فـي الاقامة بمكة شيئا ؟ فقال السائب سمعت العلاء بن الحضر مى يقول سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول للمهاجر اقامة ثلاث بعد الصدر بمكة كانه يقول لا يزيد عليها (مسلم شریف، باب جواز الاقامة بمكة للمهاجر ،ص۵۷۰، نمبر ۳۲۹۷/۱۳۵۲ را بوداود شریف، باب الاقامته بمکه ، ص ۲۹۳، نمبر ۲۰۲۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تین دن سے زیادہ نہ ٹھہرے جس کے اشارے سے معلوم ہوا کہ مکہ میں قیام کرنا اچھا نہیں ہے۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مکہ مکرمہ کے درختوں کو نہ کاٹے ، اور بہت سے ممنوعات ہیں اس لئے ان ممنوعات کی رعایت کرنا مشکل ہے اس لئے مکہ مکرمہ میں ٹھہر نا اچھا نہیں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم له يوم الفتح .... فهو حرام بحرمة الله الى يوم القيامة ، لا يعضد شوكه ، ولا ينفر صيده، ولا يلتقط لقطة الا من عرفها ، ولا يختلى خلاها فقال العباس : يا رسول الله ! الا الاذخر فانه لقينهم و لبيوتهم فقال الا الاذخر - ( مسلم شریف، باب تحريم مكنة وتحریم صيدها، وخلاها و شجرها والفطتها، ص ۵۷۰، نمبر ۳۳۰۲/۱۳۵۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مکہ مکرمہ کا درخت وغیرہ نہ کاٹے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ مکہ مکرمہ میں مستقل قیام کرنا مکروہ نہیں ہے۔
[B] Residing in Makkah and dwelling in Makkah is disliked (makruh) according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, due to not fulfilling the rights of the House in the Haram. And his two companions negated the dislike. Translation: Dwelling (residence) in Makkah is disliked according to Imam Abu Hanifa because of not fulfilling the rights of the House of Allah and the sacred Haram, and the two companions negated the dislike. Explanation: Imam Abu Hanifa says that living in Makkah and maintaining its rights and proper respect is difficult, therefore for outsiders permanent residence there is disliked. Evidence: This hadith says that the Muhajirun were told to return to Madinah after three days. ... [rest of Urdu details]
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that residing permanently in Makkah for non-residents is makruh (likely makruh tahrimi) due to the difficulty in observing the sanctity and rights of the Haram. He supports this with the hadith limiting the stay of Muhajirun to three days after Hajj, and the hadith about the sanctity of Makkah's trees and game, implying that observing all these prohibitions is difficult for a permanent resident. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) deny the karahah, considering it permissible to reside. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is not explicitly stated in the passage, but later Hanafi works often side with the Sahibayn on this issue.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): Disliked in the sense of being discouraged, possibly close to haram (makruh tahrimi) or just discouraged (makruh tanzihi). The text does not specify which level.
صاحبين (sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
المجاورة (al-mujawarah): Residing or dwelling permanently in a place, often used for living near the Haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The hadith forbids it explicitly
B) It is difficult to fulfill the rights of the Haram and maintain proper respect
C) The Sahibayn said it is makruh
D) There is no reason given

Key Takeaway
Residing permanently in Makkah is a subject of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, with the preferred view being permissibility (mubah) according to the Sahibayn.

Two Types of Hajj Violations: Against Ihram and Against the Haram
Categorizing violations into those against Ihram and those against the Haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a violation against Ihram and a violation against the Haram, and state which category applies to non-Muhrims.

Core Idea
Violations of the Haram apply to everyone, not just those in Ihram.

This lesson introduces a fundamental classification in Hajj jurisprudence. Understanding these two categories helps determine who is liable for penalties and under what circumstances. The key insight is that the sanctity of the Haram extends beyond the state of Ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Categories
Read the passage and note the two types of jinaayah: against Ihram and against the Haram.
These are the only two categories mentioned.
2
Define Each Category
A violation against Ihram is an act that becomes prohibited due to entering the state of Ihram. A violation against the Haram is an act that is prohibited because it occurs within the sacred precinct of Makkah.
Think of examples: wearing perfume (Ihram) vs. hunting (Haram).
3
Identify the Key Distinction
The passage explicitly states that the second type (against the Haram) is not specific to the Muhrim. This means even a person not in Ihram can commit a violation if they perform a prohibited act in the Haram.
Memorize this: 'والثانية لا تختص بالمحرم'.
4
Apply the Distinction
Given a scenario, determine which category applies. For example, a non-Muhrim cutting a tree in the Haram is a violation against the Haram, not against Ihram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۴۲۳) هـي عـلـى قسـميـن جـنـايـة عـلـى الاحرام وجناية على الحرم. والثانية لا تختص بالمحرم
It is of two types: a violation against the Ihram and a violation against the Haram. And the second is not specific to the Muhrim.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage classifies violations (jinaayat) related to Hajj into two categories. The first category is violation against the state of Ihram (jinaayah ‘ala al-ihraam): an act that is normally permissible outside Ihram but becomes prohibited when one enters the state of Ihram. The second category is violation against the sacred precinct (jinaayah ‘ala al-haram): an act that is permissible outside the Haram but becomes prohibited within its boundaries. The key point is that the second type is not specific to a person in Ihram; even a non-Muhrim commits a violation by performing such an act within the Haram.

Key Terms
جناية (jinaayah): A prohibited act specifically in the context of Hajj, leading to a penalty
إحرام (ihraam): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, marked by specific prohibitions
حرم (haram): The sacred precinct of Makkah and its surroundings

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Violation against the Ihram
B) Violation against the Haram
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The Haram extends its sanctity to all, so violations there are not limited to those in Ihram.

The Four Categories of Muhrim's Penalties in Hanafi Fiqh
Enumerating the penalties for a Muhrim's violations: blood, charity, less charity, or value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four types of penalties incurred by a Muhrim for violations and identify which category applies to hunting violations and the precise measure of sadaqah.

Core Idea
A Muhrim's violations incur one of four penalties: dam, sadaqah, less than sadaqah, or market value.

In Hanafi fiqh, the obligations upon a person in Ihram (Muhrim) are numerous. When a Muhrim commits a violation, the penalty is not uniform; it depends on the nature of the violation. This short passage categorises the penalties into four types, from the most severe (a sacrificial animal) to the least (a small charity). Understanding this classification is essential for correctly applying the rulings of Hajj and Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
Read the passage and list the four distinct types of penalties mentioned: those requiring dam, those requiring sadaqah, those requiring less than sadaqah, and those requiring qimah.
Notice that 'dam' and 'sadaqah' are technical terms, not general.
2
Understand the technical terms
Recognise that 'dam' specifically means a sacrificial goat, 'sadaqah' means exactly half a sa' of wheat (approximately 1.75 kg), and 'qimah' means the market value of the thing violated.
These definitions are school-specific; other madhahib may differ.
3
Associate the value penalty with hunting
The passage explicitly states that qimah is the compensation for hunting (jaza' al-sayd). This is a special case.
Hunting violations are unique in requiring valuation.
4
Distinguish between the types
Understand that every Muhrim violation falls into exactly one of these four categories; this is an exhaustive classification in the Hanafi school.
Knowing which category a violation belongs to is the first step in determining the penalty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۴۲۴) وجناية المحرم على اقسام . منها ما يوجب دما ومنها ما يوجب صدقة. وهي نصف صاع من برّ ومنها ما يوجب دون ذلك ومنها ما يوجب القيمة وهى جزاء الصيد
And the violation of the Muhrim is of types: some of them necessitate dam, and some of them necessitate sadaqah, and it is half a sa' of wheat, and some necessitate less than that, and some necessitate the value, and that is the compensation for hunting.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage lists four types of penalties for violations committed by a person in Ihram (Muhrim). First, some violations require dam (a sacrificial animal, specifically a goat). Second, some violations require sadaqah (charity) in the form of half a sa' of wheat (about 1.75 kg). Third, some violations require less than half a sa' of wheat. Fourth, some violations require paying the value (qimah) of the thing violated—particularly in the case of hunting (jaza' al-sayd), where the hunter must pay the market value of the animal killed. Note that 'dam' and 'sadaqah' in this context are technical terms with specific meanings, not the general terms.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (goat) required as a penalty for certain violations of Ihram
صدقة (sadaqah): In this context, it specifically means half a sa' of wheat given as charity for a violation
صاع (sa'): A unit of volume; a sa' is approximately 3.5 kg of wheat.
قيمة (qimah): Monetary value, especially as compensation for unlawfully killing game while in Ihram

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Half a sa' of wheat
C) Feeding the poor
D) A sacrificial animal

Key Takeaway
A Muhrim's violation leads to one of four specific penalties: dam, sadaqah (half sa' wheat), less than that, or value for hunting.

Penalty Multiplication for Joint Hajj Violations
Stating that the penalty multiplies when multiple people commit the same violation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that each joint perpetrator in a Hajj violation owes a full, independent penalty and apply it to scenarios with multiple offenders.

Core Idea
Each joint perpetrator owes a complete, undivided penalty.

In Hanafi fiqh, when multiple individuals jointly commit a prohibited act during Hajj—such as killing game while in ihram—the penalty is not shared or divided. Instead, each person is fully liable for a separate penalty. This principle strengthens deterrence and upholds the sanctity of the Hajj rituals. The following passage from a classical text states this rule in a clear, axiomatic form.

Guided Path
1
State the rule from the passage
Read the Arabic carefully: 'ويتعدد الجزاء بتعدد القاتلين المجرمين'. The penalty multiplies with the multiplicity of guilty killers. Identify the key legal point: each perpetrator must pay a full penalty.
The term 'qaatil' here refers to anyone who unlawfully kills game, but the rule applies generally.
2
Identify the key terms and their implications
Focus on 'yata'addad' (multiplies) and 'jaza' (penalty). Understand that multiplication means each individual's liability is independent. The word 'bit'addud' (with the multiplicity) directly links number of people to number of penalties.
3
Explain the consequence
If two Muhrims jointly kill one deer, two full penalties are owed—one from each. The penalty amount is not halved; it is duplicated. This contrasts with some other legal systems where joint liability is shared.
Each penalty is a wajib (obligatory compensation) such as dam, sadaqah, or equivalent value.
4
Distinguish from other areas of fiqh
Note that this rule is specific to Hajj violations. In other chapters (e.g., torts, diyat), joint offenders may share liability. The ruling here is designed to preserve the sanctity of the Haram and Ihram.
The principle is derived from the need to protect the sacred precincts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۴۲۵) ويتعدد الجزاء بتعدد القاتلين المجرمين.
And the penalty multiplies with the multiplicity of the guilty killers.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage lays down a rule for joint liability in Hajj violations. If two or more people together commit a single prohibited act (e.g., they jointly kill one game animal), the penalty is not split among them; rather, each individual owes a full penalty (dam, sadaqah, or value). This is in contrast to some other areas of fiqh where liability may be divided. The term 'al-qaatileen' (killers) specifically refers to those who kill game, but the rule applies to any violation where multiple perpetrators are involved.

Key Terms
يتعدد (yata'addad): Becomes multiple, is multiplied
جزاء (jaza'): The required compensation or penalty for a violation
قاتل (qaatil): One who kills (game) while in Ihram or in the Haram

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One, divided between them
B) Two, one from each
C) None, since it was accidental
D) One, to be paid jointly

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, joint perpetrators of a Hajj violation each owe a full, undivided penalty.

Acts That Require Dam: Perfume, Dye, and Oil During Ihram
Specifying three acts by a Muhrim that necessitate a sacrificial animal (dam)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three acts by a Muhrim that necessitate dam and explain the condition of applying to a full limb.

Core Idea
Applying perfume, henna, or oil to a complete limb during Ihram obligates a dam.

In this lesson, you'll learn the specific prohibitions that trigger the most severe penalty (dam) for a Muhrim. The Hanafi school distinguishes between full-limb application and partial application, with different penalties. Understanding this threshold helps you avoid major violations in Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts
From the text and commentary, list the three actions that require dam: applying perfume (tayyib), dyeing with henna (khidhab), and applying oil (added by the commentator).
The Arabic text only mentions perfume and dyeing; oil is included in the Urdu commentary.
2
Note the condition of a 'limb'
The text specifies 'udhw' (limb). A limb is a complete body part like the arm, leg, or head. Partial application (e.g., on a finger) does not require dam.
The entire limb must be covered; the definition of 'limb' is consistent across Hanafi fiqh.
3
Recognize the actor
The Muhrim must be 'baligh' (adult). The penalty applies only to mature pilgrims.
4
Understand the penalty distinction
For full limb: dam (a goat). For less than a limb: sadaqah (half sa'). This distinction is implied by the text and clarified in the commentary.
The dam is wajib; sadaqah is a lesser penalty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۴۲۶) فالّتي توجب دما هي ما لو طيب محرم بالغ عضوا او خضب
So that which necessitates Dam is if a mature Muhrim perfumes a limb or dyes (with henna).
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage gives examples of acts that require a dam (goat) as a penalty when done by a baaligh (adult) Muhrim. Three examples are given (though only two are in the extracted Arabic; the Urdu commentary adds a third: applying oil). First, perfuming (tayyib) any complete limb. Second, dyeing (khidhaab) the head with henna, which both perfumes and covers the head. The third (from Urdu) is applying oil (like olive oil) to a limb; oil has a perfume-like effect. The key condition is that the application covers an entire limb; if less than a limb, the penalty is sadaqah (half sa').

Key Terms
طيب (tayyib): To apply perfume or any fragrant substance
خضب (khadaba): To dye, especially with henna
عضو (udhw): A limb or distinct body part
دم (dam): A goat sacrificed as penalty

Categories of Ihram Penalties and the Multiplicity Rule
Listing four penalty categories and the rule of multiplicity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four types of penalties for ihram violations and apply the Hanafi rule that each offender pays a full separate penalty.

Core Idea
Four penalties, each offender pays in full — no sharing.

In this lesson, you will learn about the four categories of penalties for violating the state of ihram. These penalties range from sacrificing a goat to paying a small amount of wheat. You will also learn an important principle: if multiple people commit the same offense, each one must pay the full penalty, not a portion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four penalty categories
Read the passage carefully. List the four types: what requires a dam (goat), what requires sadaqah (half sa' wheat), what requires less than half a sa' of wheat, and what requires paying the value (qimah) of game.
Memorize these four as the foundation of ihram penalties.
2
Understand the technical terms
Note that 'dam' always means a goat, 'sadaqah' means half a sa' of wheat, and 'badanah' means a camel. These are fixed meanings in this context.
Do not confuse with general usage.
3
Learn the multiplicity rule
The passage states: يتعدد الجزاء بتعدد القاتلين المجرمين — the penalty multiplies by the multiplicity of guilty killers. Even if only one game is killed, each hunter owes a full penalty.
The rule applies to all ihram violations, not just hunting.
4
Apply the rule to examples
Consider two pilgrims who together kill one deer. Each must pay the full value of the deer (qimah). Similarly, if two people apply perfume, each must give sadaqah.
The penalty is not split; it is multiplied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمه : (۱۴۲۵) احرام باندھنے والے قاتلوں کے متعدد ہو جانے سے جزا بھی متعدد ہوگی۔ تشریح : قاعدہ بتا رہے ہیں کہ چاہے جرم ایک ہو لیکن اگر اس جرم کو کرنے والے دو ہوں تو دو بدلے لازم ہوں گے،مثلا ایک شکار کو دو آدمیوں نے مارا تو اگر چه شکار ایک ہے لیکن دو بدلے لازم ہوں گے ۔

Chapter of Offenses. From them is what requires less than that, and from them is what requires the value, and it is the penalty of hunting. (1425) And the penalty multiplies by the multiplicity of the guilty killers. [Arabic: ...] (Urdu: Here, blood means a goat. [2] The second type is that from this offense charity becomes obligatory, such as if one applies perfume less than a limb, then charity is obligatory. Here charity means half a sa' of wheat. [3] The third type is that from this offense less than half a sa' of wheat becomes obligatory, such as if one kills a louse in the state of ihram, then less than half a sa' becomes obligatory. [4] The fourth type is that the value becomes obligatory, such as if one kills game, then in its place its value becomes obligatory. These are the four types of offenses in the state of ihram. Lexicon: blood: wherever absolute blood is mentioned, by it is meant a goat. Charity: wherever absolute charity is mentioned, by it is meant half a sa' of wheat. And wherever badanah is mentioned, there a camel is meant. And wherever something becoming obligatory is mentioned, by it is meant less than half a sa' of wheat. Translation: (1425) The penalty also becomes multiple with the multiplication of the killers in ihram. Explanation: They are stating a rule that even if the crime is one, but if there are two perpetrators, then two penalties become obligatory, for example, one game is killed by two people, then although the game is one, two penalties become obligatory. Principle: In the offenses of Hajj, the penalty multiples with the multiplicity of the offender.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage introduces the four categories of penalties for violations committed during ihram. The first type is a blood sacrifice (dam), which is a goat. The second type is charity (sadaqah), which is half a sa' of wheat. The third type is something less than half a sa' of wheat, for minor actions like killing a louse. The fourth type is paying the value (qimah) for hunting game. The text then clarifies the technical meaning of terms: 'dam' always means a goat, 'sadaqah' always means half a sa' of wheat, and 'badanah' means a camel. Next, the rule of multiplicity is stated: if multiple persons commit the same offense, each is liable for a separate penalty. For example, if two people kill one game animal, each must pay the value, so the total is doubled. This principle applies to all ihram violations.

Key Terms
دم (dam): In this text, dam means a goat (bakra) as a penalty for certain ihram violations.
صدقہ (sadaqah): In this text, sadaqah means half a sa' of wheat as a penalty.
بدنہ (badanah): Means a camel in the context of ihram penalties.
جزاء (jaza'): Penalty or compensation for violating ihram prohibitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Any blood sacrifice
B) A goat
C) A camel
D) Half a sa' of wheat

Key Takeaway
Ihram violations incur one of four fixed penalties, and multiple offenders each pay the full penalty—never a shared portion.

Acts Obligating Dam for a Muhrim
Detailed exposition of acts obligating dam with proofs and intra-Hanafi difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the acts during ihram that require a dam (blood sacrifice) and explain the evidence for each, while identifying the intra-Hanafi difference regarding olive oil.

Core Idea
Applying perfume, dyeing with henna, wearing stitched clothes, and covering the head for a full day each obligate a dam; applying oil is disputed between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

The state of ihram brings with it a set of prohibitions, and violating them entails penalties classified by severity. Among the most serious violations are those that require a dam — a sheep or goat sacrificed in compensation. This lesson examines the specific acts that trigger this obligation, drawing on the major hadith proofs and noting the intra-Hanafi dispute over whether applying olive oil counts as perfume.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts listed
Read the passage and extract the five actions that the author states obligate a dam: applying perfume (tayyib) on a limb, dyeing with henna (khadab), applying oil (olive oil, etc.), wearing stitched clothing (makhit), and covering the head (satr ra's) for a full day.
2
Examine the evidence for perfume and dye
Analyze the hadith of Ya'la ibn Umayya (Bukhari) and the hadith of Umm Salama (Tabarani). The first commands washing off perfume; the second states henna is perfume. Both establish the prohibition and thus the penalty for violation.
Understand why these hadith are chosen as proofs: they directly address the prohibition and imply compensation.
3
Examine the evidence for oil and the intra-Hanafi dispute
Look at the practice of Hasan ibn Ali (ra) and the statement of 'Ata', which indicate that olive oil is considered perfume. Then note that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) disagree, holding that olive oil is not perfume, hence no dam is required.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school; the text seems to favour Abu Hanifa's view by including oil in the list.
4
Understand the evidence for stitched clothing and head cover
Refer to the hadith of Ibn 'Umar in Bukhari and Muslim, which explicitly forbids wearing sewn garments and covering the head. The prohibition for head cover is specific to men; women are exempted.
The duration of a full day is specified for head cover to incur dam; less than a day requires only sadaqah.
5
Apply the ruling: duration and completeness matter
Note that each action must be done completely (e.g., perfume on a full limb, head cover for a full day). Partial acts may reduce the penalty to sadaqah or less.
This nuance is crucial for accurate fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۴۲۶) فالّتي توجب دما هي ما لو طيب محرم بالغ عضوا او خضب
ہے، یہاں دم سے بکری مراد ہے ۔ [۲] دوسری قسم یہ ہے کہ اس جنایت سے صدقہ لازم ہوتا ہے، جیسے ایک عضو سے کم خوشبو لگائے تو صدقہ لازم ہوگا ۔ یہاں صدقہ سے مراد ہے کہ آدھا صاع گیہوں لازم ہوگا [۳] تیسری قسم یہ ہے کہ اس جنایت سے آدھا صاع گیہوں سے کم لا زم ہو، جیسے احرام کی حالت میں جوں مار دے تو آدھا صاع گیہوں سے کم لا زم ہوتا ہے [۴] اور چوتھی قسم یہ ہے کہ
قیمت لازم ہو، جیسے شکار مار دیا تو اس کے بدلے میں اس کی قیمت لازم ہوتی ہے احرام کی حالت میں جنایت کی یہ چار قسمیں ہیں لغت : دم : جہاں جہاں بھی مطلق دم کا ذکر ہے اس سے بکری مراد ہے۔ صدقہ : اور جہاں جہاں مطلق صدقہ کا ذکر ہے اس سے آدھا صاع گیہوں مراد ہے۔ اور جہاں بدنہ کا ذکر ہے وہاں اونٹ مراد ہے۔ اور جہاں کچھ لا زم ہونے کا ذکر ہے اس سے آدھا صاع گیہوں سے کم مراد ہے۔
ترجمه : (۱۴۲۵) احرام باندھنے والے قاتلوں کے متعدد ہو جانے سے جزا بھی متعدد ہوگی۔ تشریح : قاعدہ بتا رہے ہیں کہ چاہے جرم ایک ہو لیکن اگر اس جرم کو کرنے والے دو ہوں تو دو بدلے لازم ہوں گے،مثلا ایک شکار کو دو آدمیوں نے مارا تو اگر چه شکار ایک ہے لیکن دو بدلے لازم ہوں گے ۔
اصول : جنایات حج میں مجرم کے تعدد سے بدلہ متعدد ہو جاتا ہے۔
ترجمه : (۱۴۲۶) فالّتي توجب دما هي ما لو طيب محرم بالغ عضوا او خضب
ہے، یہاں دم سے بکری مراد ہے ۔ [۲] دوسری قسم یہ ہے کہ اس جنایت سے صدقہ لازم ہوتا ہے، جیسے ایک عضو سے کم خوشبو لگائے تو صدقہ لازم ہوگا ۔ یہاں صدقہ سے مراد ہے کہ آدھا صاع گیہوں لازم ہوگا [۳] تیسری قسم یہ ہے کہ اس جنایت سے آدھا صاع گیہوں سے کم لا زم ہو، جیسے احرام کی حالت میں جوں مار دے تو آدھا صاع گیہوں سے کم لا زم ہوتا ہے [۴] اور چوتھی قسم یہ ہے کہ
قیمت لازم ہو، جیسے شکار مار دیا تو اس کے بدلے میں اس کی قیمت لازم ہوتی ہے احرام کی حالت میں جنایت کی یہ چار قسمیں ہیں لغت : دم : جہاں جہاں بھی مطلق دم کا ذکر ہے اس سے بکری مراد ہے۔ صدقہ : اور جہاں جہاں مطلق صدقہ کا ذکر ہے اس سے آدھا صاع گیہوں مراد ہے۔ اور جہاں بدنہ کا ذکر ہے وہاں اونٹ مراد ہے۔ اور جہاں کچھ لا زم ہونے کا ذکر ہے اس سے آدھا صاع گیہوں سے کم مراد ہے۔
ترجمه : (۱۴۲۵) احرام باندھنے والے قاتلوں کے متعدد ہو جانے سے جزا بھی متعدد ہوگی۔ تشریح : قاعدہ بتا رہے ہیں کہ چاہے جرم ایک ہو لیکن اگر اس جرم کو کرنے والے دو ہوں تو دو بدلے لازم ہوں گے،مثلا ایک شکار کو دو آدمیوں نے مارا تو اگر چه شکار ایک ہے لیکن دو بدلے لازم ہوں گے ۔
اصول : جنایات حج میں مجرم کے تعدد سے بدلہ متعدد ہو جاتا ہے۔
ترجمه : (۱۴۲۶) فالّتي توجب دما هي ما لو طيب محرم بالغ عضوا او خضب، او ادهن بزيت و نحوه (۱) او لبس مخيطا او ستر رأسه يوما كاملا
السائل عن العمرة؟ اخلع عنك الجبة واغسل اثر الخلوق عنك وانق الصفرة واصنع في عمرتک کما تصنع فی حجک . (بخاری شریف، باب يفعل بالعمرة ما يفعل بالحج ص ۲۴۱ نمبر ۱۷۸۹، ابواب العمرة رمسلم شریف ، باب ما یباح للمحرم ... بیان تحریم الطيب عليه ص ۳۷۳ نمبر ۲۷۹۸/۱۱۸۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ محرم کو خوشبو نہیں لگانا چاہئے ۔ (۳)
ایک دوسری حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر قال قام رجل فقال يا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ماذا تأمرنا ان نلبس صلى الله من الثياب فى الاحرام؟ فقال النبي علة لا تلبسو ا القميص ولا السراويلات و لا العمائم و لا البرانس الا أن يـكـون احــد لـيـس له نعلان فليلبس الخفين و ليقطع أسفل من الكعبين ولا تلبسوا شيئا مسه زعفران ولا
الورس لا تتنقب المرأة المحرمة و لا تلبس القفازين - (بخاری شریف ، باب ما شخصی من الطبيب لحرم والحر متہ ص ۲۹۷ نمبر ۱۸۳۸، ابواب العمرة رمسلم شریف ، باب ما یباح للمحرم .. و بیان تحریم الطیب علیه، ص ۲۸۵، نمبر ۲۷۹۱/۱۱۷۷) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ خوشبو نہیں لگانا چاہئے ۔ (۴) اور مہندی خوشبو ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ام سلمة قالت قال رسول الله الله لا تطيبي وانت محرمة و لا تمسى الحناء فانه طیب ۔ (طبرانی کبیر ، باب خولہ یعن ام سلمۃ ، ج [۲۳] ثالث و عشرون ، ص ۴۱۸ ، نمبر ۱۰۱۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مہندی خوشبو ہے۔ (۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ مہندی کا خضاب نہ لگائے ۔ عن حماد قال لا يختضب المحرم بالحناء و لا يتوضأ بدستان - (مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ، باب فی الحرم تختصب أو يتداوى بالحناء ، ج ثالث ، ص ۲۰۸، نمبر ۱۴۶۱۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ محرم مہندی سے خضاب نہ کرے، اس کی وجہ یہی ہوسکتی ہے کہ اس میں خوشبو ہے۔ (۶) زیتون کا تیل خوشبو ہے اس کے لئے یہ قول صحابی ہے۔ ان الحسن بن على كان اذا أحرم ادهن بالزيت و ادهن أصحـابـه بـالطيب أو يدهن بالطيب . (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من کان یدھن بالزبیت ، ج ثالث ،ص۳۳۲، نمبر ۱۴۸۱۳) اس قول صحابی سے معلوم ہوا کہ زیتون کا تیل خوشبو ہے۔ (۷) تیل لگانے سے دم لازم ہوگا اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ عن عطاء قال اذا وضع المحرم على شيء منه دهنا فيه طيب فعليه الكفارة - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۲۹۶ ما قالوا فیه اذاشم الریحان، ج ثالث، ص ۳۰۸ نمبر۱۴۶۱۰) اس قول تابعی میں ہے تیل لگانے سے کفارہ لازم ہوگا ۔۔ صاحبین کے یہاں زیتون کا تیل خشبو نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کے لگانے سے دم لازم نہیں ہوگا۔
لغت : طیب: طیب سے مشتق ہے، خوشبو لگانا۔ خضب : خضاب لگانا ، مہندی لگانا۔ حناء: مہندی۔ادھن : تیل لگانا۔ ترجمه : (۱۴۲۷) یا سلا ہوا کپڑا اپنے، یا پورے ایک دن سر کو چھپائے۔
تشریح : محرم کو سلا ہوا کپڑا پہنا ممنوع ہے اسی طرح مرد کے کے لئے سرڈھانکنا منوع ہے۔ اس لئے اگر پورا دن سلا ہوا کپڑا
پہنایا پوار ادن سرڈھانکا تو اس پر دم لازم ہوگا۔
(1426) That which makes obligatory a blood sacrifice is when a mature muhrim applies perfume on a limb, or dyes (with henna), or anoints with oil like olive oil, or wears stitched clothing, or covers his head for a full day. (Hadith: ...) From this hadith it is known that a muhrim should not apply perfume. (Another hadith: ...) From this hadith also it is known that perfume should not be applied. (Hadith of Umm Salama: ...) In this hadith, henna is perfume. (Athar of Hammad: ...) In this athar, the muhrim should not dye with henna, the reason being that it contains perfume. (Qawl Sahaba: ...) From this qawl sahabi it is known that olive oil is perfume. (Qawl Tabi'i: ...) In this qawl tabi'i, applying oil necessitates kaffarah. According to the Sahibayn, olive oil is not perfume, so applying it does not require dam. Lexicon: Tayyib: derived from tayyib, applying perfume. Khadab: applying dye, applying henna. Hinna': henna. Idhan: applying oil. Translation: (1427) Or wearing stitched clothing, or covering his head for a full day. Explanation: It is prohibited for the muhrim to wear stitched clothing, and similarly it is prohibited for a man to cover his head. Therefore, if he wears stitched clothing or covers his head for a full day, then dam becomes obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the first category of ihram violations that require a dam (blood sacrifice). It lists specific actions: applying perfume on a complete limb, dyeing hair with henna, applying scented oil like olive oil, wearing stitched garments, and covering the head for an entire day. The author then provides extensive textual evidence. The prohibition of perfume is established by the hadith of Ya'la ibn Umayya where the Prophet (ﷺ) ordered a man to remove a perfumed garment and wash off the scent. The prohibition of henna is supported by the hadith of Umm Salama that henna is perfume, and the athar of Hammad prohibiting henna for a muhrim. For olive oil, the author cites the practice of Hasan ibn 'Ali (رضي الله عنه) anointing with oil, indicating it is perfume, and the statement of 'Ata' that applying oil requires expiation. However, the author notes that Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that olive oil is not perfume, so applying it does not require dam. This is an intra-Hanafi difference. The text then covers the prohibition of stitched clothing and covering the head, citing the well-known hadith from Bukhari and Muslim about what a muhrim may wear. The key point is that any of these actions, if done deliberately, necessitates a dam. The duration of a full day is specified for covering the head; less than a day may require sadaqah.

Key Terms
طیب (tayyib): Perfume; applying any scented substance to the body.
خضب (khadab): Dyeing with henna or similar substances.
مخيط (makhit): Stitched garment; clothing sewn in the usual manner.
ستر رأس (satr ra's): Covering the head; for men only, as women already cover it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following requires a blood sacrifice (dam) for a muhrim?
A) Applying perfume on less than a limb
B) Wearing stitched clothing for a full day
C) Killing a louse
D) Applying olive oil according to the Sahibayn

Key Takeaway
During ihram, applying perfume (including henna and, according to Abu Hanifa, olive oil) on a full limb, wearing stitched clothing, and covering the head for a full day each necessitate a dam; lesser violations require sadaqah.

Ruling on Perfume, Henna, and Oil for the Muhrim
Prohibits perfume, henna, and oil for muhrim with proofs and a dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on applying perfume, henna, and olive oil during ihram, cite the primary proofs, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on olive oil.

Core Idea
Perfume, henna, and (per Abu Hanifa) olive oil are prohibited for the muhrim, requiring a dam if violated.

In this lesson, we explore the prohibitions of pleasant-smelling substances for the muhrim. The author begins with a general hadith on removing perfume, then specifically addresses henna through the hadith of Umm Salamah, and finally examines the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding olive oil. This passage is a ruling-with-proof that also highlights the Hanafi method of using sahabi sayings and tabi'i fatwas as evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is applying perfume, henna, or oil to the body while in ihram. The ruling is haram, and these violations require a dam (kaffarah) as compensation.
The primary prohibition is for the muhrim, male or female.
2
Locate the dalil for perfume
The author cites a hadith from Bukhari and Muslim where the Prophet ﷺ tells a man in ihram to remove his cloak and wash off the yellow dye, indicating that any perfumed substance is prohibited.
The hadith is ahad, so the ruling is based on zanni evidence.
3
Trace the proof for henna
The hadith of Umm Salamah explicitly states 'henna is perfume', and the athar from Hammad prohibits dyeing with henna. These prove henna is included in the prohibition.
The athar does not specify a penalty, but the hadith implies it.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on olive oil
Abu Hanifa said olive oil is perfume; applying it requires a dam. The Sahibayn said olive oil is not a perfume, so no dam is needed.
This difference is found in the Nawadir.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author presents stronger evidence for Abu Hanifa's view: a sahabi action (Hasan bin Ali) and a tabi'i fatwa (Ata). Thus the mufta bihi is that olive oil is a perfume and requires a dam.
The tarjih is based on the weight of evidence, not just authority.

رأسه بحناء او ادهن بزيت و نحوه (۱) او لبس مخيطا او ستر رأسه يوما كاملا السائل عن العمرة؟ اخلع عنك الجبة واغسل اثر الخلوق عنك وانق الصفرة واصنع في عمرتک کما تصنع فی حجک . (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من کان یدھن بالزبیت ، ج ثالث ،ص۳۳۲، نمبر ۱۴۸۱۳) اس قول صحابی سے معلوم ہوا کہ زیتون کا تیل خوشبو ہے۔ (۷) تیل لگانے سے دم لازم ہوگا اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ عن عطاء قال اذا وضع المحرم على شيء منه دهنا فيه طيب فعليه الكفارة - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۲۹۶ ما قالوا فیه اذاشم الریحان، ج ثالث، ص ۳۰۸ نمبر۱۴۶۱۰) اس قول تابعی میں ہے تیل لگانے سے کفارہ لازم ہوگا ۔۔ صاحبین کے یہاں زیتون کا تیل خشبو نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کے لگانے سے دم لازم نہیں ہوگا۔
