Chapter of Offences. He applies henna to his head or applies oil like olive oil and the like (1) or wears sewn clothes or covers his head a full day. The questioner about Umrah? Take off your cloak and wash off the effect of the yellow dye and cleanse the yellowness and do in your Umrah as you do in your Hajj. (Bukhari, Bab yaf'alu bil-'umrati ma yaf'alu bil-hajj, p. 241, no. 1789; Muslim, Bab ma yabahu lil-muhrim... bayan tahrim al-tayyib 'alayh, p. 373, no. 2798/1180) From this hadith it became known that the muhrim should not apply perfume. (3) Another hadith: 'Abdullah bin 'Umar said a man stood and said O Messenger of Allah what do you command us to wear from garments in ihram? The Prophet said: Do not wear shirts, trousers, turbans, hooded cloaks unless one does not have sandals then he may wear khuffs and cut them below the ankles, and do not wear anything touched by saffron or wars, and the woman in ihram should not cover her face or wear gloves. (Bukhari, Bab ma yajtani min al-tayyib lil-muhrim wa al-muhrimah, p. 297, no. 1838; Muslim, Bab ma yabahu lil-muhrim... wa bayan tahrim al-tayyib 'alayh, p. 285, no. 2791/1177) From this hadith also it is known that perfume should not be applied. (4) And henna is perfume, for this there is a hadith: Umm Salamah said the Messenger of Allah said: Do not apply perfume while in ihram and do not touch henna for it is perfume. (Tabarani al-Kabir, Bab Khawlah ya'ni Umm Salamah, vol. 23, p. 418, no. 1012) In this hadith henna is perfume. (5) In this athar: The muhrim should not dye with henna. Hammad said: The muhrim should not dye with henna nor perform wudu with dust. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab fi al-muhrim yakhdabu aw yatadawa bil-hinna, vol. 3, p. 208, no. 14613) In this athar the muhrim should not dye with henna, the reason could be that it contains perfume. (6) Olive oil is perfume, for this there is a saying of a Sahabi: Al-Hasan bin 'Ali when he assumed ihram would apply olive oil and would apply perfume to his companions or apply perfume. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab man kana yaddahan bi al-zayt, vol. 3, p. 332, no. 14813) From this saying of a Sahabi it is known that olive oil is perfume. (7) Applying oil necessitates a dam, for this there is a saying of a Tabi'i: 'Ata said: If the muhrim places on something of him oil containing perfume, then upon him is the expiation. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 296 ma qalu fihi idha shamma al-rayhan, vol. 3, p. 308, no. 14610) In this saying of a Tabi'i applying oil necessitates kaffarah. According to the Sahibayn, olive oil is not perfume, therefore applying it does not necessitate a dam. Vocabulary: Tayyib: derived from tayyib, applying perfume. Khadab: applying dye, applying henna. Hinna: henna. Idhan: applying oil.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof on the prohibition of perfume for the muhrim. It opens with a reference to prohibitions including applying henna, oil, sewn clothes, and covering the head. The author then cites a hadith from Bukhari and Muslim where the Prophet ﷺ instructs a man to remove his cloak and wash off a yellow dye, indicating that perfumed substances are prohibited. Further hadith are quoted, including the well-known hadith of Ibn 'Umar listing prohibited garments and items touched by saffron or wars, which also covers perfume. The author then explicitly addresses henna through the hadith of Umm Salamah, calling henna a perfume. A narration from Hammad upholds the prohibition of dyeing with henna during ihram. The discussion then turns to olive oil: the author provides a sahabi saying (from Hasan bin Ali) and a tabi'i saying (from Ata) to argue that olive oil is a perfume and that applying it requires a dam. The passage concludes by noting that the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree, holding that olive oil is not perfume and thus no dam is required. The vocabulary section defines key Arabic terms. The author's arrangement gives stronger evidentiary support to Abu Hanifa's position, implying it is the relied-upon view.

Key Terms
طيب (tayyib): perfume, anything with a pleasant scent applied for fragrance
خضب (khadab): to dye, specifically applying henna to hair
حناء (hinna'): henna, a plant used as a dye and considered a perfume by Abu Hanifa
ادھن (idhan): to apply oil (e.g., olive oil) to the body

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on applying olive oil for a muhrim according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) Permissible, no penalty
B) Prohibited, requires a dam
C) Recommended
D) Makruh tanzihi

Key Takeaway
Perfume, henna, and (per Abu Hanifa) olive oil are forbidden for the muhrim; the mufta bihi requires a dam for any of these violations.

Prohibitions of Ihram: Sewn Clothes and Head Covering
Prohibits two acts and links penalty to full-day duration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two prohibited acts for a muhrim and identify the condition (full day) that triggers the obligation of a dam.

Core Idea
Wearing sewn clothes or covering the head for a full day in ihram makes dam wajib.

When a Muslim enters ihram for Hajj or Umrah, certain normal actions become prohibited. This lesson examines two such prohibitions: wearing sewn garments and covering the head. The Hanafi school specifies that these acts are haram, and if done for an entire day, a penalty (dam) becomes obligatory. Understanding the exact condition—a full day—is essential to apply the ruling correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act
Read the passage: it mentions 'wearing sewn clothes' and 'covering the head'. Both are actions that a muhrim must avoid. Recognize that these are distinct prohibitions.
Sewn clothes refer to garments tailored to fit the body, like shirts and trousers.
2
Determine the ruling for each act
The commentary clearly states both are 'mamnu' (prohibited). In Hanafi fiqh, this means the act is haram. So if done intentionally without excuse, it's a sin.
Prohibition applies equally to both acts.
3
Identify the condition for the penalty
The passage specifies that the penalty (dam) becomes wajib only if the act is done 'for a full day'. This is a key condition: a momentary or partial act may not require a dam, though it may still be sinful.
‘Full day’ means from dawn to sunset or the entire day of normal activity.
4
Apply the rule to a scenario
Consider a muhrim who wears a sewn shirt for a few hours in the morning but removes it before noon. According to this passage, no dam is due because the condition of a full day is not met. However, he has committed a sin and should seek repentance.
The ruling emphasizes the threshold of a complete day for the penalty.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools may define the threshold differently or require expiation for any violation regardless of duration. The Hanafi specificity here is precise.
This highlights the importance of madhhab-specific detail.

تشریح : محرم کو سلا ہوا کپڑا پہنا ممنوع ہے اسی طرح مرد کے لئے سرڈھانکنا منوع ہے۔ اس لئے اگر پورا دن سلا ہوا کپڑا پہنایا پوار ادن سرڈھانکا تو اس پر دم لازم ہوگا۔

Commentary
This is a ruling statement (matn) along with its commentary. The numbered point (1427) states two prohibitions: wearing sewn garments and covering the head for a full day. The commentary clarifies that both acts are prohibited (mamnu') for the muhrim, and if done for a full day, a dam (penalty) becomes wajib. The commentary does not provide explicit proof here, but references to hadith are given later in the surrounding passages.

Key Terms
دم (dam): a penalty (sacrifice of an animal) for violating a prohibition of ihram
محرم (muhrim): a person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah
سلا ہوا کپڑا (sila hua kapra): sewn clothes, i.e., garments tailored to the body like shirts, trousers, etc.

D) The clothes must cover the entire body

Key Takeaway
A muhrim must avoid sewn clothes and head covering; a full-day violation incurs a wajib dam.

Ruling on Shaving Head and Body Hair During Ihram
Ruling on shaving specific body parts during ihram with proofs from Quran and hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five prohibited acts of shaving during ihram and identify that each requires a dam, with evidence from the Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
Shaving any of your head, armpit, pubic area, or neck during ihram without necessity is prohibited and requires a dam.

During Hajj or Umrah, a pilgrim in ihram must avoid certain acts, including shaving specific hair. This lesson covers five such acts and the penalty for each, based on clear textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
List the five acts of shaving mentioned: quarter of the head, cupping site, one armpit, pubic area, and neck. Each is haram if done without necessity and requires a dam.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is Quran 2:196, which prohibits shaving the head until the sacrifice reaches its place and allows fidyah only for illness. Hadiths of Ibn 'Umar, Ibn 'Abbas, and Ka'b bin 'Ujrah further clarify the prohibition.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quran's command 'do not shave your heads' coupled with the exception for illness implies that shaving without necessity incurs a penalty (dam). The hadiths extend this to covering the head and other body parts.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other madhhabs may have different thresholds (e.g., requiring full head shave for dam) or different penalties. The Hanafi school treats quarter head as equivalent to full head.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is considered the relied-upon (mufta bihi) based on zahir al-riwayah; it holds that each of the five acts requires one dam, with no distinction between quarter and full head.

Chapter of Offences. (1428) Or he shaves a quarter of his head, or the place of cupping, or one of his armpits, or his pubic area, or his neck. Evidence: (1) The prohibition of wearing sewn clothes and covering the head is in this hadith: 'Abdullah bin 'Umar said a man stood and said O Messenger of Allah what do you command us to wear... [hadith] ... From this hadith, all the garments prohibited are sewn, so wearing sewn clothes is prohibited. And do not wear a turban or hooded cloak - from this it is understood that covering the head is prohibited. (2) Another hadith also shows covering the head is prohibited: Ibn 'Abbas said while a man was standing with the Prophet at 'Arafah, he fell from his mount and died, and the Prophet said: Wash him with water and lotus leaves, shroud him in two garments, do not apply perfume, do not cover his head, for Allah will raise him on the Day of Judgment in talbiyah. (Bukhari, Bab al-muhrim yamutu bi 'Arafah, p. 249, no. 1850) In this hadith, covering the head is prohibited for the muhrim. Translation: (1428) Or he shaves a quarter of his head, or the place of cupping, or one armpit, or pubic hair, or the hair of the neck. Commentary: A quarter of the head is like the whole head because people shave a quarter. So shaving a quarter of the head requires a dam, similarly shaving the whole head requires one dam. Or shaving the place of cupping requires a dam, or shaving an armpit, or pubic hair, or neck hair - each is shaving a single limb, so each requires one dam. Evidence (1) In the verse: 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah, but if you are prevented, then what is available of sacrificial animals, and do not shave your heads until the offering reaches its place. And whoever among you is ill or has an injury to his head, then a compensation of fasting or charity or sacrifice.' (Surah Al-Baqarah 2:196) This verse indicates that if there is a necessity due to illness, then compensation is due for shaving the head. But if there is no necessity, then only a sacrificial animal is due. (2) There is an indication in this hadith: 'Abdullah bin Ma'qil said I sat with Ka'b bin 'Ujrah and asked him about the compensation. He said it was revealed specifically for me but applies generally to you. I was carried to the Messenger of Allah while lice were falling on my face. He said: I did not think the pain had reached what I see. Can you find a sheep? I said no. He said: Fast three days, or feed six needy persons, each half a sa'. (Bukhari, Bab al-it'am fi al-fidyah nisf sa', p. 292)
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the prohibition of shaving specific areas during ihram. It begins with the matn (point 1428) listing five prohibited acts: shaving a quarter of the head, the cupping site, one armpit, the pubic area, and the neck. The 'evidence' (wajh) first cites the well-known hadith of Ibn 'Umar regarding sewn clothes and covering the head, linking the prohibition of head covering to shaving (since shaving removes hair that is meant to be covered). A second hadith from Ibn 'Abbas reinforces that covering the head is prohibited, even for a deceased muhrim. The commentary then translates and explains the matn: each of these acts requires a dam, as they are considered shaving a limb. The author then provides two additional proofs: the Quranic verse (2:196) about compensation for shaving the head due to illness, and the hadith of Ka'b bin 'Ujrah, which clarifies that if there is no necessity, a sacrifice is required. The passage thus establishes that intentionally shaving these areas without necessity incurs a dam.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): to shave; specifically shaving hair from the head or body
محجم (mahjam): the place of cupping (where a cup is applied for bloodletting)
فدية (fidyah): compensation for violating an ihram prohibition, consisting of fasting, charity, or sacrifice
دم (dam): a sacrificial animal required as penalty for violating an ihram prohibition without necessity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, what is the penalty for a muhrim who shaves his armpit without any necessity?
A) Nothing, as it is permissible
B) A dam
C) Fasting three days
D) Feeding six poor persons

Key Takeaway
Shaving even a quarter of the head or any of the five listed body parts during ihram without necessity incurs a wajib dam.

Shaving Head and Body Parts in Ihram Requires Dam
Ruling on shaving quarter head, cupping site, armpit, pubic area, or neck

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on shaving specific body parts during ihram and apply the principle that shaving a full limb requires one dam while partial shaving requires half sa' of wheat sadaqah.

Core Idea
Shaving any entire limb in ihram requires one dam; partial shaving requires half a sa' of wheat sadaqah.

This lesson explores the compensation (dam) required when a pilgrim in ihram shaves certain body parts. The text specifies that shaving a quarter of the head, the cupping site, armpit, pubic area, or neck each triggers a specific penalty. Understanding these rules helps pilgrims avoid major violations and know the required expiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act and its compensation
Determine which acts of shaving during ihram are addressed in the passage and what compensation (dam or sadaqah) is required for each.
The act is shaving hair from specific body parts while in the state of ihram.
2
Distinguish between shaving the entire head versus a quarter
Note that shaving the whole head requires one dam, while shaving only a quarter also requires one dam because a quarter is treated as the entire head for this ruling.
The text explicitly states that shaving a quarter of the head is like shaving the whole head.
3
Recognize the extension to other limbs
Understand that the same ruling applies to shaving the armpit, pubic area, cupping site, and neck. Shaving any one of these entirely requires one dam.
The text lists these explicitly and provides a proof from Imam Malik's Muwatta.
4
Locate the dalil and explain the wajh al-dalalah
Examine the Quranic verse (2:196) and the hadith of Ka'b ibn Ujrah. Explain how these proofs establish the obligation of compensation for shaving hair during ihram.
The verse addresses necessity (fidyah), while the hadith and other sources extend the ruling to non-necessity (dam).
5
Apply the principle of full limb vs. part
Use the text's principle: shaving the entire limb (pura uzv) requires one dam; shaving only some (ba'z) requires half sa' of wheat as sadaqah. Apply this to various scenarios.
This principle is stated at the end of the passage: 'Usul: Pur uzv ke liye ek dam, aur ba'z ke liye aadha sa' gheeun.'

Source Text

(1428) او حلق ربع رأسه او محجمه او احد ابطيه او عانته او رقبته وجه : (۱) سلا ہوا کپڑا پہنے اور سرڈھانکنے کی ممانعت اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر قال قام رجل فقال يا رسول الله ماذا تأمرنا ان نلبس من الثياب في الاحرام؟ فقال النبي لا تلبسوا القميص ولا السراويلات ولا العمائم ولا البرانس الا ان يكون احد ليست له نعلان فليلبس الخفين وليقطع اسفل من الكعبين ولا تلبسوا شيئا مسه زعفران ولا الورس ولا تتنقب المرأة المحرمة ولا تلبس القفازين (بخاری شریف، باب ما یفهم من الطيب للمحرم والحرمة ص ۲۴۸ نمبر ۱۸۳۸؛ مسلم شریف، باب ما یباح للمحرم بحج او عمرة البسه ص ۳۷۲ نمبر ۲۷۹۱/۱۱۷) اس حدیث میں جتنے کپڑے پہنا ممنوع قرار دیا ہے وہ سب سلے ہوئے ہیں اس لئے سلے ہوئے کپڑے پہنا ممنوع ہے۔ اور عمامہ نہ پہنو اور برنس ٹوپی نہ پہنو اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ سر ڈھانکنا ممنوع ہے (۲) ایک دوسری حدیث سے بھی سرڈھانکناممنوع معلوم ہوتا ہے وہ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال بينما رجل واقف مع النبي بعرفة اذ وقع عن راحلته فوقصته او قال فاوقصته فقال النبي اغسلوه بماء وسدر وكفنوه في ثوبين ولا تمسوه طيبا ولا تخمروا رأسه ولا تحنطوه فان الله يبعثه يوم القيامة ملبيا (بخاری شریف، باب الحرم يموت بعرفة ص ۲۴۹، نمبر۱۸۵۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ محرم کے لئے سرڈھانکنا ممنوع ہے۔

ترجمه: (۱۴۲۸) یا چوتھائی سرمنڈ والے، یا پچھنا کی جگہ کو، یا ایک بغل کو ، یا زیر ناف بال کو، یا گردن کو منڈوائے۔ تشریح: چوتھائی سرکل سر کے حکم میں ہے، کیونکہ لوگ چوتھائی سر کو مونڈ واتے ہیں، اس لئے چوتھائی سرمنڈ والے تو دم لازم ہوگا، اسی طرح کل سرمنڈ والے تو ایک دم لازم ہو گا۔ یا پچھنا کی جگہ کو مونڈے تو دم لازم ہوگا، یا بغل کو مونڈے، یا زیر ناف بال کو مونڈے، یا گردن کے بال کو مونڈے، تو یہ ایک عضو کو مونڈنا ہے اس لئے سب میں ایک ایک دم لازم ہوگا۔

وجه (۱) آیت میں ہے۔ {وَأَتِمُّوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلَّهِ فَإِنْ أُحْصِرْتُمْ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْيِ وَلَا تَحْلِقُوا رُءُوسَكُمْ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الْهَدْيُ مَحِلَّهُ فَمَنْ كَانَ مِنْكُمْ مَرِيضًا أَوْ بِهِ أَذًى مِنْ رَأْسِهِ فَفِدْيَةٌ مِنْ صِيَامٍ أَوْ صَدَقَةٍ أَوْ نُسُكٍ} (آیت ۱۹۶، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ سر میں تکلیف ہو اور سر منڈوانے کی ضرورت پڑے تو سرمنڈ والے اور روزہ یا صدقہ یا ہدی میں سے کچھ ادا کرے۔ لیکن یہ اس وقت ہے جبکہ مجبوری ہو۔ لیکن اگر مجبوری نہ ہو اور سرمنڈ والیا تو ہدی ہی دینا ہوگا۔ (۲) اس کا اشارہ اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن معقل قال جلست الى كعب بن عجرة فسألته عن الفدية فقال نزلت في خاصة وهي لكم عامة حملت الى رسول الله والقمل يتناثر على وجهى فقال ما كنت ارى الوجع بلغ بك ما ارى او ما كنت ارى الجهد بلغ ما ارى تجد شاة؟ فقلت لا قال فصم ثلثة ایام او اطعام ستة مساكين لكل مسكين نصف صاع (بخاری شریف، باب الاطعام في الفدية نصف صاع، ص۲۹۲)

نمبر ۱۸۱۶ ر مسلم شریف، باب جواز حلق الرأس للحرم اذا کان به اذی، ص ۱۵۰۰، نمبر ۲۸۸۳/۱۲۰۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سر منڈوانے پر دم لازم ہوگا۔ (۳) بغل وغیرہ کا بال مونڈوانے پر دم لازم ہوگا اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ قال مالک و من نتف شعرا من انفه او ابطه او طلى جسده بنورة او يحلق عن شجة في رأسه لضرورة او يحلق قفاه لموضع المحاجم وهو محرم ناسيا او جاهلا ان من فعل شيئا من ذلك فعليه في ذلك كله فدية ولا ينبغي له ان يحلق موضع المحاجم (موطا امام مالک، باب فدیہ من حلق قبل ان تخرص ۴۵۰) اس اثر میں ہے کہ کسی عضو کو حلق کرایا تو اس پر فدیہ ہے۔

اصول: پورا عضو حلق کرائے تو ایک دم لازم ہوگا۔ اور بعض ہو تو آدھا صاع گیہوں صدقہ لازم ہوگا۔ نوٹ: ہدی کو حرم میں ذبح کرنا ضروری ہوگا۔ کیونکہ آیت میں ہے۔ {هَدْياً بَالِغَ الْكَعْبَةِ} (آیت ۹۵ سورۃ المائدۃ ۵) اس لئے ان ہدی کو حدود حرم میں ہی ذبح کرنا ہوگا۔
Chapter of Transgressions. (1428) Or if he shaves a quarter of his head, or the place of cupping, or one of his armpits, or his pubic area, or his neck. Explanation: (1) The prohibition of wearing sewn garments and covering the head is in this hadith: From Abdullah ibn Umar that a man asked the Prophet about garments for ihram. The Prophet forbade shirts, trousers, turbans, hooded cloaks, etc. This indicates covering the head is prohibited. (2) Another hadith from Ibn Abbas: a muhrim died at Arafat, the Prophet ordered not to cover his head. Translation: (1428) Or if he shaves a quarter of his head, or the cupping spot, or one armpit, or pubic hair, or neck hair. Explanation: Shaving a quarter of the head is like shaving the whole head, so dam is required. Similarly for each limb, one dam. Proof (1): Quran 2:196: ‘And complete the Hajj and Umrah… if any of you is ill or has an ailment of the head, then a ransom of fasting, charity, or sacrifice.’ If no necessity, then a sacrifice (hady) is required. (2) Hadith of Ka’b ibn Ujrah: the Prophet told him to fast three days or feed six poor persons when he shaved due to lice. This shows dam is required. (3) Saying of Malik: one who plucks hair from nose or armpit, or shaves a wound or nape for cupping, must pay fidyah. Principle: Shaving the whole limb requires one dam; part requires half a sa’ of wheat charity. Note: The hady must be slaughtered within the Haram based on Quran 5:95.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs on the compensation (dam) required for shaving certain body parts while in ihram. The author enumerates specific actions: shaving a quarter of the head, the cupping spot, an armpit, pubic hair, or neck hair. The key principle is that shaving an entire limb (like a whole arm or leg) requires one dam, while shaving part of it requires half a sa' of wheat as sadaqah. The proofs include the Quranic verse (2:196) addressing shaving the head due to illness, and the hadith of Ka'b ibn Ujrah confirming the ransom. The author also cites a hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar prohibiting sewn garments and covering the head, establishing the prohibition of covering the head. The Maliki narration extends the ruling to other body parts. The note emphasizes that the dam must be slaughtered within the Haram based on the verse 'hadyan baligha al-Ka'bah'. This is a detailed exposition of a specific ruling within the fiqh of Hajj.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice, specifically a sheep or goat, required as compensation for certain violations during ihram.
فدیہ (fidyah): Ransom or compensation, which can be fasting, charity, or sacrifice, for shaving hair during ihram.
حلق (halq): Shaving or removing hair, the action triggering compensation in this ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a muhrim shaves his entire head without necessity?
A) No compensation
B) One dam required
C) Half sa' of wheat charity
D) Fasting three days

Key Takeaway
Shaving any entire limb in ihram without necessity requires one dam; shaving only part requires half a sa' of wheat sadaqah.

Cutting Nails in Ihram and the Rule of Tadakhul
Ruling on cutting fingernails and toenails in ihram with tadakhul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cutting nails in ihram and apply the principle of tadakhul to determine the required compensation.

Core Idea
One dam for all nail cuts in one session due to tadakhul.

This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling on cutting fingernails and toenails while in the state of ihram. The key principle is tadakhul (overlap), which means multiple similar violations in one session incur only one compensation. We will examine the proofs from the hadith of Ibn Umar and the athar of Hasan and Ata.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is cutting fingernails and/or toenails while in ihram. The ruling: it is prohibited (haram) and if done, a dam (slaughter of a sheep) is wajib as compensation.
The prohibition derives from the requirement for a muhrim to remain disheveled (sha'ath wa tafal).
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet (s) said Hajj is dishevelment and lack of cleanliness. Additional evidence: the athar from Hasan and Ata distinguishing cutting a broken nail (no penalty) vs. cutting an unbroken nail (dam).
These are from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah and Muwatta Malik.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith establishes that a muhrim must maintain dishevelment. Cutting nails removes dishevelment and provides comfort, which contradicts the required state. Therefore, compensation is required.
The athar from Hasan and Ata directly state: 'if he clips it before breaking, then dam.'
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school generally does not apply tadakhul for nails; they may require separate fidyah for each nail. The Hanafi school applies tadakhul for multiple cuts in the same session.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the principle that multiple violations of the same type in one sitting merge into a single compensation. This is supported by the athar of Ata which implies tadakhul, and by the general concept of tadakhul in ihram violations.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah confirms tadakhul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۴۲۹) او دونوں ہاتھ اور پیر کے ناخن کو ایک مجلس میں کاٹے ، یا ایک ہاتھ یا ایک پیر کے ناخن کو کاٹ لے۔ تشریح : ایک ہاتھ میں پانچ انگلیاں ہوتی ہیں۔ اور دونوں ہاتھوں اور دونوں پاؤں کے ہیں انگلیاں ہیں ، اب بیسوں انگلیوں کے ناخن کاٹے تب بھی ایک ہی دم لازم ہوگا اور تداخل ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر ایک ہاتھ کے پانچوں انگلیوں کے ناخن کاٹے تب بھی ایک دم لازم ہوگا۔

وجه : (۱) ناخن کاٹنا پراگندگی کے خلاف ہے، اور ارتفاق کامل حاصل کیا اس لئے دم لازم ہو گا ۔ (۲) اس قول قول تابعی میں ہے عن الحسن و عطاء قال اذا انكسر ظفره قلمه من حيث انكسر ، و ليس عليه شيء فان قلمه من قبل ان انكسر فعليه دم ۔ (مصنف ابن ابى هبية ، باب في الحرم ينقص ظفره ويبط الجرح ، ج ثالث ص ۱۲۹ نمبر ۱۳۷۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ناخن ٹوٹنے سے پہلے اس کو کاٹ دے تو اس پر دم ہے۔ (۲) اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ قال مالك لا يصلح للمحرم ان ينتنف من شعره شيئا ولا يحلقه ولا يقصره حتى يحل الا ان يصيبه اذى فى رأسه فعليه فدية كما امره الله ولا يصلح له ان يقلم اظفاره ولا يقتل قمله ( موطا امام مالک، باب فدية من حلق قبل ان بحر ،ص۴۵۰ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ناخن نہ کاٹے ۔ (۳) اور اس حدیث میں ہے کہ محرم کو پراگندہ ہونا چاہئے ۔ عن ابن عمر قال قام رجل الى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال يا رسول الله ! ما يوجب الحج ؟ قال الزاد و الراحلة قال يا رسول الله ! فما الحج ؟قال الشعث و التفل . (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب فضل دعاء الحاج ،ص ۴۱۹، نمبر ۲۸۹۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حاجی کو پراگندہ ہونا چاہئے ۔ (۴) اور ہیں انگلیوں کے ناخن کاٹے تو تداخل ہو جائے گا اسکی دلیل قول تابعی ہے۔ عن عطاء انه سئل عن المحرم يواقع ثم يعود
Translation: (1429) Or if he cuts the nails of both hands and feet in one gathering, or cuts the nails of one hand or one foot. Explanation: One hand has five fingers. Both hands and both feet total twenty nails. If he cuts all twenty nails, still one dam is required and tadakhul (overlap) applies. If he cuts the five nails of one hand, also one dam. Proof: (1) Cutting nails opposes dishevelment, and he obtained complete benefit, so dam is required. (2) From Hasan and Ata: If his nail breaks, he may clip it from the broken part, no penalty; if he clips it before breaking, then dam. (3) Malik said: It is not proper for a muhrim to pluck, shave, or cut hair until he exits ihram, unless he has pain in his head; also not proper to cut nails or kill lice. (4) Hadith of Ibn Umar: The Prophet said Hajj is dishevelment (sha'ath) and lack of cleanliness (tafal). (5) And the overlapping of nails cut is evidenced by the saying of Ata when asked about a muhrim who had intercourse and returns...
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on cutting nails while in ihram. The ruling is that cutting any nails, whether all twenty or just one hand's, requires one dam. The principle of tadakhul (overlap) applies: multiple acts of the same type incur only one compensation if done in one session. The proofs include the athar from Hasan and Ata distinguishing broken vs. unbroken nails, and the hadith emphasizing that a muhrim should remain disheveled (sha'ath wa tafal). Cutting nails contradicts this state, so compensation is required. The text is incomplete at the end, but the basic ruling is clear.

Key Terms
تداخل (tadakhul): Overlap/merging of obligations; if multiple violations occur in one session, only one compensation is required.
شعث (sha'ath): Dishevelment, unkempt hair and appearance; a required state for the muhrim.
تفل (tafal): Lack of cleanliness, being dusty; part of the description of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many dams are required if a muhrim cuts all twenty nails in one sitting?
A) Twenty dams
B) Five dams (one per hand/foot pair)
C) One dam
D) No dam if it was unintentional

Key Takeaway
Cutting nails in ihram requires one dam per session due to the principle of tadakhul.

Cutting Nails in Ihram: Penalty and Tadakhul
Ruling on cutting nails in ihram with proofs and tadakhul principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cutting nails in ihram, distinguish between full-limb and partial cutting, and apply the principle of tadakhul.

Core Idea
Cutting all nails of a single limb in ihram requires one dam; tadakhul merges multiple violations into one penalty.

When a pilgrim in ihram cuts his fingernails or toenails, he violates the required state of dishevelment. The Hanafi school specifies a penalty that depends on whether he cuts a complete limb or only part of it. This lesson examines the ruling, the proofs from hadith and statements of the Salaf, and the principle of tadakhul (intercession) that consolidates penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine that cutting nails while in ihram is a jinayah (violation) that incurs a wajib penalty.
The ruling is derived from the requirement for a muhrim to remain disheveled.
2
Distinguish full limb vs. partial
Cutting all nails of one hand or foot (a full limb) requires one dam. Cutting less than a full limb requires half a sa' of wheat as sadaqah.
A hand or foot is considered a complete limb.
3
Understand tadakhul
If multiple nails are cut in one sitting, penalties merge. Cutting all twenty nails of both hands and feet in one sitting still requires only one dam.
Tadakhul applies to similar violations of the same type in one session.
4
Examine the proofs
The hadith of Ibn Umar emphasizes dishevelment. Reports from Tabi'un (Hasan, Ata) and Imam Malik prohibit nail cutting. The hadith supports the general principle.
The main proof is the hadith: 'Hajj is disheveled and dusty.'
5
Note cross-madhhab dimension
The Maliki school also prohibits nail cutting, but the penalty details may differ. Both agree it is a violation.
The source quotes Malik's Muwatta.

(۱۴۲۹) او قص اظفار يديه ورجليه بمجلس او يدا او رجلا
اصول : پورا عضو حلق کرائے تو ایک دم لازم ہوگا۔ اور بعض ہو تو آدھا صاع گیہوں صدقہ لازم ہوگا۔ نوٹ : ہدی کو حرم میں ذبح کرنا ضروری ہوگا۔ کیونکہ آیت میں ہے۔ هديا بالغ الكعبة (آیت ۹۵ سورۃ المائدۃ ۵) اس لئے ان ہدی کو حدود حرم میں ہی ذبح کرنا ہوگا۔ ترجمه : (۱۴۲۹) یا دونوں ہاتھ اور پیر کے ناخن کو ایک مجلس میں کاٹے ، یا ایک ہاتھ یا ایک پیر کے ناخن کو کاٹ لے۔ تشریح : ایک ہاتھ میں پانچ انگلیاں ہوتی ہیں۔ اور دونوں ہاتھوں اور دونوں پاؤں کے ہیں انگلیاں ہیں ، اب بیسوں انگلیوں کے ناخن کاٹے تب بھی ایک ہی دم لازم ہوگا اور تداخل ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر ایک ہاتھ کے پانچوں انگلیوں کے ناخن کاٹے تب بھی ایک دم لازم ہوگا۔
وجه : (۱) ناخن کاٹنا پراگندگی کے خلاف ہے، اور ارتفاق کامل حاصل کیا اس لئے دم لازم ہو گا ۔ (۲) اس قول قول تابعی میں ہے عن الحسن و عطاء قال اذا انكسر ظفره قلمه من حيث انكسر ، و ليس عليه شيء فان قلمه من قبل ان انكسر فعليه دم ۔ (مصنف ابن ابى هبية ، باب في الحرم ينقص ظفره ويبط الجرح ، ج ثالث ص ۱۲۹ نمبر ۱۳۷۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ناخن ٹوٹنے سے پہلے اس کو کاٹ دے تو اس پر دم ہے۔ (۲) اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ قال مالك لا يصلح للمحرم ان ينتنف من شعره شيئا ولا يحلقه ولا يقصره حتى يحل الا ان يصيبه اذى فى رأسه فعليه فدية كما امره الله تعالى ولا يصلح له ان يقلم اظفاره ولا يقتل قمله ( موطا امام مالک، باب فدية من حلق قبل ان بحر ،ص۴۵۰ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ناخن نہ کاٹے ۔ (۳) اور اس حدیث میں ہے کہ محرم کو پراگندہ ہونا چاہئے ۔ عن ابن عـمـر قـال قـام رجل الى النبي صلى الله عليه فقال يا رسول الله ! ما يوجب الحج ؟ قال الزاد و الراحلة قال يا رسول الله ! فما الحج ؟قال الشعث و التفل . (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب فضل دعاء الحاج ،ص ۴۱۹، نمبر ۲۸۹۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حاجی کو پراگندہ ہونا چاہئے ۔ (۴) اور ہیں انگلیوں کے ناخن کاٹے تو تداخل ہو جائے گا اسکی دلیل قول تابعی ہے۔ عن عطاء انه سئل عن المحرم يواقع ثم يعود

ثمرة النجاح جلد ٢
۴۱۸
باب الجنايات
قال عليه هدى واحد ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی هیئتة ، باب فی المحرم یواقع مرة بعد مرة ماعلیہ، ج ثالث ص ۱۸۸، نمبر ۷ ۱۳۳۷) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ کئی بار جماع کیا تو ایک ہی ھدی لازم ہوگی۔
Chapter of Violations. (1429) Or he cuts the nails of his hands and feet in one sitting, or (the nails of) one hand or one foot. ... Principle: If he has a full limb shaved, then one dam is obligatory. And if part (of a limb), then half a sa' of wheat as sadaqah is obligatory. Note: The hady must be slaughtered in the Haram, because the verse says: 'a hady reaching the Ka'bah' (5:95). Therefore, this hady must be slaughtered within the boundaries of the Haram. Translation: (1429) Or he cuts the nails of both hands and feet in one sitting, or cuts the nails of one hand or one foot. Explanation: One hand has five fingers. Both hands and both feet have twenty fingers. So if he cuts the nails of all twenty, still one dam is obligatory and there is intercession (tadakhul). And if he cuts the nails of five fingers of one hand, still one dam is obligatory. Evidence: (1) Cutting nails is contrary to being disheveled, and he attained complete benefit, so dam is obligatory. (2) In the statement of the Tabi'i: from al-Hasan and 'Ata': 'If his nail breaks, he may trim it from where it broke, and there is nothing upon him. But if he trims it before it broke, then upon him is dam.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba...). (3) In the statement of Malik: 'It is not proper for a muhrim to pluck any of his hair, nor shave it, nor cut it until he becomes halal, unless he is harmed by something on his head, then upon him is fidyah as Allah commanded. And it is not proper for him to trim his nails or kill his lice.' (Muwatta Imam Malik...). (4) And in this hadith: the muhrim should be disheveled. From Ibn 'Umar: A man stood before the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, what makes Hajj obligatory? He said: Provision and mount. He said: Then what is Hajj? He said: Disheveled and dusty. (Ibn Majah...). (5) And if he cuts the nails of (all) fingers, tadakhul applies; its evidence is the statement of 'Ata: When asked about a muhrim who has intercourse and then repeats, he said: Upon him is one hady. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba...).
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents the ruling for a muhrim who cuts his fingernails or toenails. The ruling differentiates between cutting all nails of a complete limb (hand or foot) versus cutting less than a full limb. According to the Hanafi school, if a muhrim cuts all nails of one hand (five fingers) or one foot (five toes), or even both hands and feet (twenty nails) in one sitting, only one dam (sacrifice of one sheep) is obligatory due to tadakhul (intercession of penalties). If he cuts part of a limb (e.g., some nails but not all of one hand), then half a sa' of wheat (or its value) is given as sadaqah. The evidence includes the principle that cutting nails contradicts the state of dishevelment (sha'ath) required of a muhrim, as mentioned in the hadith of Ibn 'Umar. Also, reports from Tabi'un and Imam Malik prohibit nail-cutting for the muhrim. The principle of tadakhul is supported by a report from 'Ata' that multiple acts of intercourse in ihram only necessitate one hady. The dam must be slaughtered within the Haram, as per Qur'an 5:95.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrifice of one sheep or goat, wajib as penalty for certain violations in ihram.
صدقہ (sadaqah): Here, half a sa' of wheat (or its value) given as charity for minor violations.
تداخل (tadakhul): Intercession of penalties: multiple similar violations merge into one penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muhrim cuts all ten fingernails of both hands in one sitting, what is the penalty?
A) Ten dams
B) One dam
C) Half sa' wheat
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
Cutting all nails of one hand or foot in ihram requires one dam; partial requires half sa' sadaqah; multiple violations merge by tadakhul.

Leaving a Wajib of Hajj Requires Dam
Ruling on omitting any wajib act of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a wajib act of Hajj is omitted and identify the evidence from the Sahaba and Tabi'in.

Core Idea
Omitting any wajib of Hajj or most of it requires a dam as penalty.

In Hajj, certain acts are classified as wajib (obligatory but not integral). Omitting any such act – even unintentionally – does not invalidate the Hajj but requires a compensatory sacrifice. This lesson examines the ruling and the textual evidence from the early generations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State clearly: leaving a wajib act of Hajj (or most of it) makes dam obligatory. This is a general principle covering all wajibat such as sa'i, stoning, and staying at Muzdalifah.
Dam is a sacrifice of a goat or sheep.
2
Examine the first evidence
Read the hadith from Ibn Abbas (ra) in Darqutni: 'Whoever forgets any nusuk or leaves it, let him shed blood.' Note that 'nusuk' here includes wajib acts.
This is a qawl sahabi, considered a proof in Hanafi usul.
3
Examine the second evidence
Read the athar from al-Hasan al-Basri in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah: regarding a man who leaves sa'i between Safa and Marwa, 'upon him is dam.' This directly applies the principle to a specific wajib.
Al-Hasan was a prominent Tabi'i; his opinion is cited as corroboration.
4
Apply the principle
Test the ruling on common wajib acts: omitting one stoning, omitting most of the stoning days, leaving sa'i entirely. All require a dam. If only a sunnah act is missed, no dam is required.
The distinction between wajib and sunnah is crucial; not every missed act triggers dam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۴۳۰) او ترک واجبـا مـمـا تـقـدّم بيانه
ثمرة النجاح جلد ٢
۴۱۸
باب الجنايات
(۱۴۳۰) او ترک واجبـا مـمـا تـقـدّم بيانه
تشریح : یہاں قاعدہ بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ حج میں جتنے واجبات ہیں ان میں سے کسی ایک کے چھوڑنے پر دم لازم ہوگا۔ وجه : (۱) اس قول صحابی میں ہے ۔ عن ابن عباس انه قال من نسى شيئا من نسكه أو تركه فليهرق دما (دارقطني کتاب الحج ، ج ثانی ص ۲۱۵ نمبر ۱۲ ۲۵۱۴/۲۵ ر موطا امام مالک، باب ما يفعل من نسبی من نسکه شیبا ص ۴۵۰ رستن للبیھقی ، باب من ترک شیئا من الرمی حتی يذهب ایام منی ، ج خامس، ص ۲۴۸ نمبر ۹۶۸۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ کوئی نسک چھوڑ دے تو اس پر دم ہے۔ (۲) اس قول تابعی میں بھی ہے۔ عن الحسن فی الرجل يترك الصفا والمروة قال عليه دم ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة باب في الرجل يترك الصفا والمروة ما علیہ ، ج ثالث ،ص ۲۶۹، نمبر ۱۴۲۰۰) اس اثر میں ہے کہ صفا و مروہ کی سعی چھوڑ دے تو اس پر دم ہے، اور صفا ومروہ کی سعی واجب ہے، جس سے قاعدہ یہ نکلا کہ واجب چھوڑ دے یا اس کے اکثر کو چھوڑ دے تو اس پر دم لازم ہے۔
(1430) Or he leaves a wajib from among those whose explanation has preceded. ... Explanation: Here the principle is being stated: if any one of the wajibat of Hajj is left, then dam is obligatory. Evidence: (1) In the statement of the Companion: from Ibn 'Abbas that he said: 'Whoever forgets any ritual (nusuk) or leaves it, let him shed blood (offer dam).' (Darqutni...). (2) In the statement of the Tabi'i: from al-Hasan concerning a man who leaves (the sa'i of) Safa and Marwa: 'Upon him is dam.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba...). So from this, the principle is derived: if he leaves a wajib or most of it, then dam is obligatory.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage establishes a general principle: any wajib act of Hajj (such as sa'i between Safa and Marwa, stoning the Jamarat, staying at Muzdalifah, etc.) if omitted entirely or most of it is omitted, requires a dam (sacrifice) as a penalty. The evidence is from the companion Ibn 'Abbas who said whoever forgets or leaves a ritual must offer a dam, and from al-Hasan regarding sa'i. This is a clear ruling specific to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act of Hajj that is less than rukn; its omission requires dam but does not invalidate Hajj.
نسک (nusuk): A ritual act of Hajj or Umrah; here it includes both wajib and fard.
دم (dam): A sacrifice (usually a goat or sheep) offered as compensation for omitting a wajib or committing a violation during Hajj/Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required if a pilgrim deliberately leaves the sa'i between Safa and Marwa (which is wajib in Hanafi school)?
A) Nothing
B) Sajdah sahw
C) Dam
D) Repeat sa'i

Key Takeaway
Omitting any wajib act of Hajj or most of it necessitates a dam, based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas and the athar of al-Hasan.

Trimming the Mustache in Ihram: The Hukuma Penalty
Ruling on trimming mustache in ihram using hukuma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the hukuma process for trimming the mustache during ihram and calculate the penalty based on the appraisal.

Core Idea
If a muhrim trims his mustache, the penalty is determined by appraising the hair cut relative to a quarter of the beard's value.

Trimming hair during ihram usually incurs a penalty. For the mustache, the Hanafi school applies a unique method: hukuma, or appraisal by two experts. This lesson will walk through how the penalty is calculated based on the amount trimmed compared to the value of a quarter of the beard.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
The act is trimming the mustache (shaarib) while in the state of ihram. This is a prohibited act (mahzur) that requires compensation.
Trimming any hair during ihram is generally prohibited.
2
Understand the need for hukuma
Unlike the beard or head, the mustache has no fixed penalty (muqaddar). Therefore, the Hanafi school uses hukuma (appraisal by two just experts) to determine the penalty proportionally.
Hukuma applies to body parts without specified diya or fixed penalty.
3
Determine the benchmark: quarter of the beard
The experts compare the value of the trimmed mustache hair to the value of a quarter of the beard. Shaving a quarter of the beard requires a full dam (one goat), so this is the baseline.
The beard's quarter is used as a standard measure.
4
Apply proportionality
If the trimmed mustache hair equals the value of a quarter of the beard, a full dam is due. If it is less, the penalty is a fraction of a dam proportional to that fraction of a quarter beard.
Example: if it equals a quarter of a quarter beard, then a quarter of a dam is due.
5
Recognize the role of two just experts
Two experienced and just (adil) men perform the appraisal. Their assessment determines the exact penalty.
The experts must be trustworthy and knowledgeable in estimating values.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۴۳۱) وفى اخذ شاربه حكومة.
ثمرة النجاح جلد ٢
۴۱۸
باب الجنايات
(۱۴۳۱) وفى اخذ شاربه حكومة.
تشریح : مونچھ کا بال کتروایا تو دو تجربہ کار اور عادل آدمی یہ دیکھیں کہ چوتھائی ڈاڑھی کے حساب سے کتنا ہے،اگر مونچھ کا بال اتنا کاٹا ہے کہ چوتھائی ڈاڑھی کے برابر ہے تو ایک دم یعنی ایک بکری لازم ہوگی ، اور اگر چوتھائی ڈاڑھی کی چوتھائی ہے تو ایک بکری کی قیمت کی چوتھائی لازم ہوگی ، یا اس کا کھا نالازم ہوگا۔
(1431) And regarding taking (trimming) his mustache, there is hukuma (appraisal). Explanation: If he trims the hair of the mustache, then two experienced and just men should look at how much it is in proportion to a quarter of the beard. If the trimmed mustache hair equals a quarter of the beard, then one dam (one goat) is obligatory. And if it equals a quarter of a quarter of the beard, then one quarter of the price of a goat is obligatory, or its food.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage teaches that trimming the mustache (shaarib) during ihram requires a penalty determined by hukuma (appraisal by two experts). They compare the amount of hair removed from the mustache to the value of a quarter of the beard (since shaving the beard requires a full dam). If equal to a quarter of the beard, full dam; if less, proportionate value. This is a unique ruling for the mustache, as it is not a full limb like the beard.

Key Terms
حکومہ (hukuma): Appraisal by two just experts to determine the monetary equivalent of the violated part of the body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One dam
B) Quarter dam
C) Half sa' wheat
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
Trimming the mustache during ihram requires hukuma to determine the penalty proportionally to a quarter of the beard's value.

Minor Violations in Ihram: Half Sa' Sadaqah
Listing three minor violations with their penalty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three actions that require half a sa' of wheat as sadaqah and identify the threshold that distinguishes them from violations requiring a dam.

Core Idea
Half sa' for less: perfume less than a limb, stitched garment and head cover less than a day.

In the chapter of Hajj penalties (jinayat), the rulings are scaled according to the extent of the violation. This passage specifies three minor acts that incur only a half sa' of wheat or its value, rather than the full dam. Understanding these thresholds helps you distinguish between major and minor infractions in ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three acts
Read the Arabic list: applying perfume (طيب) to less than a limb, wearing a stitched garment (لبس مخيط), and covering the head (غطى رأسه). Each is followed by the condition 'less than' (اقل من) a limb or a day.
These are the only three acts listed for half sa' in this passage.
2
Note the threshold condition
The penalty is half sa' if the act is less than a full limb (for perfume) or less than a full day (for stitched garment and head cover). If it reaches or exceeds the full limb or full day, the penalty becomes a dam.
The passage explicitly says 'less than' (اقل من).
3
Contrast with major violations
For the same acts done fully (perfume on a full limb, wearing makhit for a day or more, covering head for a day or more), the penalty is a dam (sacrifice of a sheep). The half sa' is a reduced penalty for incomplete violations.
This scaling reflects the principle of proportionality in jinayat.
4
Locate the evidence
The passage references the hadith of Ka'b bin 'Ujrah, which established the general ruling for fidyah due to harm (like shaving head). This is the proof for the principle of lesser penalties for lesser violations.
The hadith is not quoted fully but is the known basis for fidyah scaling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۴۳۲) والتي توجب الصدقة بنصف صاع من بر او قيمته هي ما لو طيب اقل من عضو او لبس مخيطا او غطّى رأسه اقل من يوم.
ثمرة النجاح جلد ٢
۴۱۸
باب الجنايات
(۱۴۳۲) والتي توجب الصدقة بنصف صاع من بر او قيمته هي ما لو طيب اقل من عضو او لبس مخيطا او غطّى رأسه اقل من يوم.
تشریح : یہاں سے یہ بتارہے ہیں کہ کن کن جنایات میں آدھا صاع گیہوں واجب ہوتا ہے ( اس کو صدقہ کہتے ہیں ) ان میں سے پہلا یہ ہے کہ ایک پورے عضو پر دم لازم ہوتا ہے، اس لیے اس سے کم پر آدھا صاع گیہوں لازم ہوگا۔ دوسرا یہ ہے کہ ایک دن سلا ہوا کپڑا پہننے سے دم لازم ہوگا ، اور اس سے کم پہننے پر آدھا صاع گیہوں لازم ہوگا۔ اور تیسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک دن سے کم سر ڈھانکے تو آدھا صاع گیہوں لازم ہوگا۔
وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے۔ ان كعب بن عجرة حدثه قال وقف على رسول الله بالحديبية ورأسى يتهافت قملا فقال یونيك هو امک؟قلت نعم قال فاحلق رأسک، او احلق ،قال: في نزلت هذه الآية فمن كان
(1432) And those (violations) that obligate sadaqah of half a sa' of wheat or its value are: if he applies perfume to less than a limb, or wears a stitched garment (makhit) or covers his head for less than a day. Explanation: From here, he tells which violations require half a sa' of wheat (this is called sadaqah). The first: a full limb requires dam, so less than that requires half sa'. The second: wearing stitched clothes for a full day requires dam, less than a day requires half sa'. The third: covering head for less than a day requires half sa'. Evidence: (1) In the hadith: that Ka'b bin 'Ujrah said: 'The Messenger of Allah stopped at Hudaybiyyah while my head was crawling with lice. He said: Do you have an animal (sacrifice)? I said yes. He said: Shave your head. Then this verse was revealed: So whoever among you is ill...'
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage lists three minor violations that require half a sa' of wheat (about 1.5 kg) or its value as sadaqah, not a full dam. These are: applying perfume to less than a full limb, wearing a stitched garment for less than a full day, and covering the head for less than a full day. The principle is that if the violation is of a smaller magnitude than the threshold that triggers a dam, a lesser penalty applies. The hadith of Ka'b bin 'Ujrah is referenced as the basis for the general principle of fidyah for shaving the head due to harm.

Key Terms
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume; half a sa' of wheat is approximately 1.5 kg.
مخيط (makhit): Stitched garment; wearing it is prohibited for men in ihram.
عضو (udw): Limb; in Hanafi fiqh, a limb is a distinct body part like hand, forearm, upper arm, thigh, lower leg, foot, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What penalty is due if a muhrim covers his head for 12 hours?
A) Dam
B) Half sa' of wheat
C) Nothing
D) One sa' of wheat

Key Takeaway
Half sa' of wheat sadaqah is due for applying perfume to less than a limb, wearing a stitched garment for less than a day, or covering the head for less than a day.

The General Rule: Omitting a Wajib in Hajj Requires Dam
States the general rule that leaving a wajib requires blood (dam)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that omitting any wajib in Hajj requires dam and identify the proof from the Companions and Tabi'un.

Core Idea
Leaving a wajib in Hajj always demands dam — a clear rule anchored in the practice of the early generations.

In Hajj, not all acts carry the same weight. The Hanafi school distinguishes between fard (pillars) and wajib (obligatory acts). This lesson examines the general rule that omitting any wajib act triggers a compulsory sacrifice (dam). The source passage presents two key proofs from Ibn Abbas and Hasan al-Basri, establishing this principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its category
The passage states that leaving a previously explained wajib requires dam. Determine the hukm level: wajib compensation.
This rule applies to all wajibat of Hajj, not just one specific act.
2
Locate the first dalil: the athar of Ibn Abbas
Ibn Abbas said: 'Whoever forgets something from his rites or leaves it, let him shed blood.' The command indicates obligation.
The wording 'فليهرق دما' is imperative, implying wujub in Hanafi usul.
3
Locate the second dalil: the athar of Hasan al-Basri about Sa'y
Hasan al-Basri said: 'For a man who leaves Sa'y between Safa and Marwah, upon him is blood.' This shows Sa'y is wajib.
This specific example establishes the principle for all wajibat.
4
Understand the general principle
From these specific examples, the rule is extended to all wajibat of Hajj. The principle is: leaving any wajib or the majority of it requires dam.
This is a case of generalizing from two instances, supported by the consensus of the Hanafi school.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab dimension
Some schools hold that only arkan invalidate and wajibat may require sadaqah instead of dam. Hanafis maintain dam due to the generality of the evidence.
This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text

أو ترك واجبا مما تقدم بيانه
ترجمه : (١٤٣٠) یا جس واجب کا بیان پہلے ہوا ان میں سے کسی ایک واجب کو ترک کر دے۔
تشریح : یہاں قاعدہ بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ حج میں جتنے واجبات ہیں ان میں سے کسی ایک کے چھوڑنے پر دم لازم ہوگا۔ وجه : (١) اس قول صحابی میں ہے ۔ عن ابن عباس انه قال من نسى شيئا من نسكه أو تركه فليهرق دما (دارقطني کتاب الحج ، ج ثانی ص ٢١٥ نمبر ١٢ ٢٥١٤/٢٥ ر موطا امام مالک، باب ما يفعل من نسبی من نسکه شیبا ص ٤٥٠ رستن للبیھقی ، باب من ترک شیئا من الرمی حتی يذهب ایام منی ، ج خامس، ص ٢٤٨ نمبر ٩٦٨٨) اس اثر میں ہے کہ کوئی نسک چھوڑ دے تو اس پر دم ہے۔ (٢) اس قول تابعی میں بھی ہے۔ عن الحسن فی الرجل يترك الصفا والمروة قال عليه دم ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة باب في الرجل يترك الصفا والمروة ما علیہ ، ج ثالث ،ص ٢٦٩، نمبر ١٤٢٠٠) اس اثر میں ہے کہ صفا و مروہ کی سعی چھوڑ دے تو اس پر دم ہے، اور صفا ومروہ کی سعی واجب ہے، جس سے قاعدہ یہ نکلا کہ واجب چھوڑ دے یا اس کے اکثر کو چھوڑ دے تو اس پر دم لازم ہے۔
Or he leaves an obligatory act from what was previously explained. Translation: (1430) Or leaves one of the obligatory acts whose explanation preceded. Commentary: Here they are explaining the rule that in Hajj, leaving any of the obligatory acts necessitates blood (dam). Evidence: (1) In this statement of a Companion: from Ibn Abbas that he said: Whoever forgets something from his rites or leaves it, let him shed blood. (2) In this statement of a Tabi'i: from al-Hasan regarding a man who leaves Sa'y between Safa and Marwah: he said upon him is blood. So the rule derived is that if one leaves a wajib or its majority, blood is obligatory.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof establishing that omitting any wajib in Hajj requires a dam sacrifice. The author first states the rule in Arabic: 'or leaves a wajib from those previously mentioned.' The Urdu commentary explains that this is a general principle: any wajib left in Hajj necessitates dam. Two proofs are cited: (1) an athar from Ibn Abbas saying whoever forgets or leaves a rite must spill blood, and (2) an athar from Hasan al-Basri saying leaving Sa'y between Safa and Marwah requires blood, establishing that Sa'y is wajib and its omission triggers dam. The Hanafi school relies on these to uphold that wajib acts in Hajj have a penalty of dam, not just sadaqah.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as expiation for certain violations in Hajj.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act in Hajj that if omitted requires dam, but does not invalidate Hajj.
نسك (nusk): Ritual acts of Hajj or Umrah; the term includes both arkan and wajibat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi evidence cited, what is required if a pilgrim leaves Sa'y between Safa and Marwah?
A) Nothing, it is sunnah
B) Dam (a sheep)
C) Repeat Hajj
D) Give charity (sadaqah)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, omitting any wajib act in Hajj necessitates a dam sacrifice, a rule established by the practice of the Companions and the Tabi'un.

Penalty for Cutting the Mustache in Ihram: Hukuma Estimation
Penalty for mustache cutting in Ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of hukuma to determine the penalty for a muhrim cutting his mustache, and distinguish between the obligations of dam and sadaqah based on the proportion of hair removed.

Core Idea
Cutting the mustache in Ihram incurs a penalty measured by expert estimation relative to one-fourth of the beard.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hajj chapter: what happens if a muhrim (person in Ihram) cuts his mustache? The Hanafi school applies a unique estimation process called hukuma, where two just experts assess the amount of hair removed in proportion to one-fourth of the beard. The penalty ranges from a full dam (sacrifice of a goat) to a fractional sadaqah. Understanding this process clarifies how Hanafi fiqh handles variable violations with flexible, expert-determined penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is cutting the mustache while in Ihram. The ruling is that it triggers a penalty (wajib) but the exact amount depends on the quantity cut.
2
Understand hukuma
Hukuma is an estimation by two experienced, just Muslims. They compare the cut mustache hair to the standard of one-fourth of the beard. This is the Hanafi method for penalties when the exact amount is not fixed by nass.
Hukuma is used for body parts like mustache that are not explicitly mentioned in primary texts.
3
Apply the proportion rule
If the cut hair equals one-fourth of the beard, one full dam (goat) is wajib. If it equals one-fourth of that (i.e., one-sixteenth of the beard), then one-fourth of the value of a dam is due as sadaqah.
The beard standard is analogically derived from the rule for shaving the head.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that hukuma is applied as described, affirming the use of expert estimation for undefined hair parts.
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may treat mustache similarly to head hair, but Hanafis maintain the specific estimation method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي اخذ شاربه حكومة.
ترجمه : (١٤٣١) اور مونچھ کاٹنے میں جو فیصلہ کر دے۔
تشریح : مونچھ کا بال کتروایا تو دو تجربہ کار اور عادل آدمی یہ دیکھیں کہ چوتھائی ڈاڑھی کے حساب سے کتنا ہے،اگر مونچھ کا بال اتنا کاٹا ہے کہ چوتھائی ڈاڑھی کے برابر ہے تو ایک دم یعنی ایک بکری لازم ہوگی ، اور اگر چوتھائی ڈاڑھی کی چوتھائی ہے تو ایک بکری کی قیمت کی چوتھائی لازم ہوگی ، یا اس کا کھا نالازم ہوگا۔
And regarding taking his mustache, hukuma. Translation: (1431) And a ruling regarding cutting the mustache. Commentary: If he trims the hair of his mustache, then two experienced and just men should estimate how much it is relative to one-fourth of the beard. If he cut an amount equal to one-fourth of the beard, then one dam (a goat) is obligatory. If it is one-fourth of one-fourth of the beard, then one-fourth of the price of a goat is obligatory, or its food is obligatory.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the penalty for a muhrim (one in Ihram) who cuts his mustache. The Arabic says 'and regarding taking his mustache, hukuma' meaning an estimation-based penalty. The commentary explains that two expert and just assessors evaluate how much hair was removed relative to one-fourth of the beard. If the amount equals one-fourth of the beard, a full dam (goat) is due. If it is less (one-fourth of one-fourth), then one-fourth of the value of a dam is due as sadaqah. This follows the Hanafi principle that penalties for hair removal are measured against the standard of one-fourth of the head (or beard).

Key Terms
حكومة (hukuma): An estimation made by two just experts to determine the penalty for removing hair during Ihram.
دم (dam): A sacrifice of a goat or sheep, a type of penalty in Hajj/Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Mustache cutting in Ihram triggers a wajib penalty determined by hukuma—expert estimation proportional to one-fourth of the beard.
